Doubting Zakat Payment: Must Repeat Until Certain
Ruling on doubt in zakat with comparison to prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on doubt in zakat payment, distinguishing between doubt about the act and doubt about the amount, and justify the repetition ruling using the analogy to prayer within its time.

Core Idea
If you doubt whether you paid zakat, you must pay again — because your entire life is the time for zakat, unlike prayer.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the obligation to repeat zakat when in doubt about its payment. It contrasts zakat with prayer: after the prayer time ends, doubt is ignored, but since the entire lifespan is the time for zakat, any doubt is like doubt during prayer time, which requires repetition. The passage also addresses doubt about the amount paid, introducing the principle of taharrī (estimation) when one has a dominant guess.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Determine what the doubt is about: either the act of paying zakat (did I pay or not?) or the amount paid (did I pay the full amount?).
The ruling differs based on this distinction.
2
State the basic Hanafi ruling
For doubt about the act itself, the ruling is wajib to repeat. This is based on the principle that certainty of obligation is not removed by doubt.
The source explicitly says 'he must repeat'.
3
Identify the dalil
The proof is a qiyas (analogy) to prayer: if one doubts during the prayer time, he must repeat. Since life is the time for zakat, any doubt is analogous to doubt during prayer time.
No Quran/hadith is cited; it's a legal reasoning from time extension.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illa) is the ongoing time window. For zakat, there is no fixed expiry, so the obligation remains continuously valid, making doubt at any moment equivalent to doubt within an active time slot.
This distinguishes zakat from prayer after time.
5
Note the refinement by al-Ramli
Al-Ramli distinguishes between doubt about the act (must repeat) and doubt about the amount (first make taharrī; if no dominant estimate, then repeat).
This shows how later Hanafi scholars add nuance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الواقعات: ولو شك رجل في الزكاة فلم يدر أزكى أم لا فإنه يعيد . فرق بين هذا وبين ما إذا شك في الصلاة بعد ذهاب الوقت أصلاها أم لا، والفرق أن العمر كله وقت لأداء الزكاة فصار هذا بمنزلة شك وقع في أداء الصلاة أنه أدى أم لا وهو في وقتها ولو كان كذلك يعيد .اهـ. ووقعت حادثة أن شك هل أدى جميع ما عليه من الزكاة أم لا بأن كان يؤدي متفرقاً ولا يضبطه هل يلزمه إعادتها ومقتضى ما ذكرنا لزوم الإعادة قوله: (ومقتضى ما ذكر لزوم الإعادة) قال الرملي : فرق هذا بين وبين تقدم ، فما تقدم شك في الأداء وعدمه، وههنا في مقدار المؤدى فينبغي التحري كما هو الأصل في مثله أي حيث غلب على ظنه قدر معين أما إذا لم يغلب كما هو فرض كلام المؤلف فما معنى التحري تأمل.
And in al-Waqi'at: If a man doubts in zakat and does not know whether he gave it or not, then he must repeat. Distinguish this from if he doubted in prayer after the time passed whether he prayed it or not. The difference is that the entire lifespan is a time for performing zakat, so this is like a doubt that occurs in performing prayer—whether he performed it or not while he is in its time—and if that were the case he would repeat. End quote. And an incident occurred where he doubted whether he paid all the zakat due on him or not, because he was paying it in parts and did not keep track: is it necessary for him to repeat it? And what we mentioned dictates the necessity of repeating. He said: (And what we mentioned dictates the necessity of repeating). Al-Ramli said: There is a difference between this and the previous case. The previous case is doubt about performing and not performing, while here it is about the amount paid. In this case, he should make an estimation (taharrī) as is the principle in similar cases, i.e., if a specific amount becomes dominant in his mind. But if no amount becomes dominant, as is the assumption of the author's statement, then what is the meaning of estimation? Reflect.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on doubt in zakat payment. The text first states the basic rule: if a person is unsure whether he paid zakat, he must pay it again. This is based on the principle that zakat is due continuously throughout one's life; there is no fixed time window like prayer, after which doubt is ignored. The text then contrasts this with prayer: if one doubts after the prayer time has ended, he does not repeat. But for zakat, since the entire life is the time, doubt at any moment is like doubt during prayer time, which requires repetition. The passage then presents a secondary case: doubt about the amount paid when paying in installments. The author initially deduces that repetition is necessary. However, al-Ramli refines this: the earlier case is doubt about the act itself (did I pay or not?), while here it is doubt about the amount. In the latter, one should make an effort to recall (taharrī) and act on his dominant guess. If no amount is dominant, then the ruling reverts to the original principle—must repeat. The commentary ends with a note that the author's statement needs further thought.

Key Terms
شك (shakk): Doubt about whether an obligatory act (zakat) has been performed.
التحري (al-taharrī): Effort to recall and form a dominant opinion about the amount paid or other uncertain matter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person doubts whether he paid zakat but has no clear memory, what must he do?
A) Nothing, because the time for zakat has passed and doubt is ignored.
B) He must repeat the zakat payment.
C) He should estimate and act on his dominant opinion.
D) He should wait until he is certain and then pay.

Key Takeaway
For zakat, any doubt about payment requires repetition because the entire life is the time for zakat, but doubt about the amount must first be resolved by estimation if possible.

Definition of Sā'imah and Its Conditions for Zakat
Definition and conditions for sā'imah in zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the juristic definition of sā'imah and identify the conditions under which zakat becomes obligatory on grazing livestock.

Core Idea
Sā'imah: livestock that graze most of the year, kept for breeding, milk, or fattening.

In this passage from Bahr al-Rā’iq, the author defines sā'imah—the key category for livestock zakat. Understanding this definition is crucial, because not all grazing animals are subject to zakat. The passage also addresses an objection about the scope, clarifying that animals used for riding or carrying are excluded. By parsing the definition carefully, you will learn exactly which livestock obligate zakat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its two meanings
Recognize that sā'imah has a linguistic meaning (livestock that graze freely) and a juristic meaning. The passage gives the juristic definition: livestock that suffice by grazing for most of the year.
The linguistic definition is broader; the juristic one adds the condition of 'most of the year'.
2
Analyze the condition 'most of the year'
Understand that 'most' (aktar al-sannah) means more than half. If the owner feeds the animals for half the year or more, they are not sā'imah and no zakat is due due to doubt about the cause (sabab).
This condition prevents easy avoidance by feeding animals for exactly half the year.
3
Examine the hidden condition of purpose
The definition might seem to include all grazing animals, but the author notes that later clarification restricts it to animals kept for breeding, milk, or fattening. Animals for riding or carrying are excluded.
This resolves the objection that the definition is too general.
4
Distinguish from other categories
Note the distinction: animals for trade are subject to zakat al-tijārah, while animals for personal use (riding/carrying) have no zakat. The passage also explains that if trade animals are later made sā'imah, a new haul begins.
This shows the careful categorization in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صدقة السوائم أي زكاتها قالوا حيث أطلقت الصدقة في الكتاب العزيز فالمراد بها الزكاة. وبدأ أكثرهم ببيان السوائم اقتداء بكتب رسول الله فإنها كانت مفتتحة بها ولكونها أعز أموال العرب والسوائم جمع سائمة ولها معنيان: لغوي وفقهي قال في المغرب؛ سامت الماشية رعت سوماً وأسامها صاحبها أسامة والسائمة عن الأصمعي كل إبل ترسل ترعى ولا تعلف في الأهل اهـ. وفي ضياء الحلوم : السائمة المال الراعي قوله (هي التي تكتفي بالرعي في أكثر السنة) بيان للسائمة بالمعنى الفقهي لأن اسم السائمة لا يزول بالعلف اليسير ولأنه لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه . قيد بالأكثر لإفادة أنه لو علفها نصف الحول فإنها لا تكون سائمة فلا زكاة فيها لوقوع الشك في السبب لأن المال إنما صار سبباً بوصف الأسامة فلا يجب الحكم مع اعترض في النهاية بأن مرادهم تفسير السائمة التي فيها الحكم المذكور فهي تعريف بالأعم إذ بقي قيد كون ذلك لغرض النسل والدر والتسمين وإلا فيشمل الأسامة لغرض الحمل والركوب وليس فيها زكاة وأقره عليه في فتح القدير. وقد يجاب بأنهم إنما تركوا القيد لتصريحهم بعد ذلك بأن ما كان للحمل والركوب فإنه لا شيء فيه، وصرحوا أيضاً بأن العروض إذا كانت للتجارة يجب فيها زكاة التجارة وقالوا : إن العرض خلاف النقد فيدخل فيه الحيوانات. وحاصله أنه إن أسامها للحمل أو للركوب فلا زكاة أصلاً، أو للتجارة ففيها زكاة التجارة، أو للدر والنسل ففيها الزكاة المذكورة في هذا الباب. وفي المحيط : ولو اشتراها للتجارة ثم جعلها سائمة يعتبر الحول من وقت الجعل لأن حول زكاة التجارة يبطل بجعلها للسوم لأن زكاة السوائم وزكاة التجارة مختلفان قدراً وسبباً فلا يبني حول أحدهما على الآخر اهـ. فإن قلت : قد اقتصر الزيلعي وغيره على أن المراد بها التي تسام للدر والنسل فيفيد أنها لو كانت كلها ذكوراً لا تجب الزكاة فيها والمصرح به في البدائع والمحيط أنه لا فرق بين قوله : (وقد يجاب بأنهم الخ) قال في النهر : هذا غير دافع إذ التعريف بالأعم لا يصح ولا ويمكن أن يقال : المراد أن القيد المذكور ملاحظ في التعريف ينفع فيه ذكر الحكمين بعده ا هـ . واكتفوا عن التصريح به هنا لعلمه مما يأتي فلا يكون تعريفاً بالأعم تأمل. على أن عدم التعريف
Chapter on the Zakat of Sā'imah: meaning its zakat. They said: wherever sadaqah is used absolutely in the noble Book, the intent is zakat. Most of them began by explaining sā'imah, following the letters of the Messenger of Allah, for they used to open with it, and because it was the most honoured wealth of the Arabs. Sā'imah is the plural of sā'imah, and it has two meanings: linguistic and juristic. He said in al-Maghrib: al-māshiyah (livestock) grazed, and its owner sent it to graze. Al-Sā'imah according to al-Asma'i: every camel that is sent to graze and is not fed at home. And in Diyā' al-Ḥulūm: al-sā'imah is the grazing wealth. His statement (she is the one that suffices with grazing most of the year) is an explanation of sā'imah in the juristic sense, because the name sā'imah is not removed by a little feeding, and because it is not possible to avoid it. He restricted it with 'most' to indicate that if he feeds it for half the year, it is not sā'imah, so there is no zakat on it due to doubt about the cause. For wealth becomes a cause only by the attribute of being sā'imah, so the ruling is not obligated. There was an objection in al-Nihāyah that their intent is to interpret sā'imah that has the mentioned ruling; thus it is a definition by the more general, since the condition that it be for the purpose of breeding, milk, and fattening remains. Otherwise, sā'imah for the purpose of carrying loads and riding would be included, and there is no zakat on that. This was affirmed in Fatḥ al-Qadīr. And it may be answered that they only omitted the condition because they later clarified that what is for carrying and riding has nothing due on it. They also clarified that trade goods, if for trade, require zakat of trade, and they said: goods are the opposite of cash, and animals are included. The gist is that if he makes them sā'imah for carrying or riding, there is no zakat at all; if for trade, then there is zakat of trade; if for milk and breeding, then there is the zakat mentioned in this chapter. And in al-Muḥīṭ: If he buys them for trade then makes them sā'imah, the year is counted from the time of making, because the year for zakat of trade is invalidated by making them sā'imah, because the zakat of sā'imah and the zakat of trade differ in amount and cause, so the year of one cannot be built on the other. If you say: al-Zayla‘ī and others restricted it to that which is made sā'imah for milk and breeding; this would imply that if all were males, zakat would not be obligatory, whereas it is stated in al-Badā’i‘ and al-Muḥīṭ that there is no difference... His statement (And it may be answered that they...) He said in al-Nahr: This is not a rebuttal, because definition by the more general is not valid. And it can be said that the intent is that the mentioned condition is observed in the definition; it is beneficial by mentioning the two rulings after it... They were satisfied without explicit mention here because it will be known from what follows; thus it is not a definition by the more general. Reflect. Even on the non-definition...
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage is a definition-ruling at the start of the chapter on zakat of grazing livestock (ṣadaqat al-sawā'im). It begins by explaining that 'ṣadaqah' in the Quran refers to zakat. The authors begin with sā'imah following the practice of the Prophet's letters and because it was the noblest wealth of Arabs. Sā'imah is defined both linguistically (animals that graze freely) and juristically. The juristic definition is given: livestock that suffice by grazing for most of the year. The qualification 'most' means that if fed for half the year, they are not sā'imah, and no zakat is due due to doubt about the cause. A discussion follows about whether the definition is too general: it might include animals used for riding or carrying, on which there is no zakat. The author resolves this by noting that the condition of being for breeding, milk, or fattening is understood from later context. Also, animals for trade are subject to trade zakat. The passage then discusses the case of buying animals for trade and then making them sā'imah: the year for zakat of sā'imah starts anew because the two types differ. Finally, a debate is noted: al-Zayla‘ī restricts sā'imah to those for milk and breeding, which would exempt all-male herds, but the majority (al-Badā’i‘, al-Muḥīṭ) hold that there is no difference between males and females for zakat on sā'imah. The commentary ends with a note that the definition is not truly general because the specific rulings clarify it.

Key Terms
سائمة (sā'imah): Livestock that graze freely in pastures for most of the year, not fed at home, and kept for breeding, milk, or fattening.
بنت مخاض (bint makhāḍ): A female camel that has entered its second year and whose mother is pregnant with another (thus she is the daughter of a pregnant camel).
العلف (al-'ulf): Feeding livestock at home, as opposed to grazing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Livestock that suffice by grazing for most of the year.
C) Livestock kept only for trade.
D) Livestock used for riding and carrying.

Key Takeaway
The juristic definition of sā'imah requires grazing for most of the year and a productive purpose (breeding, milk, fattening); animals used for riding or carrying are not subject to zakat al-sā'imah.

Zakat Schedule for Camels (25-120)
Lists zakat due on camels at specific herd sizes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recall the zakat obligations for camel holdings between 25 and 120 and correctly identify the age category of the animal due at each threshold.

Core Idea
As the camel herd grows, the age of the due zakat animal also increases.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the prophetic schedule for zakat on camels. It specifies which type of camel is due at key thresholds from 25 to 120. Understanding these thresholds is essential for accurate zakat calculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisab
Recognize that the minimum threshold (nisab) for camels is 25. For 5 to 24 camels, a sheep is due per 5 camels.
This is separate from the camel schedule; focus on 25+ for this lesson.
2
Memorize the seven key numbers
The thresholds are 25, 36, 46, 61, 76, 91, and 120. These are the points at which the zakat animal changes.
Beyond 120, the same pattern repeats every 40 or 50 camels in higher schedules.
3
Associate each threshold with the correct animal
At 25: bint makhad (2nd year). At 36: bint labun (3rd year). At 46: hiqqa (4th year). At 61: jadha'a (5th year). At 76: two bint labun. At 91: two hiqqas. At 120: the same as 91? Actually the passage ends at 120 with 'two hiqqas'.
The schedule up to 120 is: 25 (1 bint makhad), 36 (1 bint labun), 46 (1 hiqqa), 61 (1 jadha'a), 76 (2 bint labun), 91 (2 hiqqas), 120 (2 hiqqas, same as 91-120).
4
Understand the sequence logic
As the herd increases, the zakat animal becomes older. This encourages growth: a larger herd means older animal due, which is more valuable.
Between thresholds (e.g., 50 camels), the zakat is the same as the previous threshold. Here, 50 falls between 46 and 61, so a hiqqa is due.
5
Apply linguistic knowledge
Know the age definitions: bint makhad (mother pregnant again), bint labun (mother has milk), hiqqa (fit for mounting), jadha'a (permanent teeth not fully in).
These terms help verify the schedule and avoid confusion with other livestock zakat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب في خمس وعشرين إبلاً بنت مخاض وفيما دونه في كل خمس شاة وفي ست وثلاثين بنت لبون وفي ست وأربعين حقة وفي إحدى وستين جذعة وفي ست وسبعين بنتا لبون وفي إحدى وتسعين حقتان إلى مائة وعشرين بهذا اشتهرت كتب الصدقات من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. والإبل ليس لها واحد من لفظها والنسبة إليها إبلي بفتح الباء كقولهم في النسبة إلى سلمة سلمي بالفتح لتوالي الكسرات مع الياء والمخاض النوق الحوامل، وابن المخاض هو الفصيل الذي حملت أمه قبل ابن اللبون بسنة، وكذلك بنت المخاض. والمخاض أيضاً وجع الولادة قال تعالى
And it is obligatory on twenty-five camels a bint makhad; and on what is less than that, for every five a sheep; and on thirty-six a bint labun; and on forty-six a hiqqa; and on sixty-one a jadha'a; and on seventy-six two bint labun; and on ninety-one two hiqqas up to one hundred and twenty. This is what is well-known in the books of charity from the Messenger of Allah peace be upon him. The word 'ibil' (camels) has no singular from its own root; the nisba to it is 'ibili' with fatha on the ba, like the nisba to 'salam' is 'salami' with fatha due to successive kasras together with the ya. Al-makhad are the pregnant she-camels; ibn makhad is the foal whose mother conceived before the ibn labun by a year, similarly bint makhad. Makhad also means the pain of childbirth; Allah said...
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage states the zakat thresholds for camels as established in the traditions from the Prophet. The text is a direct quote from the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) and is commented upon with linguistic explanations. The ruling: for 25 camels, due is a bint makhad (a she-camel in its second year, whose mother has conceived again). For fewer than 25 camels, if one owns 5 to 24 camels, the zakat is a sheep (or goat) per 5 camels (this is the Hanafi position, though some details differ for exact numbers). Then for 36 camels, a bint labun (a she-camel in its third year); for 46, a hiqqa (fourth year); for 61, a jadha'a (fifth year); for 76, two bint labun; for 91, two hiqqas; and so on up to 120. This is the well-known schedule from the Prophet. The author then clarifies linguistic points: the term 'ibil' is a plural with no singular from the same root; its nisba is 'ibili' with fatha. 'Makhad' refers to pregnant camels; 'ibn makhad' is a foal whose mother conceived before the previous foal (i.e., the mother is pregnant again, so the foal is young). 'Bint makhad' is the female equivalent. 'Makhad' also means birth pangs, as in the Quran. The passage is a memorization anchor for the zakat schedule.

Key Terms
بنت مخاض (bint makhad): A she-camel in its second year, so called because its mother is pregnant (makhad) again.
بنت لبون (bint labun): A she-camel in its third year (bint labun means its mother has milk, i.e., she has given birth to another foal).
حقة (hiqqa): A she-camel in its fourth year, when it is eligible to be mounted (hiqqa from haqqa: to be deserved for mounting).
جذعة (jadha'a): A she-camel in its fifth year, before its permanent teeth fully appear.
إبل (ibil): Plural for camels; has no singular from the same root.
شاة (shāh): A sheep or goat (one head).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what zakat is due on 76 camels?
A) A bint makhad
B) A bint labun
C) Two bint labun
D) Two hiqqas

Key Takeaway
Zakat on camels follows a specific schedule rooted in prophetic tradition; memorizing the thresholds ensures accurate compliance.

Condition of Sa'imah for Zakat on Camels
Commentary on the condition of sa'imah from Al-Bahr al-Raiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of sa'imah for zakat on camels and identify which uses of camels exempt them from zakat according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Zakat on camels applies only if they are sa'imah (freely grazing) and not used for riding, work, or trade.

The condition of sa'imah is a key element in Hanafi zakat law. While all camels may appear similar, the Shari'ah distinguishes between those that graze freely on public land and those that are fed at home or used for services. This lesson unpacks the exact definition of sa'imah and the legal implications of different intentions and uses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The ruling is that zakat on camels is fard 'ayn when conditions are met. The passage discusses the condition of sa'imah.
2
Locate the condition
The text mentions the condition that camels must be sa'imah. Find how the commentator defines it: camels that graze freely and are not used for riding, work, or trade.
3
Analyse the condition's purpose
The commentator clarifies that the condition negates use for riding, labour, or trade, not necessarily requiring intent for milk/offspring.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi variations
Al-Bada'i' holds that camels grazed for meat are exempt, and al-Qunyah exempts working camels fattened the rest of the year.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that sa'imah excludes work and trade, with intent for milk/offspring as the norm but not a strict condition.

كتاب الزكاة باب صدقة السوائم وفيما دونه في كل خمس شاة وفي ست وثلاثين بنت لبون وفي ست وأربعين حقة وفي إحدى وستين جذعة وفي ست وسبعين بنتا لبون وفي إحدى وتسعين حقتان إلى مائة وعشرين هذا كونها كلها إناثاً أو كونها كلها ذكوراً أو بعضها ذكوراً وبعضها إناثاً . قلت : المقصود من الشرط نفي كون الأسامة للحمل والركوب أو للتجارة لا اشتراط أن تكون للدر والنسل، ولذا زاد في المحيط أن تسام لقصد الدر والنسل والزيادة والسمن، فالذكور فقط تسام للزيادة والسمن لكن في البدائع : لو أسامها للحم لا زكاة فيها كالحمل والركوب . وفي القنية : له إبل عوامل يعمل بها في السنة أربعة أشهر ويسمنها في الباقي ينبغي أن لا يجب فيها الزكاة اهـ . والرعي مصدر رعت الماشية الكلأ والرعي بالكسر الكلأ نفسه كذا في المغرب. والمناسب هنا الفقه لأن السائمة في التي ترعى ولا تعلف في الأهل لقصد الدر والنسل كما في فتح القدير، فلو حمل الكلأ إليها في البيت لا تكون سائمة فلو ضبط الرعي في كلامهم هنا بالكسر لكانت سائمة، ولا بد أن يكون الكلأ الذي ترعاه مباحاً كما قيده الشمني به لأن الكلا اللغة كل ما رعت الدواب من الرطب واليابس فيدخل فيه غير المباح. ضبطه بالفتح هي قوله (ويجب في خمس وعشرين إبلا بنت مخاص وفيما دونه في كل خمس شاة وفي ست وثلاثين بنت لبون وفي ست وأربعين حقة وفي إحدى وستين جذعة وفي ست وسبعين بنتا لبون وفي إحدى وتسعين حقتان إلى مائة وعشرين بهذا اشتهرت كتب الصدقات من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. والإبل ليس لها واحد من لفظها والنسبة إليها إبلي بفتح الباء كقولهم في النسبة إلى سلمة سلمي بالفتح لتوالي الكسرات مع الياء والمخاض النوق الحوامل، وابن المخاض هو الفصيل الذي حملت أمه قبل ابن اللبون بسنة، وكذلك بنت المخاض. والمخاض أيضاً وجع الولادة قال تعالى هذا بالأعم اصطلاح للمتأخرين وإلا فالمتقدمون وأهل اللغة على جوازه قوله : (قلت المقصود من الشرط الخ) يدل على هذا القصد ما في تحفة الملوك من أن السائمة الراعية أكثر الحول لا للركوب والعمل ا هـ . لكن نظر في هذا الجواب في النهر بأن نفي الأسامة للحمل والركوب قد يحصل بدون قصد الدر والنسل بأن لا يقصد شيئاً أصلاً، ولا شك أن في هذه الحالة لا زكاة عليه أيضاً ا هـ . قلت : لا يخفى عليك أن محصل جواب المؤلف أنه مجاز من قبيل إطلاق الملزوم وإرادة اللازم كما في قولك «نطقت الحال» فليس المراد خصوص المذكور بل ما أطلق هو عليه، فالمراد اللازم أعني نفي كونها للحمل أو للتجارة كما أن المراد من النطق الدلالة فقد آل كلام المؤلف إلى ما قدمناه عن التحفة، ولا يخفى عدم توجه النظر عليه فكذا ما آل إليه فتدبر نعم يرد عليه ما مر عن الخانية لو ورث سائمة كان عليه الزكاة إذا حال الحول نوى أو لم ينو تأمل قوله : (ويسمنها في الباقي) الذي رأيته في القنية : ويسيمها من الأسامة لا من التسمين قوله : (فلو) ضبط الرعي الخ) قال في النهر : الكسر هو المتداول على الألسنة ولا يلزم عليه أن تكون سائمة إلا لو أطلق الكلأ على المنفصل، ولقائل منعه بل ظاهر ما مرَّ عن المغرب أي من قوله هو كل ما رعته الدواب من الرطب واليابس وعشرين ثم في كل خمس شاة إلى مائة وخمس وأربعين ففيها حقتان وبنت مخاض وفي مائة وخمسين ثلاث حقاق ثم في كل خمس شاة وفي مائة وخمس وسبعين ثلاث حقاق فأجاءها المخاض إلى جذع النخلة ) [مريم : ٢٣] وشاة لبون ذات لبن، وابن اللبون الذي استكمل سنتين ودخل في الثالثة والحق من الإبل ما استكمل ثلاث سنين ودخل في الرابعة، والحقة الأنثى والجمع حقاق والجذع من البهائم قيل الثني إلا أنه من الإبل في السنة الخامسة والأنثى جذعة هذا في اللغة. وفي الشريعة والمراد ببنت المخاض ما تم لها سنة، وبنت اللبون ما تم لها سنتان وبالحقة ما تم لها ثلاث، وبالجذعة ما تم لها أربع. ذكر الزيلعي في فصل المحرمات من النكاح أن قيد كونها بنت مخاض أو بنت لبون خرج مخرج العادة لا مخرج الشرط فالمراد السن لا أن تكون أمها مخاضاً أو لبوناً اهـ. واقتصر الفقهاء على هذه الأسنان الأربعة لأن ما عداها لا مدخل لها في الزكاة كالثني والسديس والباذل تيسيراً على أرباب الأموال بخلاف الأضحية فإنها لا تجوز بهذه الأسنان لأنه لا يجوز فيها إلا الثني ولا يجوز الجذع إلا من الضأن وقالوا هذه الأسنان الأربعة نهاية الإبل في الحسن والدر والنسل والقوة وما زاد عليه فهو رجوع كالكبر والهرم. والأصل في هذا الباب أنه توقيفي، وما في المبسوط مما يفيد أنه معقول المعنى فإنه قال : إن إيجاب الشاة في من الإبل لأن المأمور به ربع العشر بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «هاتوا ربع عشر أموالكم والشاة تقرب من ربع عشر فإن الشاة كانت تقوم بخمسة دراهم هناك وابنة مخاض بأربعين درهماً فإيجاب الشاة في الخمس كإيجابها في المائتين من الدراهم ففيه نظر، لأنه قد ورد في الحديث أن من وجب عليه سن فلم يوجد عنده فإنه يضع العشرة موضع الشاة عند عدمها وهو مصرح بخلافه. وقيد المصنف السن الواجب في الإبل بالإناث لأنه لا يجوز فيها دفع الذكور كابن المخاض إلا بطريق القيمة للإناث إلا فيما دون خمس وعشرين من الإبل فإنه يجوز الذكر والأنثى لأن النص ورد باسم الشاة فإنها تقع على الذكر والأنثى بخلاف البقر والغنم فإنه يجوز في السن الواجب فيهما الذكور والإناث كما سيصرح به من التبيع والمسن. وفي البدائع ولا يجوز في الصدقة إلا ما يجوز في الأضحية. وأطلق فيه الإبل فشمل الذكور والإناث كما قدمناه لأن الشرع ورد بنصابها باسم الإبل والبقر والغنم واسم الجنس يتناول جميع الأنواع بأي صفة كانت كاسم خمسة يفيد اختصاصه بالقائم في مدنه ولم تكن منه سائمة لأنه ملك بالجوز فتدبره . قوله : (إلا فيما دون خمس وعشرين من الإبل الخ قال الرملي : لو قال إلا في الشاة الواجبة فيها لكان أخصر وأصوب لما سيأتي من قوله أعم من الذكر والأنثى وقد «ثم في كل خمس شاة» وهي وجبت فيما زاد على العدد المذكور الذي هو دون الخمسة وعشرين من الإبل تأمل.
Book of Zakat, Chapter on Sadaqat al-Sawa'im. And for less than that, for every five camels, one sheep; for thirty-six, a bint labun; for forty-six, a hiqqah; for sixty-one, a jadha'ah; for seventy-six, a bint labun; for ninety-one, two hiqqahs up to one hundred and twenty. This is whether they are all female, or all male, or some male and some female. I said: The purpose of the condition is to negate them being used for carrying loads, riding, or trade; not to stipulate they be for milk and offspring. Hence, in al-Muhit it adds: they graze with the intent of milk, offspring, increase, and fatness. So males only graze for increase and fatness. But in al-Bada'i': if he grazes them for meat, there is no zakat on them, like carrying and riding. And in al-Qunyah: He has camels used for work four months of the year and he fattens them the rest; it should be that zakat is not obligatory on them. End. Al-Ra'y is the source word for animals grazing herbage; and al-ra'y (with kasra) is the herbage itself; as in al-Mughrib. The appropriate meaning here is fiqh, because as-sa'imah is that which grazes and is not fed at home, intending milk and offspring, as in Fath al-Qadir. So if he brings herbage to them at home, they are not sa'imah. So if ar-ra'y in their speech is taken with kasra, it would be sa'imah. And the herbage they graze must be permissible (mubah) as al-Shumunni restricted it, because herbage linguistically is everything livestock graze, wet or dry, so non-permissible enters. It is pronounced with fatha. He said (And it is obligatory on twenty-five camels, a bint makhad; and for less than that... ) such that the charity letters from the Messenger of Allah (SAW) became famous. Camels have no singular from their own word, and nisba to it is 'ibili' with fatha of ba, like saying in nisba to Salamah 'Salami' with fatha due to consecutive kasras with ya. Al-makhad are pregnant she-camels; ibn al-makhad is the foal whose mother became pregnant before ibn al-labbun by a year; likewise bint makhad. And al-makhad also means the pain of childbirth; He said (This is the common term for later scholars, otherwise the early scholars and linguists allow it). His saying (I said: the purpose of the condition... ) indicates this intent, as in Tuhfat al-Muluk: that as-sa'imah is the one that grazes most of the year, not for riding or work. End. But this answer was examined in al-Nahr: the negation of being for carrying/riding may occur without intending milk and offspring, by intending nothing at all; undoubtedly in this case there is no zakat on him either. End. I said: It is not hidden from you that the gist of the author's answer is that it is a metonymy of the type of stating the implicans and intending the implication, as in your saying 'the situation spoke', so the intention is not the specific mentioned, but rather that which is signified by it. So the intended implication is the negation of it being for riding or trade, just as the intention from 'speaking' is indication. So the author's words amount to what we presented from Tuhfah; and it is not hidden that the criticism does not apply to it; similarly what it amounts to, so reflect. Yes, it is objected by what was mentioned from al-Khaniyyah: if he inherited a sa'imah, zakat is upon him when a year passes, whether he intended or not. Reflect. His saying (and he fattens them in the remainder) : what I saw in al-Qunyah is: he lets them graze (from as-sa'm), not fattening. His saying (so if ar-ra'y is set... ) : al-Nahr said: the (kasra) is common on tongues, and it does not necessitate that it be sa'imah unless one applies 'herbage' to the disconnected [something]; and one may object; rather the apparent meaning of what was mentioned from al-Mughrib, i.e. his statement it is everything livestock grazes from wet and dry. And twenty, then for every five camels a sheep up to one hundred and forty-five, then for it two hiqqahs and a bint makhad; for one hundred and fifty, three hiqqahs; then for every five camels a sheep; for one hundred and seventy-five, three hiqqahs; 'so the pains of childbirth drove her to the trunk of a palm tree' [Maryam:23]; and a sheep with milk is one having milk; ibn al-labbun is one who has completed two years and entered the third; al-hiqq from camels is one who has completed three years and entered the fourth; al-hiqqah is the female, plural hiqaq; al-jadha' from animals is said to be the thani except that it is from camels in the fifth year, the female jadha'ah. This is in language. In Shari'ah, the meaning of bint makhad is one that has completed one year; bint labun is one that has completed two years; al-hiqqah is one that has completed three; al-jadha'ah is one that has completed four. Al-Zayla'i mentioned in the chapter on prohibited things in marriage that the restriction of being bint makhad or bint labun came out as customary, not as a condition, so the intended meaning is the age, not that its mother is pregnant or lactating. End. The jurists confined themselves to these four ages because other than them have no bearing on zakat, like thani, sadis, and badhil, to make it easy for the owners of wealth, unlike udhiyah, for it is not permitted with these ages because only thani is permitted and jadha' is not permitted except from sheep. And they said these four ages are the culmination of camels in good appearance, milk, offspring, and strength; beyond that is regression, like old age and decrepitude. The principle in this chapter is that it is tawqifi (based on revelation). And what is in al-Mabsut suggesting it is rationally understood – for he said: that obligating a sheep for five camels is because what is commanded is a quarter of a tenth by his (SAW) saying 'Bring a quarter of a tenth of your wealth', and a sheep approximates a quarter of a tenth; for the sheep was valued at five dirhams there, and a bint makhad at forty dirhams, so obligating a sheep for five is like obligating it for two hundred dirhams – but there is objection, because it has been reported in the hadith that if someone owes a certain age [of camel] and cannot find it, then he places a ten [dirhams?] in place of a sheep when it is absent, which explicitly contradicts this. The author restricted the obligatory age (sinn) in camels to females because it is not permissible to give males like ibn makhad except by way of value for females, except for less than twenty-five camels, for in that case male and female are allowed because the text mentions 'shah' (sheep) which applies to male and female, unlike cows and goats, for in the obligatory age for them males and females are allowed as will be clarified regarding al-tabee' and al-musinn. In al-Bada'i', it is not permissible in sadaqah except what is permissible in udhiyah. And it [the text] gave camels generally, including both males and females as we mentioned because the Shari'ah mentioned their nisab by the word 'ibil' (camels), 'baqr' (cows), and 'ghanam' (goats), and a generic noun includes all types whatever their description, like the noun 'five' which indicates its specificity to what is present in its cities and it was not from its sa'imah because it was owned by coercion, so reflect. His saying (except for less than twenty-five camels... ) : al-Ramli said: if he said 'except for the shah (sheep) obligatory therein' it would be more concise and correct based on what will come of his saying 'applies to male and female' and then 'for every five camels a sheep', and it was made obligatory for what exceeds the mentioned number which is less than twenty-five camels. Reflect.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This is a commentary from Al-Bahr al-Raiq on Kanz al-Daqaiq, covering the chapter of Zakat on grazing livestock (Sadaqat al-Sawa'im). The passage begins by quoting the matn regarding the nisab of camels: zakat becomes due when one owns five camels, with specific ages (bint makhad, bint labun, hiqqah, jadha'ah) increasing up to 120 camels. The commentator then clarifies a crucial condition: the camels must be Sa'imah, meaning they graze freely on public land for most of the year without being used for riding, labour, or trade. There is an intra-Hanafi discussion: al-Bada'i' holds that if grazing is for meat, no zakat is due, while the majority requires intent for milk and offspring. The correct position is that the condition of Sa'imah excludes animals used for work or trade. The passage also discusses the definition of 'ra'y' (grazing) and emphasizes that the herbage must be permissible (mubah). The second part details the ages (sinn) for zakat: bint makhad (1 year), bint labun (2 years), hiqqah (3 years), jadha'ah (4 years), and notes that these are based on the Prophet's letters (tawqifi). The commentator rejects a rationalist explanation from al-Mabsut, arguing that the nisab is divinely ordained. He also clarifies that the obligatory age (sinn) for camels is female, except below 25 camels where a sheep (which can be male or female) is given. The passage concludes with critical notes on the author's phrasing.

Key Terms
سائمة (sa'imah): Grazing livestock that freely pasture on public herbage for most of the year, without being fed at home or used for work/riding/trade.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers the obligation of zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes sa'imah according to the passage?
A) Camels that are grazed for meat.
B) Camels that graze freely and are not used for work or trade.
C) Camels that are fed at home.
D) All camels that graze.

Key Takeaway
The condition of sa'imah is essential: camels must graze freely and not be used for riding, work, or trade to incur zakat.

Nisab and Ages of Camels in Zakat
Commentary on the nisab and ages of camels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the nisab brackets for camels and identify the obligatory ages (sinn) as derived from the Prophet's letters.

Core Idea
The nisab and ages for zakat on camels are divinely ordained (tawqifi) and precisely specified in the Prophet's letters.

The zakat on camels is structured around specific numbers and ages of animals. This lesson details the nisab brackets from 5 to 120 camels, the corresponding ages due (bint makhad, bint labun, hiqqah, jadha'ah), and the proof from the Prophet's letters. It also addresses the principle that these regulations are tawqifi (revelation-based) rather than rational.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisab brackets
The text lists the thresholds: 5, 25, 36, 46, 61, 76, 91, 120 camels. Beyond 120, the pattern continues.
2
Identify the age (sinn) due at each bracket
For each bracket, determine which animal is due. For example, 5-24 camels: one sheep; 25-35: bint makhad; etc.
3
Trace the proof
The text states that these regulations are from the Prophet's letters (كتب الصدقات).
4
Analyse the definition of ages
The commentary defines each age in years (e.g., bint makhad = 1 year) and notes they are customary, not conditional.
5
Note the principle of tawqifi
The text rejects a rational explanation and emphasizes that the rules are based on revelation.

وعشرين بهذا اشتهرت كتب الصدقات من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. والإبل ليس لها واحد من لفظها والنسبة إليها إبلي بفتح الباء كقولهم في النسبة إلى سلمة سلمي بالفتح لتوالي الكسرات مع الياء والمخاض النوق الحوامل، وابن المخاض هو الفصيل الذي حملت أمه قبل ابن اللبون بسنة، وكذلك بنت المخاض. والمخاض أيضاً وجع الولادة قال تعالى هذا بالأعم اصطلاح للمتأخرين وإلا فالمتقدمون وأهل اللغة على جوازه قوله : (قلت المقصود من الشرط الخ) يدل على هذا القصد ما في تحفة الملوك من أن السائمة الراعية أكثر الحول لا للركوب والعمل ا هـ . لكن نظر في هذا الجواب في النهر بأن نفي الأسامة للحمل والركوب قد يحصل بدون قصد الدر والنسل بأن لا يقصد شيئاً أصلاً، ولا شك أن في هذه الحالة لا زكاة عليه أيضاً ا هـ . قلت : لا يخفى عليك أن محصل جواب المؤلف أنه مجاز من قبيل إطلاق الملزوم وإرادة اللازم كما في قولك «نطقت الحال» فليس المراد خصوص المذكور بل ما أطلق هو عليه، فالمراد اللازم أعني نفي كونها للحمل أو للتجارة كما أن المراد من النطق الدلالة فقد آل كلام المؤلف إلى ما قدمناه عن التحفة، ولا يخفى عدم توجه النظر عليه فكذا ما آل إليه فتدبر نعم يرد عليه ما مر عن الخانية لو ورث سائمة كان عليه الزكاة إذا حال الحول نوى أو لم ينو تأمل قوله : (ويسمنها في الباقي) الذي رأيته في القنية : ويسيمها من الأسامة لا من التسمين قوله : (فلو) ضبط الرعي الخ) قال في النهر : الكسر هو المتداول على الألسنة ولا يلزم عليه أن تكون سائمة إلا لو أطلق الكلأ على المنفصل، ولقائل منعه بل ظاهر ما مرَّ عن المغرب أي من قوله هو كل ما رعته الدواب من الرطب واليابس وعشرين ثم في كل خمس شاة إلى مائة وخمس وأربعين ففيها حقتان وبنت مخاض وفي مائة وخمسين ثلاث حقاق ثم في كل خمس شاة وفي مائة وخمس وسبعين ثلاث حقاق فأجاءها المخاض إلى جذع النخلة ) [مريم : ٢٣] وشاة لبون ذات لبن، وابن اللبون الذي استكمل سنتين ودخل في الثالثة والحق من الإبل ما استكمل ثلاث سنين ودخل في الرابعة، والحقة الأنثى والجمع حقاق والجذع من البهائم قيل الثني إلا أنه من الإبل في السنة الخامسة والأنثى جذعة هذا في اللغة. وفي الشريعة والمراد ببنت المخاض ما تم لها سنة، وبنت اللبون ما تم لها سنتان وبالحقة ما تم لها ثلاث، وبالجذعة ما تم لها أربع. ذكر الزيلعي في فصل المحرمات من النكاح أن قيد كونها بنت مخاض أو بنت لبون خرج مخرج العادة لا مخرج الشرط فالمراد السن لا أن تكون أمها مخاضاً أو لبوناً اهـ. واقتصر الفقهاء على هذه الأسنان الأربعة لأن ما عداها لا مدخل لها في الزكاة كالثني والسديس والباذل تيسيراً على أرباب الأموال بخلاف الأضحية فإنها لا تجوز بهذه الأسنان لأنه لا يجوز فيها إلا الثني ولا يجوز الجذع إلا من الضأن وقالوا هذه الأسنان الأربعة نهاية الإبل في الحسن والدر والنسل والقوة وما زاد عليه فهو رجوع كالكبر والهرم. والأصل في هذا الباب أنه توقيفي، وما في المبسوط مما يفيد أنه معقول المعنى فإنه قال : إن إيجاب الشاة في من الإبل لأن المأمور به ربع العشر بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «هاتوا ربع عشر أموالكم والشاة تقرب من ربع عشر فإن الشاة كانت تقوم بخمسة دراهم هناك وابنة مخاض بأربعين درهماً فإيجاب الشاة في الخمس كإيجابها في المائتين من الدراهم ففيه نظر، لأنه قد ورد في الحديث أن من وجب عليه سن فلم يوجد عنده فإنه يضع العشرة موضع الشاة عند عدمها وهو مصرح بخلافه. وقيد المصنف السن الواجب في الإبل بالإناث لأنه لا يجوز فيها دفع الذكور كابن المخاض إلا بطريق القيمة للإناث إلا فيما دون خمس وعشرين من الإبل فإنه يجوز الذكر والأنثى لأن النص ورد باسم الشاة فإنها تقع على الذكر والأنثى بخلاف البقر والغنم فإنه يجوز في السن الواجب فيهما الذكور والإناث كما سيصرح به من التبيع والمسن. وفي البدائع ولا يجوز في الصدقة إلا ما يجوز في الأضحية. وأطلق فيه الإبل فشمل الذكور والإناث كما قدمناه لأن الشرع ورد بنصابها باسم الإبل والبقر والغنم واسم الجنس يتناول جميع الأنواع بأي صفة كانت كاسم خمسة يفيد اختصاصه بالقائم في مدنه ولم تكن منه سائمة لأنه ملك بالجوز فتدبره . قوله : (إلا فيما دون خمس وعشرين من الإبل الخ قال الرملي : لو قال إلا في الشاة الواجبة فيها لكان أخصر وأصوب لما سيأتي من قوله أعم من الذكر والأنثى وقد «ثم في كل خمس شاة» وهي وجبت فيما زاد على العدد المذكور الذي هو دون الخمسة وعشرين من الإبل تأمل.
Book of Zakat, Chapter on Sadaqat al-Sawa'im. And for less than that, for every five camels, one sheep; for thirty-six, a bint labun; for forty-six, a hiqqah; for sixty-one, a jadha'ah; for seventy-six, a bint labun; for ninety-one, two hiqqahs up to one hundred and twenty. This is whether they are all female, or all male, or some male and some female. I said: The purpose of the condition is to negate them being used for carrying loads, riding, or trade; not to stipulate they be for milk and offspring. Hence, in al-Muhit it adds: they graze with the intent of milk, offspring, increase, and fatness. So males only graze for increase and fatness. But in al-Bada'i': if he grazes them for meat, there is no zakat on them, like carrying and riding. And in al-Qunyah: He has camels used for work four months of the year and he fattens them the rest; it should be that zakat is not obligatory on them. End. Al-Ra'y is the source word for animals grazing herbage; and al-ra'y (with kasra) is the herbage itself; as in al-Mughrib. The appropriate meaning here is fiqh, because as-sa'imah is that which grazes and is not fed at home, intending milk and offspring, as in Fath al-Qadir. So if he brings herbage to them at home, they are not sa'imah. So if ar-ra'y in their speech is taken with kasra, it would be sa'imah. And the herbage they graze must be permissible (mubah) as al-Shumunni restricted it, because herbage linguistically is everything livestock graze, wet or dry, so non-permissible enters. It is pronounced with fatha. He said (And it is obligatory on twenty-five camels, a bint makhad; and for less than that... ) such that the charity letters from the Messenger of Allah (SAW) became famous. Camels have no singular from their own word, and nisba to it is 'ibili' with fatha of ba, like saying in nisba to Salamah 'Salami' with fatha due to consecutive kasras with ya. Al-makhad are pregnant she-camels; ibn al-makhad is the foal whose mother became pregnant before ibn al-labbun by a year; likewise bint makhad. And al-makhad also means the pain of childbirth; He said (This is the common term for later scholars, otherwise the early scholars and linguists allow it). His saying (I said: the purpose of the condition... ) indicates this intent, as in Tuhfat al-Muluk: that as-sa'imah is the one that grazes most of the year, not for riding or work. End. But this answer was examined in al-Nahr: the negation of being for carrying/riding may occur without intending milk and offspring, by intending nothing at all; undoubtedly in this case there is no zakat on him either. End. I said: It is not hidden from you that the gist of the author's answer is that it is a metonymy of the type of stating the implicans and intending the implication, as in your saying 'the situation spoke', so the intention is not the specific mentioned, but rather that which is signified by it. So the intended implication is the negation of it being for riding or trade, just as the intention from 'speaking' is indication. So the author's words amount to what we presented from Tuhfah; and it is not hidden that the criticism does not apply to it; similarly what it amounts to, so reflect. Yes, it is objected by what was mentioned from al-Khaniyyah: if he inherited a sa'imah, zakat is upon him when a year passes, whether he intended or not. Reflect. His saying (and he fattens them in the remainder) : what I saw in al-Qunyah is: he lets them graze (from as-sa'm), not fattening. His saying (so if ar-ra'y is set... ) : al-Nahr said: the (kasra) is common on tongues, and it does not necessitate that it be sa'imah unless one applies 'herbage' to the disconnected [something]; and one may object; rather the apparent meaning of what was mentioned from al-Mughrib, i.e. his statement it is everything livestock grazes from wet and dry. And twenty, then for every five camels a sheep up to one hundred and forty-five, then for it two hiqqahs and a bint makhad; for one hundred and fifty, three hiqqahs; then for every five camels a sheep; for one hundred and seventy-five, three hiqqahs; 'so the pains of childbirth drove her to the trunk of a palm tree' [Maryam:23]; and a sheep with milk is one having milk; ibn al-labbun is one who has completed two years and entered the third; al-hiqq from camels is one who has completed three years and entered the fourth; al-hiqqah is the female, plural hiqaq; al-jadha' from animals is said to be the thani except that it is from camels in the fifth year, the female jadha'ah. This is in language. In Shari'ah, the meaning of bint makhad is one that has completed one year; bint labun is one that has completed two years; al-hiqqah is one that has completed three; al-jadha'ah is one that has completed four. Al-Zayla'i mentioned in the chapter on prohibited things in marriage that the restriction of being bint makhad or bint labun came out as customary, not as a condition, so the intended meaning is the age, not that its mother is pregnant or lactating. End. The jurists confined themselves to these four ages because other than them have no bearing on zakat, like thani, sadis, and badhil, to make it easy for the owners of wealth, unlike udhiyah, for it is not permitted with these ages because only thani is permitted and jadha' is not permitted except from sheep. And they said these four ages are the culmination of camels in good appearance, milk, offspring, and strength; beyond that is regression, like old age and decrepitude. The principle in this chapter is that it is tawqifi (based on revelation). And what is in al-Mabsut suggesting it is rationally understood – for he said: that obligating a sheep for five camels is because what is commanded is a quarter of a tenth by his (SAW) saying 'Bring a quarter of a tenth of your wealth', and a sheep approximates a quarter of a tenth; for the sheep was valued at five dirhams there, and a bint makhad at forty dirhams, so obligating a sheep for five is like obligating it for two hundred dirhams – but there is objection, because it has been reported in the hadith that if someone owes a certain age [of camel] and cannot find it, then he places a ten [dirhams?] in place of a sheep when it is absent, which explicitly contradicts this. The author restricted the obligatory age (sinn) in camels to females because it is not permissible to give males like ibn makhad except by way of value for females, except for less than twenty-five camels, for in that case male and female are allowed because the text mentions 'shah' (sheep) which applies to male and female, unlike cows and goats, for in the obligatory age for them males and females are allowed as will be clarified regarding al-tabee' and al-musinn. In al-Bada'i', it is not permissible in sadaqah except what is permissible in udhiyah. And it [the text] gave camels generally, including both males and females as we mentioned because the Shari'ah mentioned their nisab by the word 'ibil' (camels), 'baqr' (cows), and 'ghanam' (goats), and a generic noun includes all types whatever their description, like the noun 'five' which indicates its specificity to what is present in its cities and it was not from its sa'imah because it was owned by coercion, so reflect. His saying (except for less than twenty-five camels... ) : al-Ramli said: if he said 'except for the shah (sheep) obligatory therein' it would be more concise and correct based on what will come of his saying 'applies to male and female' and then 'for every five camels a sheep', and it was made obligatory for what exceeds the mentioned number which is less than twenty-five camels. Reflect.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This is a commentary from Al-Bahr al-Raiq on Kanz al-Daqaiq, covering the chapter of Zakat on grazing livestock (Sadaqat al-Sawa'im). The passage begins by quoting the matn regarding the nisab of camels: zakat becomes due when one owns five camels, with specific ages (bint makhad, bint labun, hiqqah, jadha'ah) increasing up to 120 camels. The commentator then clarifies a crucial condition: the camels must be Sa'imah, meaning they graze freely on public land for most of the year without being used for riding, labour, or trade. There is an intra-Hanafi discussion: al-Bada'i' holds that if grazing is for meat, no zakat is due, while the majority requires intent for milk and offspring. The correct position is that the condition of Sa'imah excludes animals used for work or trade. The passage also discusses the definition of 'ra'y' (grazing) and emphasizes that the herbage must be permissible (mubah). The second part details the ages (sinn) for zakat: bint makhad (1 year), bint labun (2 years), hiqqah (3 years), jadha'ah (4 years), and notes that these are based on the Prophet's letters (tawqifi). The commentator rejects a rationalist explanation from al-Mabsut, arguing that the nisab is divinely ordained. He also clarifies that the obligatory age (sinn) for camels is female, except below 25 camels where a sheep (which can be male or female) is given. The passage concludes with critical notes on the author's phrasing.

Key Terms
بنت مخاض (bint makhad): A female camel that has completed one year of age (referred to as ibn makhad for male).
بنت لبون (bint labun): A female camel that has completed two years of age.
حقة (hiqqah): A female camel that has completed three years of age.
جذعة (jadha'ah): A female camel that has completed four years of age.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers the obligation of zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
At what nisab does zakat on camels begin?
A) 1 camel
B) 5 camels
C) 10 camels
D) 25 camels

Key Takeaway
The nisab and ages for zakat on camels are precisely defined by the Prophet's letters and are tawqifi (revealed), not based on analogy.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
10 min
Zakat Grades for Camels: Schedule, Age Terms, and Key Rulings
Hanafi zakat schedule for camels with definitions and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi zakat schedule for camels from 5 to 200+, define the four age terms (bint makhad, bint labun, hiqqa, jadha'a) as pure age indicators, and apply the rulings for gender and emaciated camels.

Core Idea
Zakat on camels follows a fixed schedule revealed by the Prophet (tawqifi), with age‐based terms that refer to the camel's own age, not its mother's condition.

The zakat on camels is not a simple percentage; it is a graded schedule based on the number of camels owned and the animals' ages. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq opens by presenting the exact obligations from 5 to over 200 camels. It then clarifies the legal meanings of the age terms—bint makhad, bint labun, hiqqa, jadha'a—emphasising that they indicate the camel's own completed years, not its mother's pregnancy or lactation. The author also discusses the school's reliance on textual command (tawqifi) rather than rational analogy, and addresses practical issues such as which gender is due and how to calculate zakat on emaciated camels.

Guided Path
1
Memorise the schedule for 5–200 camels
Read the matn (italicised in the commentary) which lists obligations: for every 5 camels up to 25, one she-ep or he-goat; at 25–35, a bint makhad; at 36–45, a bint labun; at 46–60, a hiqqa; at 61–75, a jadha'a; then every 5 adds a sheep until 145, where two hiqqas and a bint makhad are due; at 150, three hiqqas; at 175, three hiqqas and a bint makhad; at 186, three hiqqas and a bint labun; at 196, four hiqqas; at 200, the owner may choose four hiqqas or five bint labun.
The schedule is tawqifi, meaning it is based on revelation, not rational derivation.
2
Define the four age terms
For each term—bint makhad (1 year), bint labun (2 years), hiqqa (3 years), jadha'a (4 years)—note that the Hanafi school treats them as purely age-based. The linguistic reference to the mother's condition (pregnancy/lactation) is customary, not a condition.
Al-Zayla'i explicitly states this in the chapter on prohibited women in marriage.
3
Understand the proof (tawqifi vs. rational)
The passage mentions the hadith 'Give a quarter-tenth of your wealth' and an attempt to rationalise the schedule: a sheep is about one-fifth the value of a bint makhad, so it approximates the quarter-tenth of five camels. However, the author rejects this because a different hadith (substituting ten sheep when the owed age is absent) contradicts that analogy. Thus, the schedule is finally from revelation (tawqifi).
This reinforces that zakat on camels is an ibadah with fixed rules, not subject to ijtihad.
4
Apply gender and value rules
For camels under 25, the due animal (shah) can be male or female. For higher nisabs, the zakat must be a female camel (except by value). The rule for emaciated (mahazil) camels is that zakat must be proportional to their value, using the average healthy camel as a reference to avoid hardship on the owner.
The text cites al-Bada'i' and al-Walwalijiyya for these details.

للإناث إلا فيما دون خمس وعشرين من الإبل فإنه يجوز الذكر والأنثى لأن النص ورد باسم الشاة فإنها تقع على الذكر والأنثى بخلاف البقر والغنم فإنه يجوز في السن الواجب فيهما الذكور والإناث كما سيصرح به من صفة كانت كاسم الحيوان، وسواء كان متولداً من الأهليين أو من أهلي ووحشي بعد أن كان الأم أهلية كالمتولد الشاة والظبي إذا كان أمه شاة والمتولد من البقر الأهلي والوحشي إذا كان أمه أهلية فتجب الزكاة فيه كذا في البدائع وشمل الصغار والكبار لكن بشرط أن لا يكون الكل صغاراً لما سيصرح به بعد ذلك فالصغار تبع للكبار عند الاختلاط وشمل الأعمى والمريض والأعرج في العدد ولا يؤخذ في الصدقة كما في الولوالجية، وشمل السمان والعجاف لكن قالوا: إذا كان له خمس من الإبل مهازيل وجب فيها شاة بقدرهن ومعرفة ذلك أن ينظر إلى الشاة الوسط كم هي من بنت المخاض الوسط؛ فإن كانت قيمة بنت مخاض وسط خمسين وقيمة الشاة الوسط عشرة تبين أن الشاة الوسط خمس بنت مخاض فوجب في المهازيل شاة قيمتها قيمة خمس واحدة منها، وإن كان سدسها فسدس، وعلى هذا قياسه. وإن كان لا يبلغ قيمة كلها قيمة بنت مخاض وسط ينظر إلى قيمة أعلاهن فيجب فيها من الزكاة قدر خمس أعلاهن، فإن كانت قيمة أعلاهن فإن كانت قيمة أعلاهن عشرين فخمسه أربعة فيجب فيها شاة تساوي أربعة دراهم وإن كانت قيمة أعلاهن ثلاثين فخمسه ستة دراهم لأنه لاوجه لإيجاب الشاة الوسط لأنه لعل قيمتها تبلغ قيمة واحدة من العجاف أو تربو عليها فيؤدي إلى الإجحاف بأرباب الأموال فأوجبنا شاة بقدرهم ليعتدل النظر من الجانبين، وكذا في العشرة منها يجب شاتان بقدرهن إلى خمس وعشرين فيجب واحدة من أفضلهن، وتمام تفريعات زكاة العجاف في الزيادات والمحيط وغيرها . قوله: (ثم في كل خمس شاة إلى مائة وخمس وأربعين ففيها حقتان وبنت مخاض وفي مائة وخمسين ثلاث حقاق ثم في كل خمس شاة وفي مائة وخمس وسبعين ثلاث حقاق وبنت مخاض وفي مائة وست وثمانين ثلاث حقاق وبنت لبون وفي مائة وست وتسعين أربع حقاق إلى مائتين ثم تستأنف أبداً كما بعد مائة وخمسين كما ورد ذلك في كتاب عمرو بن حزم. وفي المبسوط وفتاوى قاضيخان: إذا صارت مائتين فهو مخير إن شاء أدى فيها أربع حقاق في كل خمسين حقة، وإن شاء أدى خمس بنات لبون في كل أربعين بنت لبون. وفي معراج الدراية: إن له الخيار فيما إذا كانت مائة وستاً وتسعين إن شاء أدى أربع حقاق وإن شاء صير
Book of Zakat, Chapter on Zakat of Grazing Livestock. (From twenty) then for every five a sheep until one hundred and forty-five: then in it two hiqqas and one bint makhad. For one hundred and fifty: three hiqqas. Then for every five a sheep. For one hundred and seventy-five: three hiqqas. And the pains of childbirth drove her to the trunk of a palm tree [Maryam: 23]. And a sheep labun (having milk), and ibn al-labun (the one who has completed two years and entered the third). And al-hiqq of camels: what has completed three years and entered the fourth. Al-hiqqa is the female, plural hiqaq. And al-jadha' of animals: it is said the thani except that it is from camels in the fifth year, and the female is jadha'a. This is linguistic. In shari'ah, what is meant by bint makhad is one year completed; bint labun: two years completed; al-hiqqa: three years completed; al-jadha'a: four years completed. Al-Zayla'i mentioned in the chapter on prohibited women in marriage that the restriction of being bint makhad or bint labun is customary, not conditional; so the meaning is age, not that its mother is pregnant or lactating. The jurists confined to these four ages because others have no part in zakat, like al-thani and al-sadis and al-badhl, as a facility for owners of wealth, unlike sacrifice for which these ages are not permissible because only al-thani is permissible and al-jadha' is not permissible except from sheep. They said these four ages are the peak of camels in beauty, milk, offspring, and strength; what is beyond is regression like old age and senility. The basis is that it is tawqifi (restricted to textual command). What is in al-Mabsut indicating it is rationally understood: that the obligation of a sheep for five camels is because what is commanded is a quarter-tenth from his statement (peace be upon him) 'Give a quarter-tenth of your wealth', and a sheep is close to a quarter-tenth, for a sheep was valued at five dirhams there and a bint makhad at forty dirhams, so obligating a sheep at five is like obligating it at two hundred dirhams. But there is consideration because it is reported in the hadith that if someone owes a particular age and does not have it, he should substitute ten [sheep] when a sheep is absent, which explicitly contradicts that. The author restricted the due age in camels to females because it is not permissible to give males like ibn makhad except by way of value for females, except for camels under twenty-five, where both male and female are allowed because the text came with the word 'shah' which applies to both male and female, unlike cattle and sheep where males and females are allowed as will be stated from al-tabi' and al-musinn. In al-Bada'i': 'And nothing is permissible in sadaqah except what is permissible in sacrifice.' And he used the absolute term camels, covering both males and females, because the shari'ah came with the nisab using the names of camels, cattle, and sheep, and the genus term encompasses all types regardless of quality, like the name animal. And it includes whether it is born from domesticated parents or from a domesticated and wild parent as long as the mother is domesticated, like the offspring of a sheep and a gazelle if its mother is a sheep, and the offspring of domesticated cattle and wild cattle if its mother is domesticated; then zakat is due as in al-Bada'i'. And it includes young and old, but with the condition that they are not all young, as will be stated later; minors follow majore when mixed. And it includes the blind, sick, and lame in counting, but they are not taken in sadaqah as in al-Walwalijiyyah. And it includes fat and thin, but they said: If one has five emaciated camels, a sheep proportional to them is due. The way to determine that is to look at the average sheep value relative to the average bint makhad; if the average bint makhad is worth fifty and the average sheep ten, then the average sheep is one-fifth of a bint makhad; so for emaciated camels, a sheep worth one-fifth of a single one of them is due; if it is one-sixth, then one-sixth, and so on. And if the value of all of them does not reach the value of an average bint makhad, then look to the value of the best of them; then zakat due is one-fifth of the best of them. If the value of the best is twenty, its fifth is four; so a sheep worth four dirhams is due; if thirty, its fifth is six dirhams. This is because there is no basis for obligating the average sheep since its value might reach the value of one of the thin ones or exceed it, leading to injustice against the owners. So we obligate a sheep proportional to them to achieve balance. Similarly, for ten emaciated camels, two sheep proportional to them are due, up to twenty-five, then one of the best of them is due. The full rulings on zakat of thin animals are in al-Ziyadat, al-Muhit, and others. His statement: (Then for every five a sheep until one hundred and forty-five: then in it two hiqqas and a bint makhad. For one hundred and fifty: three hiqqas. Then for every five a sheep. For one hundred and seventy-five: three hiqqas and a bint makhad. For one hundred and eighty-six: three hiqqas and a bint labun. For one hundred and ninety-six: four hiqqas until two hundred. Then it starts again as after one hundred and fifty) as recorded in the book of Amr ibn Hazm. In al-Mabsut and Fatawa Qadikhan: when it reaches two hundred, the owner has the option: if he wishes, he gives four hiqqas, one hiqqa for every fifty; if he wishes, he gives five bint labun, one bint labun for every forty. In Miraj al-Dirayah: he has the option when it is one hundred and ninety-six: if he wishes, he gives four hiqqas; if he wishes, he gives...
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the zakat schedule for camels. It opens with the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq listing the obligations at various nisab levels from 5 to 200. The commentary then defines the key age terms: bint makhad (1 year), bint labun (2 years), hiqqa (3 years), jadha'a (4 years). The author explicitly follows the Hanafi position that these terms refer to age, not actual lactation/pregnancy status, as stated by al-Zayla'i. The Hanafi school limits zakat on camels to these four ages for convenience, unlike sacrifice (udhiyya) where only thani and jadha' from sheep are allowed. The text then discusses the proof: the hadith 'Give a quarter-tenth of your wealth' and the analogy that a sheep approximates a quarter-tenth of five camels in value. However, the author notes a problem with this rational explanation because another hadith requires substituting ten sheep when the owed age is unavailable, contradicting the proportional argument. Hence the hanafi position is that the schedule is tawqifi (based solely on revelation). The passage then clarifies the gender rule: for camels under 25, male or female sheep (shah) is accepted because the term is generic; for higher numbers, only female camels are due, except by value. This differs from cattle and sheep where both genders are acceptable. The text then covers rulings for mixed breeds (offspring of domestic and wild) and includes young, old, blind, sick animals in the count but not taken as payment. Finally, it details the calculation for emaciated (mahazil) camels: the zakat must be proportional to the value of the camel, using the average value relative to a healthy bint makhad, to avoid hardship. The schedule ends at 200 camels, where the owner has options between hiqqas and bint labun.

Key Terms
بنت مخاض (bint makhad): A she-camel that has completed one year and entered the second; linguistically it refers to a young camel whose mother is pregnant (makhad means pregnant), but in shari'ah it denotes age only.
بنت لبون (bint labun): A she-camel that has completed two years and entered the third; linguistically referring to a camel whose mother is lactating (labun), but legally indicates age.
حقة (hiqqa): A she-camel that has completed three years and entered the fourth; the female is called hiqqa, plural hiqaq.
جذعة (jadha'a): A she-camel that has completed four years and entered the fifth; also used for other animals but in camels it's the fourth year.
شاة (shah): A sheep or goat, used as zakat payment for camels up to 25; includes both male and female.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
At what number of camels does the zakat increase to two hiqqas and one bint makhad?
A) 50 camels
B) 145 camels
C) 150 camels
D) 175 camels

Key Takeaway
Zakat on camels follows a fixed, revealed schedule (tawqifi) where age terms indicate the camel's own completed years, and rules for gender and emaciated animals ensure fairness.

Zakat on Crossbred and Emaciated Camels
Ruling on crossbred and emaciated camels in zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for crossbred camels and calculate zakat for emaciated camels using the proportional value method.

Core Idea
Zakat on emaciated camels is proportional to value, not count, to avoid injustice to the owner.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies two special cases in camel zakat: crossbred animals and emaciated ones. For crossbred camels, the ruling depends on the mother's domesticity. For emaciated camels, the standard count-based zakat would be unfair, so the Hanafi school requires a value-based calculation. Understanding this proportional method is essential for correctly fulfilling your zakat obligation on weak or thin livestock.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for crossbred camels
Note that the passage states that crossbred animals are treated as domestic animals if their mother is domestic, regardless of the father. For example, a camel born to a domestic camel mother and a wild camel father is subject to zakat like any domestic camel.
This applies to all animal types (sheep, cattle, camels).
2
Recognize inclusion of all camel types in nisab
The passage explains that small, blind, sick, and lame camels are counted in the total number for determining nisab. However, they are not taken as zakat payments themselves; instead, a healthy animal is given.
Small camels follow the large when mixed, but if all are small the ruling differs.
3
Distinguish emaciated camels and the need for value-based zakat
Emaciated camels are also counted in the nisab, but when it comes to paying zakat, their low condition is considered. Instead of taking a specific age category (like bint makhad), the Hanafi school prescribes a sheep whose value is proportional to the value of the camels.
This prevents forcing the owner to give a healthy animal worth more than the camels themselves.
4
Apply the proportional calculation method
To find the zakat due on five emaciated camels: compare the value of an average sheep to an average bint makhad camel. If an average bint makhad is worth 50 dirhams and an average sheep is worth 10, then each camel's zakat is 1/5 of a bint makhad, i.e., a sheep worth 1/5 of one camel's value. If the total value of the five camels is less than one bint makhad, look at the best camel, take one-fifth of its value, and give a sheep of that value.
For 10 emaciated camels, two sheep proportional to value; for 25, one from the best.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من الحيوان، وسواء كان متولداً من الأهليين أو من أهلي ووحشي بعد أن كان الأم أهلية كالمتولد الشاة والظبي إذا كان أمه شاة والمتولد من البقر الأهلي والوحشي إذا كان أمه أهلية فتجب الزكاة فيه كذا في البدائع وشمل الصغار والكبار لكن بشرط أن لا يكون الكل صغاراً لما سیصرح به بعد ذلك فالصغار تبع للكبار عند الاختلاط وشمل الأعمى والمريض والأعرج في العدد ولا يؤخذ في الصدقة كما في الولوالجية، وشمل السمان والعجاف لكن قالوا : إذا كان له خمس من الإبل مهازيل وجب فيها شاة بقدرهن ومعرفة ذلك أن ينظر إلى الشاة الوسط كم هي من بنت المخاض الوسط ؛ فإن كانت قيمة بنت مخاض وسط خمسين وقيمة الشاة الوسط عشرة تبين أن الشاة الوسط خمس بنت مخاض فوجب في المهازيل شاة قيمتها قيمة خمس واحدة منها، وإن كان سدسها فسدس، وعلى هذا قياسه. وإن كان لا يبلغ قيمة كلها قيمة بنت مخاض وسط ينظر إلى قيمة أعلاهن فيجب فيها من الزكاة قدر خمس أعلاهن، فإن كانت قيمة أعلاهن فإن كانت قيمة أعلاهن عشرين فخمسه أربعة فيجب فيها شاة تساوي أربعة دراهم وإن كانت قيمة أعلاهن ثلاثين فخمسه ستة دراهم لأنه لاوجه لإيجاب الشاة الوسط لأنه لعل قيمتها تبلغ قيمة واحدة من العجاف أو تربو عليها فيؤدي إلى الإجحاف بأرباب الأموال فأوجبنا شاة بقدرهم ليعتدل النظر من الجانبين، وكذا في العشرة منها يجب شاتان بقدرهن إلى خمس وعشرين فيجب واحدة من أفضلهن، وتمام تفريعات زكاة العجاف في الزيادات والمحيط وغيرها .
From animals, and it is the same whether it is born from two domestic parents or from a domestic and a wild one provided that the mother is domestic, like a sheep and a gazelle if its mother is a sheep, and like a domestic cow and a wild cow if its mother is domestic; so zakat is obligatory on it. Thus in al-Bada'i. And it includes small and large but with the condition that they are not all small, as will be stated later. So the small are dependent on the large when mixed. And it includes the blind, the sick, and the lame in the count, and they are not taken in sadaqah, as in al-Walwaljiyyah. And it includes the fat and the emaciated, but they said: if he has five emaciated camels, then one sheep is obligatory according to their value. The knowledge of that is that one looks at the average sheep: how much is it of the average bint makhad? If the value of an average bint makhad is fifty and the value of an average sheep is ten, it becomes clear that the average sheep is one-fifth of a bint makhad. So for emaciated camels, a sheep whose value is one-fifth of one of them is obligatory. And if it were one-sixth, then one-sixth, and so on. And if the value of all of them does not reach the value of an average bint makhad, then one looks at the value of the best among them, and zakat is obligatory on them to the extent of one-fifth of the best among them. If the value of the best is twenty, then one-fifth is four, so a sheep worth four dirhams is obligatory. If the value of the best is thirty, then one-fifth is six dirhams. Because there is no basis for obligating the average sheep because perhaps its value reaches the value of one of the emaciated or exceeds it, leading to injustice to the owners. So we have obligated a sheep according to their value to balance the consideration from both sides. Similarly, for ten of them, two sheep according to their value, up to twenty-five, then one from the best of them is obligatory. The complete details of zakat on emaciated animals are in al-Ziyadat, al-Muhit, and others.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq, discussing the rulings on zakat for camels that are crossbred or emaciated. The author states that crossbred animals are treated as domestic if the mother is domestic, regardless of the father. This includes offspring of a domestic sheep and a wild gazelle, or domestic cow and wild cow, with the condition that the mother is domestic. Zakat is due on them. The ruling also covers both young and adult camels, but if all are young, the condition differs. Small camels follow the large when mixed. Blind, sick, and lame camels are counted in the total number but are not taken as zakat themselves. Fat and emaciated camels are also included. For emaciated camels, the zakat due is proportional to their value. The author explains the calculation: compare the value of an average sheep to an average bint makhad (a specific type of camel). For five emaciated camels, if the total value is less than a bint makhad, look at the best among them and take one-fifth of its value as a sheep. This avoids injustice to the owner. The reasoning is qiyas-based, using the effective cause of proportional value. The full details are in other sources, indicating this is not exhaustive.

Key Terms
مهازيل (mahāzīl): Emaciated camels, thin and weak, for which zakat is calculated based on their value rather than count.
بنت مخاض (bint makhāḍ): A female camel that has entered its second year and whose mother is pregnant (makhad). It is a specific age category used in zakat schedules.
شاة (shāh): A sheep (or goat) that is given as zakat for camels when the number reaches certain thresholds.

Key Takeaway
Zakat on emaciated camels is value-proportional, ensuring fairness by avoiding overburdening the owner.
