Zakat Schedule for Camels: From 145 to 200+ and the Intra-Hanafi Option
Explains the zakat schedule for camels and presents intra-Hanafi differences on options for payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the zakat schedule for camels from 145 to 200+ and state the intra-Hanafi option at 200 camels, as well as the unresolved question about the life of the sheep.

Core Idea
At 200 camels, the Hanafi school allows the owner to choose between 4 hiqaq or 5 bint labun.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the fixed zakat schedule for camels, but reveals an important intra-Hanafi flexibility: at certain thresholds, the owner has a choice between two valid options. Understanding this ikhtilaf within the school is crucial for accurate fatwa and practice. The passage also touches on an unresolved point regarding whether the sheep offered must be alive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base schedule
Read the matn's fixed schedule from 145 to 200 camels: at 145, two hiqaq and a bint makhad; at 150, three hiqaq; and so on. Note that the schedule restarts after 200 as it did after 150.
This schedule is derived from the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi option
Find the statement from al-Mabsut and Fatawa Qadikhan: at 200 camels, the owner may choose between 4 hiqaq (one per 50) or 5 bint labun (one per 40). Note that Ma'arij al-Diraya extends this option to 196 camels.
This option is a later development within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the expansion
The commentator explains the difference between the restart after 150 and after 120, showing how the schedule scales beyond 200. He also reports al-Ramli's question about whether the sheep must be alive.
The expansion clarifies the calculations and unresolved issues.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
According to later Hanafi authorities, the option at 200 is the relied-upon position. The question of the sheep's life remains unresolved (tawaqquf) by some, while others require life.
The mufta bihi is the option, but the life condition is not definitively settled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم في كل خمس شاة إلى مائة وخمس وأربعين ففيها حقتان وبنت مخاض وفي مائة وخمسين ثلاث حقاق ثم في كل خمس شاة وفي مائة وخمس وسبعين ثلاث حقاق وبنت مخاض وفي مائة وست وثمانين ثلاث حقاق وبنت لبون وفي مائة وست وتسعين أربع حقاق إلى مائتين ثم تستأنف أبداً كما بعد مائة وخمسين كما ورد ذلك في كتاب عمرو بن حزم. وفي المبسوط وفتاوى قاضيخان : إذا صارت مائتين فهو مخير إن شاء أدى فيها أربع حقاق في كل خمسين حقة، وإن شاء أدى خمس بنات لبون في كل أربعين بنت لبون. وفي معراج الدراية : إن له الخيار فيما إذا كانت مائة وستاً وتسعين إن شاء أدى أربع حقاق وإن شاء صير لتكمل مائتين فيخير بينها وبين خمس بنات لبون. وإنما قيد في الاستئناف بقوله «كما بعد مائة وخمسين ليفيد أنه ليس كالاستئناف الذي بعد المائة والعشرين. والفرق بينهما أن في الاستئناف الثاني إيجاب ليفيد أنه ليس كالاستئناف الذي بعد المائة والعشرين، والفرق بينهما أن في الاستئناف الثاني إيجاب بنت لبون، وفي الاستئناف الأول لم يكن لانعدام نصابه، وأن الواجب في الاستئناف الأول تغير من الخمس إلى أن تستأنف الفريضة، وفي الاستئناف الثاني لم يكن كذلك، فإذا زاد على المائتين خمس ففيها شاة مع الأربع حقاق أو الخمس بنات لبون، وفي عشر شاتان معها، وفي خمسة عشر ثلاث شياه معها، وفي عشرين أربع معها، فإذا بلغت مائتين وخمساً وعشرين ففيها بنت مخاض معها إلى ست وثلاثين فبنت لبون معها إلى ست وأربعين ومائتين ففيها خمس حقاق إلى مائتين وخمسين ثم تستأنف كذلك ففي مائتين وست وتسعين ست حقاق إلى ثلثمائة وهكذا قوله : (ثم في كل خمس شاة ذكر الرملي أنه ورد سؤال لبعض الفضلاء أنه هل تشترط حياة
His statement: 'Then for every five, a sheep until one hundred and forty-five, then for that there are two hiqaq and a bint makhad, and at one hundred and fifty, three hiqaq, then for every five a sheep, and at one hundred and seventy-five, three hiqaq and a bint makhad, and at one hundred and eighty-six, three hiqaq and a bint labun, and at one hundred and ninety-six, four hiqaq until two hundred, then it restarts forever as after one hundred and fifty' as reported in the book of Amr ibn Hazm. And in al-Mabsut and Fatawa Qadikhan: when it reaches two hundred, he has a choice: if he wishes, he gives four hiqaq for each fifty a hiqqa, and if he wishes, he gives five bint labun for each forty a bint labun. And in Ma'arij al-Diraya: he has the choice when it is one hundred and ninety-six: if he wishes, he gives four hiqaq, and if he wishes, he can make up to two hundred and then choose between that and five bint labun. And he restricted the restart by his statement 'as after one hundred and fifty' to indicate that it is not like the restart after one hundred and twenty. The difference between them is that in the second restart there is an obligation of bint labun, while in the first restart there was no nisab for it, and the wajib in the first restart changed from five to that the fard starts again, but not in the second restart. So when it exceeds two hundred by five, there is a sheep with the four hiqaq or the five bint labun; at ten, two sheep with them; at fifteen, three sheep; at twenty, four sheep. When it reaches two hundred and twenty-five, there is a bint makhad with them up to two hundred and thirty-six, then a bint labun with them up to two hundred and forty-six, then five hiqaq up to two hundred and fifty, then it restarts likewise. At two hundred and ninety-six, six hiqaq up to three hundred, and so on. His statement: 'Then for every five, a sheep' – al-Ramli mentioned that a question came from some scholars: is life (of the sheep) a condition?
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on the matn statement regarding the zakat schedule for camels from 145 to 200 and beyond. The matn states the fixed rates: at 145, two hiqaq and a bint makhad; at 150, three hiqaq; at 175, three hiqaq and a bint makhad; at 186, three hiqaq and a bint labun; at 196, four hiqaq up to 200. Then the schedule restarts similarly as after 150 camels. This schedule is based on the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm, a written instruction from the Prophet. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding options. According to al-Mabsut and Fatawa Qadikhan, at 200 camels, the owner can choose to give either 4 hiqaq (one per 50) or 5 bint labun (one per 40). Ma'arij al-Diraya extends this option to 196 as well. The text then explains the difference between the restart after 150 and after 120, and details the calculations for numbers beyond 200. At the end, al-Ramli notes a question about whether the sheep offered must be alive; the answer is suspended (tawaqquf) according to some, while others insist on life. This is an unresolved point within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
حقة (ḥiqqa): A female camel that has entered its fourth year and is ready to be bred; used as a zakat category.
بنت لبون (bint labūn): A female camel that has entered its third year and whose mother is lactating; another zakat category.
استئناف (istiʼnāf): Restarting the schedule; after certain numbers, the sequence begins again.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Mabsut and Fatawa Qadikhan, what option does the owner of 200 camels have?
A) Only 4 hiqaq are obligatory
B) Only 5 bint labun are obligatory
C) He may choose between 4 hiqaq or 5 bint labun
D) He may choose between 4 hiqaq or 4 bint labun

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits an option at 200 camels, allowing the owner to choose between 4 hiqaq or 5 bint labun.

Bactrian Camels Treated Like Arabian Camels for Zakat
Defines Bactrian camels and equates their zakat ruling to Arabian camels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the zakat ruling for Bactrian camels and explain why they are included under the general term 'ibil'.

Core Idea
Bactrian camels are included in 'ibil' for zakat; type difference does not exclude from the genus.

When calculating zakat on livestock, the type of camel matters only within the species. This lesson examines a basic but critical rule: Bactrian camels (two-humped, crossbred) are treated identically to Arabian (one-humped) camels for zakat. The reason is linguistic and legal: the Quranic term 'ibil' covers all camels, regardless of breed. We'll break down the passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq that confirms this principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is owning a certain number of Bactrian camels. The ruling is that zakat is wajib on them just as on Arabian camels.
The hukm is the same; no separate nisab or rate for different camel types.
2
Understand the Legal Basis
The basis is that the word 'ibil' (camels) in the Quran and hadith includes all camels, regardless of breed or origin. The difference in type (single-humped vs. double-humped) does not remove them from the genus.
This is a straightforward application of linguistic generality.
3
Clarify the Terminology
'البخت' (al-bakht) refers to crossbred camels, offspring of Arabian and non-Arabian. 'العراب' (al-'irab) are pure Arabian camels. The passage explains the etymology and plural forms.
Understanding the terms helps avoid confusion about which animals are subject to zakat.
4
Apply to a Scenario
If a person has 5 Bactrian camels (over a year), they are subject to the same zakat as 5 Arabian camels – i.e., one goat for 5-9 camels. No exemption due to breed.
The nisab and payment rates are identical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والبخت كالعراب) لأن اسم الإبل يتناولهما واختلافهما في النوع لا يخرجهما من الجنس والبخت جمع بختى وهو الذي تولد من العربي والعجمي منسوب إلى بخت نصر والعراب جمع عربي للبهائم وللأناسي عرب ففرقوا بينهما في الجمع. والعرب هم الذين استوطنوا المدن والقرى العربية والأعراب أهل البدو واختلف في نسبتهم ، فالأصح أنهم نسبوا إلى عَرَبة بفتحتين وهي من تهامة لأن أباهم إسماعيل عليه السلام نشأ بها كذا في المغرب والله أعلم بالصواب وإليه المرجع والمآب.
His statement: 'And the Bactrian camels are like the Arabian camels.' Because the name 'ibil' encompasses both, and their difference in type does not remove them from the genus. Al-Bakht (Bactrian) is the plural of bakhti, which is the offspring of an Arabian and a non-Arabian, attributed to Bukht Nasr. Al-Arab (Arabian) is the plural of arabi for animals, and for humans, 'arab' and 'a'rab' are distinguished in their plurals. 'Arab' are those who settled in Arab cities and villages, while 'a'rab' are bedouins. There is a difference in their attribution; the most correct is that they are attributed to 'Arabah (with two fatha's), which is a place in Tihamah, because their father Isma'il (peace be upon him) grew up there. Thus in al-Mughrib. And Allah knows best the truth, and to Him is the return and the refuge.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage explains the matn statement 'والبخت كالعراب' (Bactrian camels are like Arabian camels). The commentator clarifies that the word 'ibil' (camels) includes both types, so they share the same zakat rulings. The difference in breed or origin does not change the genus. He then provides linguistic notes: 'بخت' (Bactrian) is plural of 'بختى', a crossbreed between Arabian and non-Arabian camels, named after Bukht Nasr. 'عراب' (Arabian) is plural of 'عربي' for animals, while for humans, 'عرب' and 'أعراب' are distinguished: 'عرب' are settled Arabs, 'أعراب' are bedouins. The commentator also mentions the correct etymology of 'عرب' from 'عربة' in Tihamah, where Isma'il grew up. This passage is a brief linguistic and legal clarification, with no proof beyond the general rule.

Key Terms
البخت (al-bakht): Bactrian camels, a type of camel with two humps, often crossbred between Arabian and non-Arabian camels.
العراب (al-ʿirāb): Arabian camels, the single-humped dromedary camels, considered the standard type for zakat.

Key Takeaway

Zakat on Cattle: Rates and the Condition of the Animal
States the zakat schedule for cattle and discusses a condition dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the zakat schedule for cattle from 30 to 80 head, identify the terms tabi' and musinn, and explain the Hanafi disagreement on whether the zakat animal must be given alive or can be slaughtered.

Core Idea
Cattle zakat follows a fixed schedule per ten animals, but the requirement of a live animal is debated within the Hanafi school.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq provides the zakat schedule for cattle as stated in the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, and then expands on a scholarly difference: must the animal be handed over alive, or can it be slaughtered? Understanding this schedule and the ikhtilaf is crucial for correctly discharging zakat on cattle.

Guided Path
1
State the zakat schedule for each nisab level
For 30 cattle, pay a tabi' (one-year-old calf); for 40, a musinn (two-year-old); for 60, two tabi'an; for 70, a musinnah and a tabi'; for 80, two musinnatain. The pattern changes every ten.
The schedule is from the matn and is accepted as Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Understand the terminology of zakat categories
Tabi' is a male or female calf entering its second year; musinn is a male or female bovine entering its third year. These terms specify the age and type of animal to be given.
The commentator also explains the linguistic derivation of 'baqar' to clarify the genus.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the condition of the animal
Some Hanafi scholars suspend judgment (tawaqquf) due to lack of a clear text; others insist that the animal must be alive and that a slaughtered one only suffices by valuation (taqwim).
This ikhtilaf affects whether one can give a slaughtered animal without appraisal.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If the animal must be alive, then the payer cannot simply slaughter and give it; they must hand over the live animal. If valuation is allowed, a slaughtered animal can be accepted if its value equals the zakat due.
The mufta bihi is not explicitly stated here; a mufti would need to weigh the views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

In al-Mughrib: 'baqara' means he slit his belly, from the root طلب; and al-baqoor, al-bayqoor, al-abqoor, and al-baqar are the same. In al-Takmila from Qutrub: 'al-baqoorah' is the bovine. End. And 'baqar' is a genus, its singular is 'baqarah', whether male or female, like 'tamr' and 'tamrah', so the 'ta' is for singularity, not for femininity. In Diya' al-Huloom: 'al-baqir' is the group of cattle with their shepherds. His statement: (For thirty cattle, a tabi' of one year or a tabi'ah; for forty, a musinn of two years or a musinnah; and for what increases, by its calculation, up to sixty, then two tabi'an; at seventy, a musinnah and a tabi'; at eighty, two musinnatain. So the fard changes every ten from tabi' to the sheep or not?) And the answer was mentioned by some with suspension, that if there is no text on it; and by some with the definite condition that the slaughtered (animal) does not suffice except by way of valuation. He elaborated on it, so refer to it. Chapter of Zakat on Cattle. His statement: (And the answer is that when it was in the 'araq, it is not bovine...) He said in al-Nahr: There is consideration in it, and the better is to say:

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on zakat of cattle (baqar). The commentator first explains why this chapter comes before sheep: because cattle are closer to camels in size, and the term 'badanah' (sacrificial camel) also applies to cattle. He then gives linguistic derivations for the word 'baqar' (cattle). The passage ends abruptly.

مسن (musinn): A two-year-old bovine, used as a zakat category for cattle.
البدنة (al-badanah): A sacrificial animal, usually a camel, but here the term is said to include cattle due to size.

Zakat of Cows: Nisab, Proof, and the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on Increase Between 40 and 60
Commentary on matn with hadith proof and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab thresholds and obligatory dues for cows according to the Hanafi school, identify the hadith proof, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the zakat on the increase between 40 and 60 cows, including the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
For cows, the nisab starts at 30; the increase between 40 and 60 is disputed: proportional obligation or no obligation until 60.

In this lesson, we dive into the Hanafi rulings on cow zakat as presented in the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq and its commentary by al-Bahr al-Raiq. You will learn the specific thresholds and the animals due at each level, all grounded in the hadith of Mu'adh. The commentary then opens up an important intra-madhhab disagreement: how do we handle cows between 40 and 60? Two conflicting narrations from Abu Hanifa himself are recorded, and later scholars settled on one for fatwa. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply zakat correctly in complex cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisab thresholds and obligatory dues
From the matn, list the threshold numbers (30, 40, 60, 70, 80) and the corresponding animal due at each (tabi', musinn, etc.). Note that buffalo is treated identically to cows.
The pattern changes every ten cows from tabi' to musinn.
2
Locate the dalil and its role
The passage cites the hadith of Mu'adh as the primary evidence for the obligation and the specific rates. Identify this as an ahad hadith with zanni thubut and dalala.
The imperative 'أمر' indicates wujub (obligation) in Hanafi usul.
3
Isolate the point of ikhtilaf
The dispute centers on the phrase 'بحسابه' (proportionally) in the matn for the increase beyond 40. Two interpretations exist.
One reading requires proportional calculation; the other ignores the increase until the next full nisab at 60.
4
Trace the two narrations
Follow the text: the narration of Abu Yusuf (recorded in al-Mukhtasar) mandates proportional calculation. The narration of al-Hasan ibn Ziyad (the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, i.e., the Sahibayn) says no zakat is due until 60.
Both narrations are attributed to Abu Hanifa, creating an intra-madhhab dispute.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Despite the apparent narration being the proportional view in al-Mukhtasar, later authorities like al-Asbijabi and 'Allamah Qasim in his Tashih on al-Quduri declared the fatwa to be on the Sahibayn's view (no zakat on increase until 60).
This illustrates how later tarjih can differ from the zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صدقة البقر
قدمت على الغنم لقربها من الإبل في الضخامة حتى شملها اسم البدنة. وفي المغرب : بقر بطنه شقه من باب طلب والباقور والبيقور والأبقور والبقر سواء، وفي التكملة عن قطرب الباقورة البقر ا هـ والبقر جنس واحده بقرة ذكراً كان أو أثنى كالتمر والتمرة فالتاء للوحدة لا للتأنيث، وفي ضياء الحلوم : الباقر جماعة البقر مع رعائها قوله : (في ثلاثين بقراً تبيع ذو سنة أو تبيعة وفي أربعين مسن ذو سنتين أو مسنة وفيما زاد بحسابه إلى ستين ففيها تبيعان وفي سبعين مسنة وتبيع وفي ثمانين مسنتان فالفرض يتغير في كل عشر من تبيع إلى مسنة والجاموس كالبقر . تم
مسنة) بهذا أمر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم معاذاً حين بعثه إلى اليمن ولا خلاف فيما في المختصر إلا في قوله وفيما زاد على الأربعين فبحسابه ففيه روايات عن الإمام فما في المختصر رواية عن أبي يوسف عنه فيجب في الزائد إذا كان واحدة جزءاً من أربعين جزءاً من مسنة، وروى الحسن عنه أنه لا شيء في الزيادة إلى ستين وهو قولهما، وظاهر الرواية ما في المختصر كذا في غاية البيان لكن في المحيط رواية أسد أعدل الأقوال وفي جامع الفقه: قولهما هو المختار وذكر الأسبيجابي أن الفتوى على قولهما كما ذكره العلامة قاسم في تصحيحه على القدوري. وسمي الحولي من أولاد البقر بالتبيع لأنه أمه يتبع بعد. والمسن من البقر والشاء ما له سنتان، ومن الإبل ما دخل في السنة الثامنة. ثم لا يتعين الأنوثة في هذا الباب ولا في الغنم بخلاف الإبل لأنها لا تعد فضلاً فيهما بخلاف الإبل وفي المحيط معزياً إلى الزيادات : له أربعون من البقر عجافاً فعليه مسنة بقدرهن. ومعرفة ذلك أن ينظر إلى قيمة التبيع الوسط وقيمة المسنة الوسط، فإن كانت قيمة التبيع أربعين وقيمة المسنة خمسين تبين أن المسنة مثل تبيع وربع تبيع فعليه واحدة من أفضلهن وربع التي تليها، وإن كان قيمة أفضلهن ثلاثين وقيمة التي تليها عشرين فعليه مسنة قيمتها خمسة وثلاثون وعلى هذا تجري المسائل ا هـ
Chapter of Zakat of Cows: It is given precedence over sheep because of its similarity to camels in size, such that the term 'badanah' (sacrificial animal) includes it. In al-Mughrib: 'baqara' means to slit his belly from the chapter of 'talab', and 'baqur', 'biqur', 'abqur', and 'baqar' are equivalent. In al-Takmilah from Qutrub: 'al-baqurah' means cows. End. And 'baqar' is a genus, its singular is 'baqarah', whether male or female, like 'tamr' and 'tamrah'; the 'ta' is for singularity, not femininity. In Diya' al-Hulum: 'al-baqir' is a group of cows with their shepherds. His statement: (For thirty cows, a tabi' of one year or a tabi'ah; for forty, a musinn of two years or a musinnah; for what exceeds, proportionally until sixty, then two tabi's; for seventy, a musinnah and a tabi'; for eighty, two musinnahs; the obligation changes every ten from tabi' to musinnah, and the buffalo is like the cow. End. The musinnah) – with this the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) commanded Mu'adh when he sent him to Yemen. There is no disagreement in al-Mukhtasar except in his statement 'and for what exceeds forty, proportionally.' There are narrations from the Imam: what is in al-Mukhtasar is a narration from Abu Yusuf from him – so what is obligatory in the increase, if it is one part of forty parts of a musinnah. And al-Hasan narrated from him that there is nothing in the increase until sixty, and this is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The apparent narration is what is in al-Mukhtasar, as in Ghayat al-Bayan. But in al-Muhit, the narration of Asad is the most balanced of sayings. In Jami' al-Fiqh, the view of the two is the chosen one. And al-Asbijabi mentioned that the fatwa is on the view of the two, as mentioned by 'Allamah Qasim in his Tashih on al-Quduri. The one-year-old from the offspring of cows is called tabi' because it follows its mother. 'Musinn' from cows and sheep means two years old; from camels, one that has entered the eighth year. Then, femininity is not specified in this chapter nor in sheep, unlike camels, because there is no superiority (in counting) in them [؟]. In al-Muhit, citing al-Ziyadat: If one has forty thin cows, he owes a musinnah equivalent to them. The way to know that is to look at the value of an average tabi' and the value of an average musinnah. If the value of a tabi' is forty and the value of a musinnah is fifty, it becomes clear that the musinnah equals one and a quarter tabi'. So he owes one of the best of them and a quarter of the next. If the value of the best is thirty and the next is twenty, he owes a musinnah worth thirty-five. And on this pattern the cases proceed. End.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn on zakat of cows from Kanz al-Daqaiq. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq first justifies the order of chapters: the cow chapter is placed before sheep because cows are larger and closer to camels (even sharing the term 'badanah' for sacrificial animals). He then gives linguistic background on the word 'baqar'. The matn states the nisab and obligatory dues: at 30 cows, a tabi' (one-year-old male or female); at 40, a musinn (two-year-old); from 40 to 60, proportional calculation; at 60, two tabi's; at 70, one musinnah and one tabi'; at 80, two musinnahs; the obligation changes every ten between tabi' and musinnah. The matn ends by stating that buffalo is treated like a cow (to be covered in the next lesson). The commentary provides the proof: the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) commanded Mu'adh ibn Jabal with this when he sent him to Yemen. This hadith establishes the basic framework. Then comes a crucial intra-madhhab dispute: while al-Mukhtasar (by al-Quduri) states that for increases beyond 40, it is proportional (i.e., for every 40, one musinnah, so for 50, 1.25 musinnah etc.), there are differing narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa. One narration via Abu Yusuf (the basis of al-Mukhtasar) requires for each additional cow a proportional part of a musinnah. Another narration via al-Hasan ibn Ziyad holds that no additional zakat is due until the herd reaches 60 (i.e., the first increase is ignored). This is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn). The author states that the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) is what is in al-Mukhtasar (Abu Yusuf's narration), but many later scholars like Asad ibn al-Furat, the author of Jami' al-Fiqh, and al-Asbijabi consider the Sahibayn's view to be the chosen one (mukhtar) for fatwa. The commentary then defines 'tabi'' and 'musinn' and notes that unlike camels, gender is not specified—both male and female satisfy the obligation. Finally, a ruling for thin (emaciated) cows: if a person has 40 thin cows, they must pay a musinnah of equivalent value (not necessarily a specific animal). The method uses average values to determine the number of animals owed.

Key Terms
تبيع (tabi'): A one-year-old calf (male or female) that follows its mother.
مسن (musinn): A two-year-old cow or sheep; for camels, entering the eighth year.
بحسابه (bi-hisabihi): Proportionally, meaning for each additional cow a proportional fraction of the obligatory animal.
عجاف (ijaf): Thin, emaciated cows (as opposed to fat ones).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position regarding the zakat on the increase between 40 and 60 cows?
A) A proportional amount is due for every additional cow.
B) No zakat is due until the herd reaches 60 cows.
C) One extra musinnah is due.
D) Zakat is only due when the herd reaches 80.

Key Takeaway
Intra-madhhab differences matter: later Hanafi scholars settled on the Sahibayn's view that the increase between 40 and 60 cows is not subject to zakat.

Buffaloes Treated Like Cows: Zakat and Oath Rulings
Commentary on the matn clause 'wal-jawamis kal-baqar' with rulings on zakat and oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on buffaloes for zakat and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether an oath against cow includes buffalo, applying the role of custom ('urf).

Core Idea
Buffaloes are like cows for zakat but for oaths custom decides; the Hanafi ikhtilaf pivots on 'urf.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq unpacks the matn's claim that 'the buffalo is like the cow'. While the zakat ruling is straightforward—buffaloes complete the nisab and attract the same zakat rate—the oath implications reveal a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute. At stake is whether swearing not to eat cow meat also prohibits buffalo. The commentary navigates the dispute by prioritizing custom ('urf) over generic name, and also clarifies the mixing rule when herds contain both cows and buffaloes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Read the opening statement: the buffalo is like the cow because the name 'cow' encompasses it. This means for zakat, buffaloes complete the nisab of cows and zakat is obligatory on them at the same rate.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position from the early Hanafi masters.
2
Understand the mixing rule
When cows and buffaloes are mixed in a herd, zakat is taken from the majority type. If equal, take the higher of the lower value or the lower of the higher value—a fairness principle.
This rule applies to any mixed zakatable animals.
3
Locate the oath dispute
The matn's comparison raises a question: if someone swears not to eat cow meat, does eating buffalo break the oath? The text cites al-Hidaya saying no, because people's minds in that region do not immediately connect buffalo to cow due to its scarcity. Then it reports Qadikhan's Fatawa where some say yes (oath broken) and others say the opposite or no in both cases due to custom.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the core issue is the scope of the oath's subject.
4
Trace the arguments and role of 'urf
Al-Hidaya's view relies on custom ('urf): common understanding does not include buffalo. The opposing view relies on the generic name (ism jins). The passage then notes that al-Muhit supports the comparison for oaths (buying a cow includes buffalo), but the preferred view is that custom governs. The truth is in al-Hidaya and al-Tabyin.
Tarjih: 'urf overrides literal inclusion unless custom dictates otherwise.
5
Evaluate the critique of the matn's wording
The commentary criticizes the phrase 'like the cow' because it implies they are not the same. The better expression, from al-Walwaliji, is 'buffaloes are from the cow' (min al-baqar). Some resolve the issue by adding an implied word 'hukm' (ruling), but the preferred view is that they are a type of cow, not merely similar.
This linguistic precision avoids the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والجاموس كالبقر) لأن اسم البقر يتناوله إذ هو نوع منه فيكمل نصاب البقر به وتجب فيه زكاتها، وعند الاختلاط تؤخذ الزكاة من أغلبها إن كان بعضها أكثر من بعض، وإن لم يكن فيأخذ أعلى الأدنى وأدنى الأعلى ولا يرد عليه ما إذا حلف لا يأكل لحم البقر فأكله فإنه لا يحنث كما في الهداية، لأن أوهام الناس لا تسبق إليه في ديارنا لقلته. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان من فصل الأكل من الأيمان قال بعضهم : لو حلف لا يأكل لحم البقر فأكل لحم الجاموس حنث . ولو حلف أن لا يأكل لحم الجاموس فأكل لحم البقر لا يحنث وهذا أصح، وينبغي أن لا يحنث في الفصلين للعرف ا.هـ. فعلى هذا التصحيح كان التشبيه في قوله «كالجاموس» عاماً في الأيمان أيضاً ويوافقه ما في المحيط والجواميس بمنزلة البقر، ولهذا لو حلف لا يشتري بقراً فاشترى جاموساً يحنث بخلاف البقر الوحشي لأنه ملحق بخلاف الجنس كالحمار الوحشي وإن ألفت فيما بيننا لا يلتحق بالأهلي حكماً حتى يبقى حلال الأكل فكذا البقر الوحشي ا هـ . والحق ما في الهداية وفي التبيين. وقوله والجاموس كالبقر» ليس بجيد لأنه أنه ليس ببقر ا.هـ. وجوابه أنه لما كان في العرف ليس ببقر كان ذلك كافياً في التغاير المقتضي لصحة التشبيه وعبارة الولوالجي أحسن وهي : والجواميس من البقر لأنها نوع منه والله أعلم بالصواب وإليه المرجع والمآب.
يوهم :
إن في كلامه مضافاً محذوفاً أي وحكم الجاموس كالبقر فلا إشكال ا.هـ. وفيه نظر لأن كون حكمهما واحداً لا يدفع إيهام أنهما نوعان فالأولى ما ذكره المؤلف تأمل.
His statement: (And the buffalo is like the cow) because the name 'cow' encompasses it, as it is a type of it. So the nisab of cows is completed with it and zakat is obligatory on it. In case of mixing, zakat is taken from the majority if one type is more; if not, then take the higher of the lower and the lower of the higher. And it does not contradict the case where one swears not to eat cow meat and then eats buffalo—he does not break the oath, as in al-Hidaya, because people’s minds do not immediately connect to it in our lands due to its scarcity. In the Fatawa of Qadikhan, from the chapter of eating on oaths: some said: if one swears not to eat cow meat and eats buffalo, he breaks the oath. And if he swears not to eat buffalo and eats cow, he does not break the oath, and this is more correct. And it should be that he does not break the oath in both cases because of custom. End. On this correction, the comparison in his saying 'like the buffalo' is general also for oaths. And what is in al-Muhit agrees: buffaloes are like cows in status. For this reason, if one swears not to buy a cow and buys a buffalo, he breaks the oath, unlike wild cows because they are attached to a different genus, like the wild ass. Even if they are domesticated among us, they are not attached to the domesticated legally, so they remain halal to eat. Likewise wild cows. End. And the truth is what is in al-Hidaya and al-Tabyin. And his saying 'the buffalo is like the cow' is not good because it is not a cow. End. And its answer: since in custom it is not a cow, that is sufficient for the difference required for the validity of the comparison. And the expression of al-Walwaliji is better: 'buffaloes are from the cow because they are a type of it.' Allah knows best the truth, and to Him is the return and resort. It creates the impression that in his statement there is a deleted annex, i.e., 'the ruling of the buffalo is like the cow,' so there is no problem. End. But there is a consideration: that the ruling being the same does not repel the impression that they are two types. The better is what the author mentioned. Contemplate.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the matn clause 'wal-jawamis kal-baqar' (the buffalo is like the cow). The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq begins by affirming that buffaloes are a type of cow (baqar), completing the nisab and having zakat obligatory. When herds are mixed (cows and buffaloes together), zakat is taken from the majority; if equal, take the higher of the lower value or lower of the higher value (a fairness principle). Then comes a discussion on oaths: apparently, the matn's statement might be taken literally that buffalo is equivalent to cow in all rulings, but the author qualifies, citing al-Hidaya, that if someone swears not to eat cow meat and eats buffalo, he does not break the oath because in many regions (like the author's) buffalo is rare and not commonly called 'cow'. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute. Qadikhan's Fatawa reports that some say eating buffalo violates an oath against cow, but the more correct view is the opposite: swearing against cow does not encompass buffalo, but swearing against buffalo does encompass cow? Actually, the text says 'and this is more correct' referring to the second view (swearing against buffalo does not encompass cow). But then it says 'and it should be that he does not break the oath in both cases because of custom.' This is a third view based on 'urf (custom). The author then notes that if we accept the correction of the matn's comparison, it affects oaths generally. The ruling in al-Muhit supports that buffaloes are treated like cows, so buying a buffalo violates an oath not to buy a cow. However, wild cows (baqar wahshi) are not included because they are a different genus. The passage then points out a potential objection: the author's phrase 'wal-jawamis kal-baqar' (buffalo is like cow) could be criticized as it implies they are not actually cows. The answer given (attributed to al-Walwaliji) is that in custom ('urf) they are distinct, but that distinction does not preclude the legal comparison for rulings. The better expression is 'wal-jawamis min al-baqar' (buffaloes are from the cow genus). The commentary concludes by noting that some resolve the issue by implying a deleted word 'hukm' (the ruling of buffalo is like the ruling of cow), but this is not fully satisfactory. The author encourages reflection.

Key Terms
جاموس (jawamis): Buffalo, considered a type of cow (baqar) by Hanafi jurists for zakat purposes.
الاختلاط (al-ikhtilat): Mixing of two types (e.g., cows and buffaloes) in one herd for zakat.
اليمين (al-yamin): Oath; the commentary discusses how the legal comparison affects oath rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because buffalo is a type of cow.
B) No, because custom ('urf) does not consider buffalo as cow in that region.
C) It depends on the intention at the time of the oath.
D) The oath is invalid because deer is not specified.

Key Takeaway
Buffaloes are like cows for zakat, but for oaths custom decides; intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is resolved by preferring 'urf over generic name.

Zakat of Cattle: Nisab, Rates, and the Surplus Dispute
Explains zakat on cattle with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab for cattle, apply the Hanafi rates, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on surplus calculation.

Core Idea
Zakat on cattle is due at 30 (one tabi') and 40 (one musinnah); surplus between 40 and 60 is disputed.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the rulings of zakat on cattle. It details the nisab thresholds, defines the animals due, and addresses an important intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding how to handle cattle counts exceeding 40. Understanding this dispute is key to applying the correct fatwa in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisab thresholds
Find the main ruling: for every 30 cattle, one tabi'; for 40, one musinnah. Note that this is based on the Prophet's command to Mu'adh.
The hadith is the primary dalil.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Examine the text's discussion of the surplus clause: 'And for what exceeds forty, it is according to its calculation.' This triggers a difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
Abu Hanifa holds proportional calculation; Sahibayn require waiting until 60.
3
Analyze the tarjih (preference)
Note that although the zahir al-riwaya supports Abu Hanifa, later authorities (al-Asbijabi, 'Allamah Qasim) adopt the Sahibayn's view for fatwa.
This shows how later scholarship weighs practical ease.
4
Define key terms and extensions
Understand the definitions of tabi', musinnah, and the ruling on buffalo. Recognize that buffalo is included in 'baqr' for zakat.
Gender is not considered for cattle and sheep, unlike camels.
5
Apply to a numerical example
Work through the example: 50 cattle. Under Abu Hanifa: 1 musinnah + 1/4. Under Sahibayn: nothing until 60.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).

Book of Zakat, Chapter on Zakat of Cattle. It changes with every ten from a tabi' to a musinnah, and the buffalo is like cattle. (Musinnah:) With this the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم commanded Mu'adh when he sent him to Yemen. There is no disagreement in al-Mukhtasar except in his statement 'And for what exceeds forty, it is according to its calculation'; there are narrations from the Imam. The one in al-Mukhtasar is a narration from Abu Yusuf from him: for the excess, if it is one, it is a part of forty parts of a musinnah. Al-Hasan narrated from him that there is nothing for the increase up to sixty, and this is their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) statement. The apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) is what is in al-Mukhtasar, as in Ghayat al-Bayan, but in al-Muhit, the narration of Asad is the most balanced of the statements. In Jami' al-Fiqh: their statement is the chosen one. Al-Asbijabi mentioned that the fatwa is upon their statement, as mentioned by 'Allamah Qasim in his correction of al-Quduri. The one-year-old from the offspring of cattle is called tabi' because it follows its mother. Al-musinn from cattle and sheep is what has two years, and from camels what enters the eighth year. Then, femininity is not specified in this chapter nor in sheep, unlike camels, because they (cattle and sheep) do not reckon excess in them, unlike camels. In al-Muhit, citing al-Ziyadat: He has forty lean cattle; upon him is a musinnah equal to their value. The knowledge of that is to look at the value of the average tabi' and the value of the average musinnah; if the value of the tabi' is forty and the value of the musinnah is fifty, it becomes clear that the musinnah equals one tabi' and a quarter of a tabi', so he owes one of the best of them and a quarter of the next; and if the value of the best is thirty and the value of the next is twenty, he owes a musinnah worth thirty-five; and on this the cases proceed. End. His statement: (And the buffalo is like cattle) because the name 'baqr' encompasses both, as it is a type of it; thus the nisab of cattle is completed with it, and its zakat is obligatory. When they are mixed, zakat is taken from the majority if one kind is more; if not, the higher of the lower and the lower of the higher. And it is not refuted by the case of one who swears not to eat the meat of cattle (baqr) and then eats buffalo meat, for he does not break his oath, as in al-Hidayah, because people's minds do not reach it in our land due to its scarcity. In Fatawa Qadikhan from the chapter on eating from oaths: Some say: If one swears not to eat cattle meat and eats buffalo meat, he breaks his oath. But if he swears not to eat buffalo meat and eats cattle meat, he does not break his oath, and this is more correct. It is better that he does not break his oath in both cases due to custom. End. According to this correction, the simile in his statement 'like cattle' is general in oaths as well. It is supported by what is in al-Muhit: buffaloes are like cattle; thus if one swears not to buy cattle and buys a buffalo, he breaks his oath, unlike wild cattle because it is annexed to a different genus, like the wild donkey; even if it is accustomed among us, it is not annexed to the domestic one by law, so it remains halal to eat, thus also the wild cattle. End. The truth is what is in al-Hidayah and al-Tabyin. His statement 'the buffalo is like cattle' is not good because it is not cattle. End. The answer: Since in custom it is not cattle, that is sufficient for the difference necessitating the correctness of the simile. The expression of al-Walwaliji is better: 'Buffaloes are from cattle because they are a type of it.' And Allah knows best what is correct, and to Him is the return and the destination. It suggests: There is an omitted addendum in his speech, meaning the ruling of buffalo is like the ruling of cattle, so no problem. End. But there is consideration: That their ruling is one does not remove the implication that they are two types; the better is what the author mentioned. Consideration.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the chapter of zakat on cattle. It begins with the basic ruling that the zakat on cattle changes with every ten head: from a tabi' (one-year-old) to a musinnah (two-year-old). The proof is the hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal, whom the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم sent to Yemen with these instructions. The author then addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute: in al-Mukhtasar, it states that for cattle exceeding forty, the calculation is proportional. Imam Abu Hanifa's view (according to one narration) requires a fraction of a musinnah for any surplus over forty, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that no zakat is due on the increase until it reaches sixty. The zahir al-riwaya supports the view in al-Mukhtasar, but later authorities like al-Asbijabi and 'Allamah Qasim give fatwa on the Sahibayn's view. The definitions of tabi' (a one-year-old that follows its mother) and musinnah (two years old for cattle and sheep, eight years for camels) are clarified. Notably, gender is not considered for cattle and sheep, unlike camels. A detailed example shows how to calculate zakat when lean cattle are given: the average value of a tabi' and musinnah determines the obligation. The passage then discusses buffalo: since the term 'baqr' includes buffalo as a type, the nisab and zakat apply equally. A digression on oaths illustrates the legal effects: whether eating buffalo breaks an oath about cattle depends on custom (urf). The author critiques the statement 'buffalo is like cattle' because in custom people distinguish them, but concludes with al-Walwaliji's view that buffalo is a type of cattle. The final note suggests the author's wording may imply a difference despite same ruling.

Key Terms
تبيع (tabi'): A one-year-old calf that still follows its mother.
مسنة (musinnah): A two-year-old cow or sheep (or eight-year-old camel).
جاموس (jamus (buffalo)): Considered a type of cattle for zakat and oath rulings.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmission from Imam Muhammad in the six core books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One musinnah and one-quarter of a musinnah
B) One musinnah and nothing on the surplus
C) No zakat because the nisab is not complete
D) One tabi' and one musinnah

Key Takeaway
Zakat on cattle is wajib at 30 (tabi') and 40 (musinnah); the surplus over 40 is subject to intra-Hanafi dispute, but the mufta bihi (Sahibayn's view) imposes no further zakat until 60.

Nisab of Sheep and Goats in Zakat
Sets nisab thresholds and rules for mixed ownership and crossbreeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab thresholds for sheep and goats, explain the rule for mixed breeds, and apply the collector's duty regarding splitting or combining flocks.

Core Idea
Zakat on small livestock: 1 sheep per 40, but the flock's unity of ownership matters more than the collector's arithmetic.

This lesson covers the foundational nisab for sheep and goats, including how to count them, the rule for crossbreeds, and how ownership affects zakat collection. Understanding these thresholds ensures accurate calculation of zakat on flocks.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisab thresholds
The text lists specific numbers: 40, 121, 201, 400, then 1 per 100. Memorize these.
These thresholds are by consensus (ijma).
2
Understand the term 'shah'
The text clarifies that shah includes both male and female sheep; similarly goats are included under the same nomenclature.
Goats and sheep are one genus for nisab completion.
3
Apply the mother rule for crossbreeds
The offspring of a sheep-gazelle cross is treated according to the mother’s species for zakat.
If the mother is a sheep, zakat is due and the offspring completes the nisab.
4
Respect ownership unity
The collector cannot split a single flock to take more than owed, nor combine separate flocks to create a nisab.
Each owner’s liability is based on his own ownership.
5
Handle lean animals in payment
If the flock is lean, pay an average or best sheep; for multiple nisabs, take proportional middle value.
This ensures fair valuation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الغنم في أربعين شاة شاة وفي مائة وإحدى وعشرين شاتان وفي مائتين وواحدة ثلاث شياه وفي أربعمائة أربع شياه ثم في كل مائة شاة شاة بالإجماع وقدمنا أن الشاة تشمل الذكر والأنثى. وفي المحيط : والمتولد بين الغنم والظباء يعتبر فيه الأم، فإن كانت غنماً وجبت فيها الزكاة ويكمل به النصاب وإلا فلا. وفي الولوالجية : لو كان لرجل مائة وعشرون شاة حتى وجبت فيها شاة ليس للساعي أن يفرقها فيجعلها أربعين أربعين فيأخذ ثلاث شياه لأن باتحاد الملك صار الكل نصاباً، ولو كان بين رجلين أربعون شاة حتى لم يجب على كل واحد منهما الزكاة ليس للساعي أن يجمعها ويجعلها نصاباً ويأخذ الزكاة منها لأن ملك كل واحد منهما قاصر على النصاب ا هـ . وفي العجاف إن كانت شاة وسط تعينت وإلا واحدة من أفضلها، فإن كانت نصابين أو ثلاثة كمائة وإحدى وعشرين أو مائتين وواحدة وفيها عدد الواجب وسط تعينت أو قيمتها، وإن بعضه تعين هو وكمل من أفضلها بقية الواجب فتجب الواحدة الوسط واحدة أو اثنتان عجفا وأن يحسب ما يكون الواجب ،والموجود وتمامه في الزيادات قوله : (والمعز كالضأن لأن النص ورد باسم الشاة والغنم وهو شامل لهما فكانا جنساً واحداً. وفي فتح القدير والضأن والمعز سواء أي في تكميل النصاب لا في أداء الواجب ا هـ . وفي المعراج الضأن جمع ضائن كركب جمع راكب من ذوات الصوف والضأن اسم للذكر، والنعجة للأنثى، والمعزذات الشعر اسم للأنثى واسم الذكر التيس قوله : (ويؤخذ الثني في زكاته لا الجذع لقول علي رضي الله عنه : لا يجزئ في الزكاة إلا الثني فصاعداً. وأطلقه فشمل الضأن والمعز ولا خلاف أنه لا يؤخذ في المعز إلا الثني كما ذكره قاضيخان. واختلف في الضأن، فما في المختصر ظاهر الرواية ويقابله جواز الجذع وهو قولهما قياساً على الأضحية وهو ممتنع لأن جواز التضحية به عرف نصاً فلا يلحق به غيره والثني ما تم له سنة. واختلف في الجذع ففي الهداية أنه ما أتى عليه أكثرها، وذكر الناطفي أنه ماتم له ثمانية أشهر، وذكر هي فصل في الغنم قوله : (فإما أن تكون سائمة أو علوفة الأصوب حذفه لأنه أصل المقسم .
Section on sheep. For forty sheep, one sheep; for one hundred and twenty-one, two sheep; for two hundred and one, three sheep; for four hundred, four sheep; then for every hundred, one sheep, by consensus. We have already stated that 'shah' includes both male and female. In al-Muhit: The offspring between sheep and gazelle is considered based on the mother; if she is a sheep, zakat is obligatory and the nisab is completed with it; otherwise no. In al-Walwaljiyya: If a man had one hundred and twenty sheep such that one sheep became obligatory, it is not for the collector to divide them and make them forty each and take three sheep, because the single ownership makes the whole a nisab. And if between two men there are forty sheep such that zakat is not obligatory on each of them, it is not for the collector to combine them and make them a nisab and take zakat from them, because the ownership of each one is below the nisab. End. Regarding lean (thin) sheep: if there is an average sheep, it is determined; otherwise one of the best. If there are two or three nisabs like one hundred twenty-one or two hundred one, and among them the number of the obligatory average, it is determined or its value. If some is determined, it and the rest are completed from the best. So one average sheep is obligatory, or two lean ones, and it is calculated what the obligatory is and the existing is. Its completion is in al-Ziyadat. His statement: (And the goat is like the sheep) because the text came with the word 'shah' (sheep) and 'ghanam' (small livestock) which includes both, so they are one genus. In Fath al-Qadir: Sheep (ḍā'in) and goats (ma'z) are equal in completing the nisab, not in discharging the obligatory. End. In al-Mi'raj: Ḍā'in is the plural of ḍā'in like rakib is plural of raakib, they are wool-bearing animals; ḍā'in is the male and na'jah is the female. Ma'z (goats) are hair-bearing animals; the female is called ma'z and the male is called tays. His statement: (Only the thani is taken in its zakat, not the jadha') due to the saying of Ali, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Nothing is sufficient in zakat except the thani and above.' He gave it generally, so it includes both sheep and goats. There is no disagreement that nothing except thani is taken for goats, as Qadikhan mentioned. They differed regarding sheep: what is in al-Mukhtasar is the apparent narration, and it is opposed by the permissibility of jadha', which is their statement (the Sahibayn) by analogy on udhiyah (sacrificial animal). But this is prevented because the permissibility of sacrificing it is known by text, so others are not attached to it. The thani is what completed one year. They differed regarding jadha': in al-Hidayah it is what has passed most of a year? and al-Natafi mentioned that it is what completed eight months. And it is said: Section on sheep. His statement: (As for whether it is grazing or fodder-fed, the more correct is to delete it because it is the basis of the division).
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This section from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq covers the zakat of sheep and goats. It begins with the nisab thresholds by consensus: 40 sheep require 1 sheep, 121 require 2, 201 require 3, 400 require 4, and thereafter 1 per 100. The term 'shah' includes both genders. The author then addresses mixed livestock: the offspring of a sheep and a gazelle follows the mother; if the mother is a sheep, zakat applies. The collector cannot artificially split or combine flocks to alter zakat liability—single ownership makes the whole nisab, while separate ownership below nisab cannot be combined. The method of payment with lean animals is detailed: if an average animal exists, it suffices; otherwise the best, and for multiple nisabs, a proportional average. The ruling that goats (ma'z) are like sheep (ḍā'in) is based on the text covering both under 'ghanam'. However, in discharging zakat, each type must be given from its own kind. The age requirement: only a thani (one-year-old or more) is acceptable; jadha' (younger) is not, based on a hadith of Ali (RA). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding sheep: the Sahibayn analogize from sacrificial animals to permit jadha', but the author rejects this because the permission for sacrifice is specific to text. The passage concludes with a textual note by the author that the phrase 'either grazing or fodder-fed' should be omitted as it is the basis of the division.

Key Terms
شاة (shah): Sheep (includes both male and female).
ثني (thani): A sheep or goat that has completed one year of age.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many sheep are due for a flock of 121 sheep?
A) 1 sheep
B) 2 sheep
C) 3 sheep
D) 4 sheep

Key Takeaway
The nisab for sheep and goats is 40, 121, 201, 400, then 1 per 100, with unity of ownership being crucial.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Age Requirement for Zakat: Thani vs Jadha'
Sets the age requirement and addresses the intra-Hanafi dispute on jadha'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires thani (≥1 year) for zakat of sheep and goats, and evaluate the Sahibayn's analogy permitting jadha'.

Core Idea
Only thani is accepted for zakat sheep and goats; jadha' is rejected despite analogy with udhiyah.

This lesson focuses on a key age requirement for zakat: only animals that have completed one year (thani) are acceptable. The proof is a hadith of Ali (RA). The Sahibayn analogized from sacrifice animals, but the author of al-Bahr al-Ra’iq rejects this because the permission for jadha' in udhiyah is text-specific. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish textual rulings from analogical extension.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states: 'Only the thani is taken in its zakat, not the jadha'.'
Thani = one year old or more; jadha' = less than one year.
2
Examine the dalil
The hadith of Ali: 'Nothing is sufficient in zakat except the thani and above.' The phrase indicates exclusivity.
The hadith is ahad, so its thubut and dalala are zanni, but it is accepted.
3
Note the agreement on goats
There is no dispute that only thani is accepted for goats.
Qadikhan confirms this.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on sheep
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) analogize jadha' from udhiyah; the author rejects this because the udhiyah ruling is based on a specific text.
The muta’akhkhirun follow the thani-only view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that only thani is accepted for both sheep and goats.
This is the zahir al-riwayah and the fatwa.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Zakat on Sheep and Goats: Nisab, Rates, and the Thani Requirement
Ruling with proof on nisab and age requirement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab thresholds for sheep and goats in zakat, explain why the thani is required, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute over jadha'.

Core Idea
Zakat on grazing sheep/goats is due at 40, with payment of a yearling (thani), not a younger jadha'.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the Hanafi ruling on zakat for sheep and goats, detailing the nisab amounts and the required age of the animal paid. It also addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: whether a jadha' (six-month-old) sheep suffices, with Abu Hanifa insisting on thani based on a hadith, while the Sahibayn analogize to udhiya. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the nisab schedule, the definition of sa'ima, and the strength of textual evidence over analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisab thresholds
Memorize the progressive rates: 40 sheep → 1; 121 → 2; 201 → 3; 400 → 4; then 1 per hundred. Note that goats are treated identically.
The word 'shah' includes both male and female.
2
Clarify the scope of the genus
Understand why goats and sheep are one genus (ghanam) for nisab: the Arabic term ghanam encompasses both, as per the hadith.
In Fath al-Qadir: equal for completing nisab, not for the animal paid.
3
Locate the proof for the age requirement
The hadith of Ali (RA): 'لا يجزئ في الزكاة إلا الثني فصاعداً' (Nothing suffices in zakat except the thani and above). The negation negates sufficiency of jadha'.
This is a hadith ahad, zanni al-thubut, but relied upon for the wajib ruling.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad analogize to udhiya (sacrificial animal) where jadha' is allowed. The commentator rejects this because the udhiya permission is text-specific and cannot be extended via qiyas.
The thamarah al-khilaf: if a jadha' is given, Abu Hanifa says it is invalid; the Sahibayn say it suffices.
5
Define the technical terms
Thani for sheep = one year old; for goats = also one year. Jadha' for sheep = six months old (by most Hanafi jurists); for cattle and camels, different ages.
No disagreement that only thani is accepted for goats.

للأنثى، والمعزذات الشعر اسم للأنثى واسم الذكر التيس قوله : (ويؤخذ الثني في زكاته لا الجذع لقول علي رضي الله عنه : لا يجزئ في الزكاة إلا الثني فصاعداً. وأطلقه فشمل الضأن والمعز ولا خلاف أنه لا يؤخذ في المعز إلا الثني كما ذكره قاضيخان. واختلف في الضأن، فما في المختصر ظاهر الرواية ويقابله جواز الجذع وهو قولهما قياساً على الأضحية وهو ممتنع لأن جواز التضحية به عرف نصاً فلا يلحق به غيره والثني ما تم له سنة. واختلف في الجذع ففي الهداية أنه ما أتى عليه أكثرها، وذكر الناطفي أنه ماتم له ثمانية أشهر، وذكر الزعفراني أنه ما تم له سبعة أشهر وذكر الأقطع . قال الفقهاء: الجذع من الغنم ماله ستة أشهر ا هـ. وهو الظاهر وحاصله أن الجذع من الغنم عند الفقهاء ابن نصف سنة، ومن البقر ابن سنة، ومن الإبل ابن أربع سنين والثني عندهم ما تم له سنة من الغنم، ومن البقر ابن سنتين ومن الإبل ابن خمسة والمذكور في التبيين من كتاب الأضحية أن الثني من الضأن والمعز سواء وهو مأتم له سنة ولم أرسن الجذع من المعز عند الفقهاء وإنما نقلوه عن الأزهري أن الجذع من المعز ما تم له سنة .
قوله : (فإما أن تكون سائمة أو علوفة الأصوب حذفه لأنه أصل المقسم .
Chapter on sheep/goats. For forty sheep: one sheep; for one hundred and twenty-one: two sheep; for two hundred and one: three sheep; for four hundred: four sheep; then for every hundred: one sheep. And goats are like sheep. And the thani (yearling) is taken. It is called ghanam because it has no means of defense, so it is spoil for every seeker. His statement: (For forty sheep: one sheep...) by consensus, and we have stated that 'shah' includes male and female. In al-Muhit: For a hybrid between sheep and antelope, the mother is considered; if she is a sheep, zakat is due and it completes the nisab; otherwise not. In al-Walwaljiyya: If a man has one hundred and twenty sheep so that one sheep is due, the collector may not separate them into groups of forty and take three sheep, because by unity of ownership the whole becomes a nisab. And if two men have forty sheep such that neither owes zakat, the collector may not combine them to make a nisab and take zakat, because each one's ownership is deficient of nisab. End quote. And regarding thin animals: if there is a medium sheep, it is specified; otherwise one from the best. If there are two or three nisabs (like 121 or 201) and the number of the due is a medium, it is specified or its value. If part is specified, it is, and the remainder of the due is completed from the best, so one or two medium thin sheep are due. And that the due and the existing be calculated. Its completion is in al-Ziyadat. His statement: (And goats are like sheep) because the text came with the word 'shah' and 'ghanam', which includes both, so they are one species. In Fath al-Qadir: Sheep and goats are equal i.e. in completing the nisab, not in paying the due. End quote. In al-Mi'raj: ضأن is plural of ضائن, like ركب of راكب, from wool-bearing animals; ضأن is for the male, نعجة for the female; معز are hair-bearing, the name for the female, and the name for the male is تيس. His statement: (And the thani is taken in its zakat, not the jadha') due to the saying of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Nothing suffices in zakat except the thani and above.' He made it absolute, so it includes sheep and goats. There is no disagreement that only the thani is taken for goats, as Qadikhan mentioned. There is disagreement regarding sheep: what is in al-Mukhtar is the apparent narration, and opposed to it is permissibility of the jadha', which is their statement (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) by analogy with udhiya, and it is impermissible because the permissibility of sacrificing it is known by text, so others are not analogized to it. And thani is what has completed one year. There is disagreement about jadha': in al-Hidaya it is what most of its (year) has passed; al-Natafi said it is what has completed eight months; al-Za'farani said it is what has completed seven months; and al-Aqta' said. The jurists said: The jadha' from sheep is what has six months. End quote. And it is the apparent. Its summary: the jadha' from sheep according to the jurists is half a year old; from cattle one year; from camels four years. And thani according to them is what has completed one year from sheep, from cattle two years, from camels five years. And what is mentioned in al-Tabyin from the book of Udhiya is that thani from sheep and goats is the same, and it is what has completed one year, and I have not found jadha' from goats according to the jurists; rather they transmitted from al-Azhari that jadha' from goats is what has completed one year. His statement: (So it is either sa'ima or 'alufa) the correct view is to delete it because it is the basis of division.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the zakat of sheep and goats. The author (the commentator) first states the nisab thresholds from the matn: 40 sheep require 1, 121 require 2, 201 require 3, 400 require 4, then 1 per hundred. This is by consensus. The term 'shah' includes both male and female. Hybrids with antelope follow the mother: zakat is due only if the mother is a sheep. Joint ownership is treated as a single holding if ownership is unified; the collector cannot artificially split or combine herds to avoid or create zakat. If the herd consists of two or more nisabs (e.g. 121 or 201), the exact number due is a medium animal or its value. The commentator then explains that goats are like sheep for zakat because the Arabic word 'ghanam' includes both species; however, this applies only to completing the nisab, not to the specific animal paid. For the animal paid, only a thani (yearling) is accepted, not a jadha' (younger). This is based on the hadith of Ali (RA): 'Nothing suffices in zakat except the thani and above.' There is a dispute among the Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa (and the matn) insist on thani, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad analogize to udhiya (sacrificial animal) where a jadha' is allowed. The commentator rejects this qiyas because the permission for udhiya is text-based and cannot be extended. He then gives definitions of jadha' and thani for sheep, cattle, and camels. Finally, he remarks that the phrase in the matn 'either sa'ima or 'alufa' was correctly deleted because it is the basis of the entire division (i.e., the chapter's organization).

Key Terms
شاة (shāh): A single head of sheep or goat; includes both male and female for zakat purposes.
الْغَنَم (al-ghanam): Collective term for sheep and goats, treated as one genus for zakat nisab.
ثَنِيّ (thaniyy): For sheep: one year old; for goats: also one year old. Required for zakat payment.
جَذَع (jadha'): For sheep: six months old. Not sufficient for zakat according to Abu Hanifa.
سَائِمَة (sā'imah): Livestock that graze freely on natural pasture for most of the year. Basis for zakat on animals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith quoted in the passage, which animal suffices for zakat on sheep?
A) Any sheep between six months and one year.
B) Only a thani (yearling) or older.
C) Only a jadha' (six-month-old).
D) Only a female sheep.

Key Takeaway
The nisab for sheep/goats starts at 40, and the obligatory animal must be a thani (yearling), not a jadha', based on a hadith from Ali (RA).

Zakat — Almsgiving

No Zakat on Horses, Donkeys, and Mules Except for Trade
Ruling on zakat for equines with internal Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for horses, donkeys, and mules and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The relied-upon Hanafi position: no zakat on equines except when they are trade goods.

This lesson addresses a common misconception: that because horses are valuable, zakat must be due. However, the clear hadith and the majority Hanafi view state otherwise. We will examine the proof and the internal Hanafi dispute that led to the mufta bihi ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its source
State the ruling: no zakat on horses, donkeys, or mules unless they are trade goods. The matn explicitly says 'nothing on horses, donkeys, mules'.
2
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith from Bukhari: 'There is no sadaqah on a Muslim for his slave nor for his horse.' This explicitly negates obligation for horses. For donkeys and mules, the hadith says 'nothing has been sent down concerning them.'
The proof is an explicit text (nass) that takes precedence over analogy.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa held that under certain conditions (sa'ima, not for riding, with males and females), zakat might be due based on analogy with other livestock and the practice of Umar. The Sahibayn rejected this due to the explicit hadith.
The dispute is between the explicit text (Sahibayn) and qiyas (Abu Hanifa).
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Al-Khaniyya states the fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view: no zakat at all on horses, donkeys, and mules unless for trade. This is the relied-upon position for practice.
Even though later scholars like Shams al-A'imma favored Abu Hanifa, the simpler and safer view prevails in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا شيء في الخيل اختيار لقولهما لحديث البخاري مرفوعاً «ليس على المسلم في عبده ولا في فرسه صدقة ولا يرد عليه أن فيها زكاة التجارة إذا كانت لها اتفاقاً لأن كلامه في زكاة السوائم لا مطلق الزكاة، وأما عند أبي حنيفة فلا يخلو إما إن تكون سائمة أو علوفة، وكل منهما لا يخلو إما أن تكون للتجارة أو لا، فإن كانت للتجارة وجبت فيها زكاة التجارة سائمة كانت أو علوفة لأنها من العروض، وإن لم تكن للتجارة فلا يخلو إما أن تكون للحمل والركوب أو لا، فإن كانت للحمل والركوب فلا شيء فيها مطلقاً، وإن كانت لغيرهما فإما أن تكون سائمة أو علوفة، فإن كانت علوفة فلا شيء فيها، وإن كانت سائمة للدر والنسل فلا يخلو فإن كانت ذكوراً وإناثاً فلا يخلو، فإن كانت من أفراس العرب فصاحبها بالخيار إن شاء أعطى عن كل فرس ديناراً وإن شاء قومها وأعطى عن كل مائتين خمسة دراهم وهو مأثور عن عمر رضي الله عنه كما في الهداية. وإن لم تكن من أفراس العرب فإنها تقوم ويؤدي عن كل مائتين خمسة دراهم، والفرق أن أفراس العرب لا تتفاوت تفاوتاً فاحشاً بخلاف غيرها كما في الخانية. وإن كانت ذكوراً فقط أو إناثاً، فقط فعنه روايتان المشهور منهما عدم الوجوب، لأنها غير معدة للاستنماء لأن معنى النسل لا يحصل منها ومعنى السمن فيها غير معتبر لأنه غير مأكول اللحم. كذا في المحيط وصححه في البدائع. وفي التبيين: الأشبه أن تجب في الإناث لأنها تتناسل بالفحل المستعار ولا تجب في الذكور لعدم النماء. ورجح قوله شمس الأئمة وصاحب التحفة وتبعهما في فتح القدير وذكر في الخانية أن الفتوى على قولهما وأجمعوا أن الإمام لا يأخذ منهم صدقة الخيل جبراً ا هـ . واختلف المشايخ على قوله في اشتراط نصاب لها والصحيح أنه لا يشترط لعدم النقل بالتقدير قوله : (ولا في الحمير والبغال لقوله عليه السلام لم ينزل على فيهما شيء» والمقادير ثبتت سماعاً إلا أن تكون للتجارة لأن الزكاة حينئذ تتعلق بالمالية كسائر أموال التجارة .
(۱) رواه مسلم في كتاب الزكاة حديث .۹ أبو داود في كتاب الزكاة باب .۱۱. النسائي في كتاب الزكاة باب ١٦، ١٧. ابن ماجه في كتاب الزكاة باب ١٥. الموطأ في كتاب الزكاة حديث ٣٧. مسنده (٢/ ٢٤٩، ٢٧٩. أحمد في
His statement: (And nothing on horses) is a choice of their statement (the Sahibayn) due to the hadith of Bukhari raised: 'There is no sadaqah on a Muslim for his slave nor for his horse.' And it is not objected that there is zakat of trade on them when they are for trade by agreement, because his speech is about zakat on grazing animals, not absolute zakat. And according to Abu Hanifa, it is either sa'ima or 'alufa, and each of these is either for trade or not. If they are for trade, zakat of trade is due whether sa'ima or 'alufa because they are trade goods. If they are not for trade, they are either for riding/load or not. If for riding/load, nothing is due at all. If for other purposes, then either sa'ima or 'alufa. If 'alufa, nothing is due. If sa'ima, for milk and offspring, then if they are males and females, then if they are from Arab horses, the owner has a choice: if he wishes, he gives one dinar per horse; if he wishes, he values them and gives for every two hundred (dirhams) five dirhams. This is narrated from Umar (RA) as in al-Hidaya. If they are not from Arab horses, then they are valued and he pays for every two hundred five dirhams. The difference is that Arab horses do not vary extremely, unlike others, as in al-Khaniyya. If they are only males or only females, then from him (Abu Hanifa) there are two narrations, the more famous is non-obligation, because they are not prepared for growth, since the meaning of offspring is not obtained from them, and the meaning of fatness is not considered because their meat is not eaten. Thus in al-Muhit and he corrected it in al-Bada'i'. In al-Tabyin: it is more likely that it is due on females because they reproduce with a borrowed stallion, and not due on males due to lack of growth. Shams al-A'imma and the author of al-Tuhfa favored his (Abu Hanifa's) statement, and they followed him in Fath al-Qadir. It is mentioned in al-Khaniyya that the fatwa is on their statement (the Sahibayn), and they agreed that the ruler does not forcibly take sadaqah of horses. End quote. The scholars disagreed on his (Abu Hanifa's) condition of a nisab for them, and the correct is that it is not required due to lack of transmitted estimation. His statement: (And nothing on donkeys and mules) due to his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Nothing has been sent down to me concerning them.' And amounts are established by hearing, except if they are for trade, because zakat then pertains to financial value like other trade goods.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that there is no zakat on horses, donkeys, or mules unless they are trade goods. The commentator notes that the matn's statement 'nor on horses' represents the choice of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), based on the hadith of Bukhari that the Prophet said there is no sadaqah on a slave or a horse. However, this applies only to zakat on grazing animals; if horses are for trade, zakat al-tijarah is due by consensus. The commentator then details Abu Hanifa's more nuanced position: horses used for riding or load have no zakat; if they are for other purposes and are sa'ima (grazing), then for Arab horses the owner has an option to pay either a dinar per horse or to value them and pay 2.5% of the value (based on a practice of Umar). For non-Arab horses, only the valuation method applies because prices vary widely. For horses that are only males or only females, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa; the more famous is that no zakat is due because they cannot reproduce or increase in value through fattening. However, the Sahibayn hold that a breeding female herd can generate income via borrowed stallions, so zakat is due on females but not males. Many later scholars (Shams al-A'imma, author of al-Tuhfa, Fath al-Qadir) favor Abu Hanifa's more detailed view, but the actual fatwa (as stated in al-Khaniyya) is on the simpler view of the Sahibayn: no zakat on horses at all, and the ruler cannot force collection. There is also a question of nisab for horses; the correct view is no nisab required because no specific amount is transmitted. For donkeys and mules, the hadith explicitly states nothing was revealed, so no zakat except if they are for trade. This confirms the general principle: zakat is on grazing animals (camel, cattle, sheep/goats), not on equines or young livestock.

Key Terms
خَيْل (khayl): Horses; no zakat on them according to the relied-upon position, except for trade.
حِمَار (himār): Donkey; no zakat except for trade.
بَغْل (baghl): Mule; no zakat except for trade.
زَكَاة التِّجَارَة (zakāt al-tijārah): Zakat on trade goods, applicable to horses/donkeys/mules if bought and sold for profit.
أَفْرَاس الْعَرَب (afrās al-ʿarab): Arab horses (purebred), considered less variable in value; special optional payment rule from Umar (RA).
سائمة (sā'ima): Grazing livestock that feed on natural pasture for most of the year; subject to zakat for camels, cattle, sheep/goats, but not for horses.
علوفة (ʿalūfa): Stall-fed animals that do not graze freely; not subject to zakat on livestock even for zakatable animals, but trade zakat may apply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Zakat is due on all horses if they are sa'ima.
B) No zakat is due unless the horses are trade goods.
C) Zakat is due only on Arab horses.
D) Zakat is due only on female horses.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that no zakat is due on horses, donkeys, or mules unless they are trade goods, based on explicit hadith and the consensus of the Sahibayn.
