Zakat on Horses: Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Mufta Bihi
Expansion of a matn ruling via intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi on zakat of horses and explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, citing the primary proof.

Core Idea
The mufta bihi: no zakat on horses as sa'imah, following the Sahibayn and the hadith.

This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on zakat for horses kept as grazing livestock. While the matn states flatly 'nothing on horses', the commentary reveals an important intra-madhhab dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa had a more nuanced position. We will trace the evidence for the relied-upon view and understand the practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mufta bihi
Determine which position the author of the matn and later fatwa authorities adopted. Look for phrases like 'اختيار لقولهما' and 'الفتوى على قولهما'.
The mufta bihi is the view of the Sahibayn: no zakat at all on horses as sa'imah.
2
State the proof for the mufta bihi
Find the primary textual evidence cited for the Sahibayn's position. It is a marfu' hadith from Bukhari.
The hadith: 'ليس على المسلم في عبده ولا في فرسه صدقة'.
3
Outline Abu Hanifa's position
List the categories Abu Hanifa uses to differentiate when zakat applies. Note the conditions for trade, riding, breeding, and gender.
Abu Hanifa's view is detailed but not the fatwa.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference between the two positions. The key is whether horses for breeding (sa'imah) incur zakat.
Under Abu Hanifa, breeding horses may incur zakat; under Sahibayn, they do not.
5
Note the nisab dispute
The text briefly mentions a dispute among later scholars over whether a nisab is required. Identify the correct view.
No nisab is required because no specific amount was transmitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا شيء في الخيل اختيار لقولهما لحديث البخاري مرفوعاً «ليس على المسلم في عبده ولا في فرسه صدقة ولا يرد عليه أن فيها زكاة التجارة إذا كانت لها اتفاقاً لأن كلامه في زكاة السوائم لا مطلق الزكاة، وأما عند أبي حنيفة فلا يخلو إما إن تكون سائمة أو علوفة، وكل منهما لا يخلو إما أن تكون للتجارة أو لا، فإن كانت للتجارة وجبت فيها زكاة التجارة سائمة كانت أو علوفة لأنها من العروض، وإن لم تكن للتجارة فلا يخلو إما أن تكون للحمل والركوب أو لا، فإن كانت للحمل والركوب فلا شيء فيها مطلقاً، وإن كانت لغيرهما فإما أن تكون سائمة أو علوفة، فإن كانت علوفة فلا شيء فيها، وإن كانت سائمة للدر والنسل فلا يخلو فإن كانت ذكوراً وإناثاً فلا يخلو، فإن كانت من أفراس العرب فصاحبها بالخيار إن شاء أعطى عن كل فرس ديناراً وإن شاء قومها وأعطى عن كل مائتين خمسة دراهم وهو مأثور عن عمر رضي الله عنه كما في الهداية. وإن لم تكن من أفراس العرب فإنها تقوم ويؤدي عن كل مائتين خمسة دراهم، والفرق أن أفراس العرب لا تتفاوت تفاوتاً فاحشاً بخلاف غيرها كما في الخانية. وإن كانت ذكوراً فقط أو إناثاً، فقط فعنه روايتان المشهور منهما عدم الوجوب، لأنها غير معدة للاستنماء لأن معنى النسل لا يحصل منها ومعنى السمن فيها غير معتبر لأنه غير مأكول اللحم. كذا في المحيط وصححه في البدائع. وفي التبيين: الأشبه أن تجب في الإناث لأنها تتناسل بالفحل المستعار ولا تجب في الذكور لعدم النماء. ورجح قوله شمس الأئمة وصاحب التحفة وتبعهما في فتح القدير وذكر في الخانية أن الفتوى على قولهما وأجمعوا أن الإمام لا يأخذ منهم صدقة الخيل جبراً ا هـ . واختلف المشايخ على قوله في اشتراط نصاب لها والصحيح أنه لا يشترط لعدم النقل بالتقدير
His statement: (And nothing on horses) is a choice for the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) due to the hadith of Bukhari raised: 'There is no charity on a Muslim for his slave nor for his horse.' And it does not refute that there is zakat of trade if they are for trade by agreement, because his speech is about zakat of grazing livestock, not absolute zakat. As for according to Abu Hanifa, [the case] is not free from being either grazing or fodder-fed, and each of them is not free from being for trade or not. If they are for trade, zakat of trade is obligatory whether they are grazing or fodder-fed because they are trade goods. And if they are not for trade, they are not free from being for riding and transport or not. If they are for riding and transport, nothing is due absolutely. If they are for other than that, then either grazing or fodder-fed. If fodder-fed, nothing is due. If grazing for milk and offspring, then if they are males and females, if they are from Arab horses, their owner has a choice: if he wishes, he gives a dinar for every horse, and if he wishes, he values them and gives for every two hundred [dirhams] five dirhams, which is narrated from Umar (RA) as in al-Hidayah. If they are not from Arab horses, they are valued and he pays for every two hundred five dirhams. The difference is that Arab horses do not differ excessively unlike others, as in al-Khaniyyah. If they are only males or only females, then from him (Abu Hanifa) there are two narrations; the more famous of which is non-obligation, because they are not prepared for growth since the meaning of offspring is not obtained from them and the meaning of fattening is not considered because their meat is not eaten. Likewise in al-Muhit and confirmed in al-Bada'i. In al-Tabyin: the more similar is that it is obligatory on females because they reproduce by a borrowed stallion, and not obligatory on males due to lack of growth. Shams al-A'imma and the author of al-Tuhfah preferred his saying, and they were followed in Fath al-Qadir. It is mentioned in al-Khaniyyah that the fatwa is on the saying of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and they all agreed that the Imam does not take the charity of horses forcibly. And the scholars differed over his saying regarding the condition of a nisab for it, and the correct view is that it is not conditioned due to the lack of transmission of estimation.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding the matn ruling 'ولا شيء في الخيل' (nothing on horses). The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq explains that the matn's author (of Kanz al-Daqa'iq) chose the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) based on the hadith that there is no sadaqah on a Muslim for his slave or his horse. This hadith appears in Sahih al-Bukhari. The commentary then presents the detailed view of Imam Abu Hanifa, which is not the chosen position but is explained for completeness. According to Abu Hanifa, the ruling depends on the purpose of the horses: if they are for trade, zakat of trade applies by consensus; if for riding or transport, no zakat; if they are grazing for breeding, then for Arab horses the owner has an option (one dinar per horse or 2.5% of value based on Umar's practice), while non-Arab horses must be valued and 2.5% paid. If the horses are only males or only females, the majority narration from Abu Hanifa is that no zakat is due because they are not for growth. Later scholars differed on whether a nisab is required; the correct view is that no nisab is needed because no specific amount was transmitted.

Key Terms
سائمة (sa'imah): Livestock that graze freely for most of the year without being fed by the owner
علوفة (ma'lufah): Livestock that are fed by the owner, not left to graze freely
أفراس العرب (afras al-'arab): Purebred Arab horses known for their quality and minimal price variation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school regarding zakat on horses kept for breeding?
A) Zakat is due at 2.5% of value.
B) No zakat is due, following the hadith of the Prophet (PBUH).
C) Zakat is due with a choice between paying per head or by value.
D) Zakat is due only on female horses.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school: no zakat on horses as sa'imah, based on the hadith of the Prophet (PBUH) and the tarjih of the Sahibayn's view.

Zakat on Young Livestock: The Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat liability for young grazing livestock

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa holds no zakat on young livestock alone and evaluate Abu Yusuf's qiyas with emaciated animals.

Core Idea
Young livestock alone are not subject to zakat; texts specify ages and qiyas cannot override the nass.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: whether zakat is due on young grazing livestock (lambs, weaned camel calves, calves) when they are owned alone without any adult animals. The matn states no zakat, but Abu Yusuf and Zufar dissent. Understanding the reasoning reveals the Hanafi methodology of prioritizing explicit texts (nusus) over qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the matn
The matn states that no zakat is due on lambs, weaned camel calves, and young cows. Recognize that this is the statement of the author (al-Quduri) being commented upon.
This is the base ruling that the commentator expands.
2
Distinguish the three positions
Note: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say no zakat. Abu Yusuf says one sheep is due. Zufar says full adult zakat is due. Each uses different reasoning.
Abu Yusuf's view is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; Zufar is a separate Hanafi scholar.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's qiyas with emaciated animals
Abu Yusuf analogizes young animals (sighar) to emaciated animals (mahazil): both have a deficiency (nuqsan). In mahazil, deficiency reduces the obligation but does not drop it; similarly, young age should reduce rather than drop.
The illa is 'deficiency', but Abu Hanifa rejects this illa as inappropriate.
4
Examine Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa argues that the texts (nusus) specify exact ages for zakat (e.g., jadha'a, thaniyya). Young animals do not meet those ages. Qiyas has no entry where nass is explicit.
This illustrates the principle: al-nass muqaddam 'ala al-qiyas (text overrides analogy).
5
Apply the ruling to mixed herds and note the mufta bihi
When adults are present, zakat is due by consensus. When alone, the relied-upon position is no zakat (Abu Hanifa). Understand the practical implications.
The mufta bihi protects owners from overpaying zakat on non-nisab animals.

أخذت وإن كانت جيدة لو تؤخذ ويؤدي صاحب المال شاة وسطاً، وإن كانت دون الوسط لم يجب إلا هذه، فإن هلكت الكبيرة بعد الحول بطل الواجب كله عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد لأن الصغار كانت تبعاً للكبار عندهما، وعند أبي His statement: (and not on lambs, weaned camel calves, and young cows). 'Lambs' (al-himlan) with damma on the ha, and in al-Diwan Ibn... with kasra, plural of hamal with two fatha, meaning sheep offspring. 'Weaned camel calves' (al-fislan) plural of fasil, offspring of a she-camel before becoming a pregnant camel. 'Young cows' (al-'ajajil) plural of 'ajul meaning calf, offspring of a cow. The non-obligation of zakat on young of grazing livestock is the position of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: one [shah] is obligatory from them. In al-Muhit: They discussed the form of the issue, for it is problematic because zakat is not obligatory without the passing of a year, and after the year they are no longer young. It was said: its form is that the year commences on these young ones, such that he owned them at the beginning of the year and then the year passed over them; is zakat obligatory in them even if they are no longer young? And it was said: its form is when they have mothers, and six months pass, and they give birth to offspring, then the mothers die and the offspring remain, then the year passes over them while they are young; is zakat obligatory in them or not? And the sounder [view] according to Abu Yusuf is that if we made obligatory in them what is obligatory in full-grown animals, as Zufar said, we would be harsh on the owners of wealth; and if we made obligatory a sheep in them, we would harm the poor; so we made one [sheep] obligatory, by analogy with emaciated animals, for the deficiency in description, when it affected the lightening of the obligatory, not its dropping, so likewise in dropping the age. And the correct [view] is the statement of Abu Hanifa, because the text made obligatory for zakat specific ages, and there is no room for analogy in that, and it is absent in young ones. End. In Mi'raj al-Diraya: It is conceived in the case when he has twenty-five camels. He said: It was not conceived at five because Abu Yusuf made one obligatory from them, and that cannot be conceived in less than twenty-five. And this difference is when there is no adult with the young ones. But if there is, then it is obligatory by consensus, such that if there is a one-year-old with thirty-nine lambs, it is obligatory and the one-year-old is taken, and similarly in camels and cows. End. In Ghayat al-Bayan, attributed to al-Ziyadat: A man has thirty-nine [lambs] and one one-year-old ewe. If the one-year-old is average, it is taken; if it is good, it is not taken and the owner pays an average sheep; and if it is below average, nothing is obligatory except this. If the adult dies after the year, all the obligation becomes void according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, because the young were followers of the adults in their view. According to Abu Yusuf, on the remaining there is thirty-nine fortieths of a lamb, for the excess over the lamb was only obligatory due to the adult, so it becomes void by its death. And if all die except the adult, then it contains a fortieth of a one-year-old sheep. Similarly, a man has twenty-four weaned camel calves and a one-year-old she-camel fat or average. And similarly twenty-nine young cows and in them a one-year-old or a two-year-old. Then the principle that is considered in the case of mixing young and adult is that the number obligatory in adults exists, such as if he has two one-year-olds and one hundred nineteen lambs, then two one-year-olds are obligatory in their two's view. As for if he has one one-year-old and one hundred twenty lambs, one one-year-old is obligatory according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and according to Abu Yusuf, one one-year-old and a lamb are obligatory. Similarly his statement: (and it is the most correct) said in al-Nahr: perhaps its face is that according to the first conception, there remains no room for dispute where the obligatory exists, which is the yearling, as pointed out in al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyya. Page 381: Book of Zakat, Section 381: fifty-nine young cows and a two-year-old, where the two-year-old is taken only according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] because there is nothing that suffices for obligation other than it. Abu Yusuf said: the two-year-old and a calf are taken with it, and its completion is in Sharh al-Ziyadat of Qadi Khan.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether zakat is due on young grazing livestock when they are separate from adults. The matn states that zakat is not due on lambs, weaned camel calves, and young cows. The commentator explains that this non-obligation is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two disciples). However, Abu Yusuf himself is reported to have said that one sheep is due from them. The commentator from al-Muhit notes that the issue is problematic because zakat requires a full lunar year, and after the year the animals are no longer young. Two possible scenarios are presented: (1) the owner owned young animals at the beginning of the year and they remained young at the end? Actually the year passes and they become older, so the dispute is whether zakat is due on them at the end of the year if they were young at the start. (2) The second scenario involves mothers giving birth, then the mothers die, and the offspring remain and complete the year while still young. Abu Yusuf's view is that one sheep is due, drawing an analogy with emaciated animals: just as deficiency in condition reduces the obligation but does not eliminate it, deficiency in age should similarly reduce the obligation. Zufar's view is mentioned as requiring full adult zakat, which is rejected as harsh. Abu Hanifa's position is that the texts specify particular ages for zakat, and analogy has no entry; since young animals do not meet those ages, no zakat is due. The correct position according to the commentator is that of Abu Hanifa. The passage then provides detailed examples from al-Ziyadat illustrating the effect of mixing young and adult, and the consequences if the adult dies after the year. The key principle is that when young are mixed with adults, the adults alone determine the zakat; the young are followers. Abu Yusuf differs in some cases, requiring a proportional obligation from the young. The passage ends with the note that the dispute applies only when there is no adult; with an adult present, zakat is due by consensus.

Key Terms
الصغار (al-sighar): Young livestock that have not reached the age for zakat (e.g., lambs under one year, camel calves under one year, calves under one year).
السوائم (al-sawa'im): Grazing livestock that are allowed to pasture freely for most of the year without being fed fodder.
المهازيل (al-mahazil): Emaciated animals that are weak or thin due to lack of fodder or illness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, what is the basis for obligating one sheep from young livestock?
A) Analogy with emaciated animals
B) Consensus of the companions
C) A clear Quranic verse
D) A hadith from the Prophet

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that young livestock alone are not subject to zakat because the texts specify ages, and analogy cannot extend the obligation.

Zakat on Fodder-Fed and Working Animals: The Hanafi Exemption
Ruling on ma'lufah and 'awamil exemption from livestock zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for fodder-fed and working animals and identify the hadith and rationale for the exemption.

Core Idea
Fodder-fed and working animals are exempt from livestock zakat; only grazing animals are zakatable.

Many assume all livestock are subject to zakat, but the Hanafi school draws a crucial distinction. This lesson clarifies that only grazing animals (sa'imah) incur livestock zakat, while animals fed on fodder (ma'lufah) or used for work ('awamil) are exempt unless held for trade. The ruling is based on a hadith and the principle that zakat requires growth (nama'), which is absent in animals with ongoing expenses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that no zakat is due on ma'lufah (fodder-fed) and 'awamil (working) animals as sa'imah.
Note: The exemption is only from livestock zakat; trade zakat may apply if held for sale.
2
Locate the proof
The author cites a hadith: 'There is no sadaqah on pregnant, working, and fodder-fed animals.'
This is an ahad hadith, but it suffices to negate obligation in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the rationale
The cause (sabab) for livestock zakat is wealthy that grows (mal namy). Growth is evidenced by free grazing (sa'imah) or preparation for trade. Ma'lufah animals have expenses that negate true growth.
The passage also mentions that working animals are exempt even if they sometimes graze, because their primary purpose is labor.
4
Apply the exception for trade
If the animals are held for trade, zakat al-tijarah applies. The exemption only applies to livestock zakat, not trade zakat.
The phrase 'والمراد بنفي الزكاة عن العلوفة زكاة السائمة' clarifies this limitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا) في العلوفة والعوامل) للحديث «ليس في الحوامل والعوامل والعلوفة صدقة» ولأن السبب هو المال النامي ودليله الأسامة أو الأعداد للتجارة ولم يوجدا، ولأن في العلوفة تتراكم المؤنة فينعدم النماء معنى والمراد بنفي الزكاة عن العلوفة زكاة السائمة لأنها لو كانت للتجارة وجبت فيها زكاة التجارة والمراد بنفيها عن العوامل التعميم. والعلوفة بفتح العين ما يعلف من الغنم وغيرها الواحد والجمع سواء، والعُلوفة بالضم جمع علف يقال علفت الدابة ولا يقال أعلقتها والدابة معلوفة وعليف كذا في غاية البيان. وقدمنا عن القنية أنه لو كان له إبل عوامل يعمل بها في السنة أربعة أشهر ويسمنها في الباقي ينبغي أن لا تجب فيها الزكاة .
His statement: (and not on fodder-fed and working animals) due to the hadith: 'There is no sadaqah on pregnant, working, and fodder-fed animals.' And because the cause is wealth that grows, and its evidence is pasturing or preparation for trade, and these two are not found. And because in fodder-fed animals, expenses accumulate, so growth is nonexistent in meaning. And what is meant by negating zakat on fodder-fed animals is the zakat of grazing animals, because if they were for trade, the zakat of trade would be obligatory on them. And what is meant by negating it on working animals is general negation. And al-'ulufah with fatha on the 'ayn is what is fed to sheep and others, the singular and plural are the same. And al-'ulufah with damma is the plural of 'alaf. It is said: 'alaftu al-dabbata (I fed the animal) and 'alaqtuha is not said; the animal is ma'lufah and 'alif. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. And we have previously mentioned from al-Qunyah that if he has working camels that work for four months in the year and he fattens them for the rest, it is appropriate that zakat is not obligatory on them.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling that no zakat is due on 'al-ulufah' (animals fed on fodder rather than pastured) and 'al-'awamil' (working animals used for plowing, transport, etc.). The proof is a hadith: 'There is no sadaqah on pregnant, working, and fodder-fed animals.' The commentator explains the rationale: the cause of zakat on livestock is growth (nama'), which is evidenced by free grazing (sa'imah) or being prepared for trade. Fodder-fed animals have ongoing expenses that negate real growth. Importantly, this exemption applies only to the zakat of sa'imah; if the animal is held for trade, then zakat al-tijarah (trade zakat) applies. The working animals are generally exempt even if they are also grazed sometimes, because the purpose is work. The commentator also notes a linguistic point: 'al-ulufah' with fatha is a singular/plural noun meaning fodder-fed animals, while 'al-'ulufah' with damma is plural of 'alaf (fodder). A ruling from al-Qunyah is cited: if working camels work for part of the year and are fattened for the rest, it is still appropriate that no zakat is due on them as sa'imah.

Key Terms
العلوفة (al-'ulufah): Animals that are fed on fodder (grain, hay, etc.) rather than grazed on pasture. They are not subject to zakat as sa'imah.
العوامل (al-'awamil): Working animals used for plowing, carrying loads, etc. They are exempt from zakat as sa'imah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A farmer owns oxen that he uses to plow his fields and feeds them hay in a barn. Are these oxen subject to zakat as sa'imah?
A) Yes, because they are animals.
B) No, because they are working animals ('awamil) and also fodder-fed (ma'lufah).
C) Yes, because they are used for agriculture.
D) No, but only if the owner has less than 5 oxen.

Key Takeaway
Fodder-fed and working animals are not subject to livestock zakat because they lack the growth characteristic of sa'imah; trade zakat applies if held for commerce.

Zakat on 'Afw: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Surplus Livestock and Post-Year Losses
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat on surplus livestock and allocation of post-year losses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi concept of 'afw, distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad/Zufar regarding zakat on surplus livestock, and apply the ruling on attributing post-year losses to determine zakat obligation.

Core Idea
No zakat on 'afw (surplus between nisabs) is the relied-upon Hanafi view; post-year losses are attributed to the 'afw first, protecting the nisab obligation.

This passage addresses a crucial intra-Hanafi dispute: whether the surplus animals between two zakat thresholds (al-'afw) are themselves subject to zakat. While the majority hold that only the nisab itself triggers zakat, Muhammad and Zufar argue that the surplus should also be zakatable. The practical consequence emerges when some livestock perish after the year: does the zakat obligation reduce proportionally, or is the loss allocated to the 'afw first, leaving the nisab obligation intact? The passage lays out the positions, the method of attributing losses, and detailed examples that clarify how each view plays out in real calculations.

Guided Path
1
Define 'afw linguistically and technically
Identify the lexical meanings of 'afw (best of wealth, surplus, etc.) and its technical legal definition as the amount of livestock between two established nisabs (e.g., 4 camels between 5 and 9). Understand that this surplus is not a nisab itself.
Pay attention to the example: 9 camels = nisab of 5 + 4 'afw.
2
State the two positions on zakat on 'afw
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: no zakat on 'afw; zakat is only on the nisab. Muhammad and Zufar: zakat is due on both the nisab and the 'afw. This is the core dispute.
The passage notes that the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.
3
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
When animals die after the completion of the year, how does the obligation change? Under the first view, loss is attributed to the 'afw first, so if the nisab remains intact, the zakat remains unchanged. Under the second view, loss reduces the total obligation proportionally.
Example: 9 camels, loss of 4 → one view says full zakat remains, the other says 4/9ths of a sheep drops.
4
Analyze the method of attributing losses
Imam Abu Hanifa attributes loss first to the last (highest) nisab, then to the previous ones, because the first nisab is the basis. Abu Yusuf (in a weak narration) attributes loss to the 'afw first, then to the nisabs proportionally. The correct narration from Abu Yusuf agrees with Abu Hanifa.
The passage in al-Muhit declares the contrary narration from Abu Yusuf as weak.
5
Apply to given examples
Work through the numerical examples: 9 camels losing 4, 120 sheep losing 80, 121 sheep losing 81, 40 camels losing 20, 25 camels losing 10. Compute the zakat due under each view and see how the attribution method produces different results.
For 121 sheep, the calculation involves fractions (41/121 of 2 sheep under the opposing view).

Source Text

قوله : (ولا في العفو) أي لا زكاة في العفو وهو لغة مشترك بين أفضل المال وأفضل المرعى، والمعروف والإعطاء من غير مسألة والفاضل عن النفقة والمكان الذي لم يوطأ، والصفح والإعراض عن عقوبة المذنب. وشرعاً ما بين النصب كالأربعة الزائدة على الخمسة من الإبل إلى العشر، وكالعشرة الزائدة على خمس وعشرين من الإبل، فعند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف الزكاة في النصاب لا في العفو، وعند محمد وزفر فيهما حتى لو هلك العفو وبقي النصاب يبقى كل الواجب عند الأولين ويسقط بقدره عند الأخرين، فلو كان له تسع من الإبل أو مائة وعشرون من الغنم فهلك بعد الحول من الإبل أربعة ومن الغنم ثمانون لم يسقط شيء من الزكاة عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، وعند محمد وزفر يسقط في الأول أربعة أتساع شاة وفي الثانية ثلثا شاة. وفي الهداية وغيرها: إن الهلاك يصرف بعد العفو إلى النصاب الأخير ثم إلى الذي يليه إلى أن ينتهي عند الإمام لأن الأصل هو النصاب الأول وما زاد عليه تابع، وعند أبي يوسف يصرف إلى العفو أولاً ثم إلى النصب شائعاً. وفي المحيط : إن هذه رواية ضعيفة عن أبي يوسف وظاهر الرواية عنه كقول إمامه وتظهر فائدته فيما إذا كان له مائة وإحدى وعشرون شاة فهلك إحدى وثمانون بقي من الواجب شاة عند الإمام، وعند الثلاثة يجب أربعون جزءاً . مائة وإحدى وعشرين جزءاً من شاتين. ولو هلك شاة فقط من بقي من الواجب شاة عنده، وعند الثلاثة يسقط جزء واحد من مائة وإحدى وعشرين جزءاً من شاتين ويبقى الباقي، وإذا كان له أربعون من الإبل فهلك نصفها بعد الحول فعند الإمام الواجب أربع شياه، وعند أبي يوسف عشرون جزءاً من ستة وثلاثين جزءاً من بنت اللبون، وعند محمد نصف بنت لبون. ولو هلك عشرة من خمس وعشرين فعنده الواجب ثلاث شياه، وعند الثلاثة ثلاثة أخماس بنت المخاض. وفي غاية البيان. ينبغي لك أن تعلم أن العفو
His statement: (and not on al-'afw) meaning no zakat on al-'afw. Lexically, it is shared between the best of wealth, the best of pasture, charity, giving without being asked, the surplus beyond living expenses, the place not trodden, and turning away from punishing the guilty. Legally, it is what is between the nisabs, such as the four [camels] exceeding the five up to ten, and the ten exceeding the twenty-five up to [the next nisab]. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, zakat is on the nisab, not on the 'afw. According to Muhammad and Zufar, it is on both, such that if the 'afw is lost and the nisab remains, the entire obligation remains according to the former two, and drops proportionally according to the latter two. So if a man has nine camels or one hundred twenty sheep, and after the year four camels or eighty sheep die, nothing of the zakat drops according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; according to Muhammad and Zufar, in the first case four-ninths of a sheep drops, in the second two-thirds of a sheep drops. In al-Hidayah and others: Loss (halaak) is attributed after the 'afw to the last nisab, then to the one before it, until it ends, according to the Imam, because the basis is the first nisab and what is beyond it is subordinate. According to Abu Yusuf, it is attributed to the 'afw first, then to the nisabs in a proportional manner. In al-Muhit: This is a weak narration from Abu Yusuf; the apparent narration from him is like the statement of his Imam. Its benefit appears in the case where he has one hundred twenty-one sheep and eighty-one die: one sheep remains of the obligation according to the Imam; according to the three, forty one hundred-twenty-first parts of two sheep are obligatory. And if only one sheep dies, one sheep remains of the obligation according to him; according to the three, one part of one hundred twenty-one parts of two sheep drops and the rest remains. And if he has forty camels and half die after the year, according to the Imam the obligation is four sheep; according to Abu Yusuf, twenty parts of thirty-six parts of a bint labun; according to Muhammad, half a bint labun. And if ten die out of twenty-five, according to him the obligation is three sheep; according to the three, three-fifths of a bint makhad. And in Ghayat al-Bayan: You should know that al-'afw...
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage discusses the concept of 'afw, which refers to the surplus amount of livestock between two nisabs that does not trigger additional zakat. The legal definition is the quantity between established thresholds, e.g., the four camels between five and ten (since the nisab for camels starts at five, then jumps to ten without a specific zakat for six, seven, eight, nine). The dispute is whether zakat is due on these intermediate animals. The relied-upon position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is that zakat is only on the nisab itself, not on the 'afw. Muhammad and Zufar hold that zakat is due on both the nisab and the 'afw. The practical consequence appears when some animals are lost after the completion of the year. For example, if someone has 9 camels (nisab of 5+4 'afw) and 4 camels die after the year, according to Abu Hanifa, the full zakat (one sheep) remains due because the loss is attributed to the 'afw first, which does not affect the nisab obligation. But according to Muhammad, since the 'afw is also zakatable, the loss reduces the total obligation proportionally (four-ninths of a sheep drops). The passage explains the methodology of attributing losses: Imam Abu Hanifa attributes loss first to the furthest nisab (the highest number), then to the previous, because the first nisab is the basis. Abu Yusuf (according to a weak riwaya) attributes loss first to the 'afw, then to the nisabs proportionally. The correct narration from Abu Yusuf aligns with Abu Hanifa. Detailed examples for camels and sheep are provided to illustrate the positions.

Key Terms
العفو (al-'afw): The surplus amount of livestock between two nisabs that is not subject to zakat according to the relied-upon position, e.g., the 4 camels between 5 and 9.
الهلاك بعد الوجوب (al-halāk ba‘d al-wujūb): The situation where livestock (or part of them) die after the obligation of zakat has become due (i.e., after the completion of the lunar year).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Zaid owns 9 camels (nisab of 5 with 4 as 'afw). After the year, 2 camels die. What is the zakat due according to Abu Hanifa?
A) One sheep remains due.
B) The zakat reduces proportionally (7/9 sheep).
C) No zakat is due because the nisab is no longer intact.
D) Two sheep are due.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the surplus between nisabs (al-'afw) is exempt from zakat, and post-year losses are charged against the 'afw first, preserving the obligation on the nisab.

The Zakat Exemption for ʿUlūfah and ʿAwāmil
Ruling with proof and explanation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that zakat is not due on fodder-fed and work animals, cite the primary hadith proof, and explain the rationale of lacking natural growth.

Core Idea
Fodder-fed and work animals are exempt from zakat because they do not naturally grow.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies an important exception to the general rule of zakat on livestock. While grazing animals (sa'imah) are subject to zakat, those that are fed by hand or used for labor are exempt. The proof is a prophetic hadith and a rational cause: the high costs of maintenance prevent the natural increase that triggers zakat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two exempt categories
Note the terms 'ulufah (fodder-fed) and 'awamil (work animals). Understand that these are separate from sa'imah (free-grazing).
The exemption is specific to non-trade animals.
2
Analyze the hadith proof
Examine the hadith 'There is no charity on pregnant, work, and fodder-fed animals.' Recognize that this is a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in practice.
The hadith explicitly negates zakat, making the ruling clear.
3
Understand the 'illah (cause)
The passage gives a rational cause: fodder-fed animals incur high feeding costs, so their wealth does not grow naturally. Work animals are also not growing. Zakat is linked to growing wealth (mal nami).
The cause is the absence of natural increase.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا) في العلوفة والعوامل) للحديث ليس في الحوامل والعوامل والعلوفة صدقة ولأن السبب هو المال النامي ودليله الأسامة [؟] أو الأعداد للتجارة ولم يوجدا، ولأن في العلوفة تتراكم المؤنة فينعدم النماء معنى والمراد بنفي الزكاة عن العلوفة زكاة السائمة لأنها لو كانت للتجارة وجبت فيها زكاة التجارة والمراد بنفيها عن العوامل التعميم. والعلوفة بفتح العين ما يعلف من الغنم وغيرها الواحد والجمع سواء، والعُلوفة بالضم جمع علف يقال علفت الدابة ولا يقال أعلقتها والدابة معلوفة وعليف كذا في غاية البيان. وقدمنا عن القنية أنه لو كان له إبل عوامل يعمل بها في السنة أربعة أشهر ويسمنها في الباقي ينبغي أن لا تجب فيها الزكاة.
His saying: (And not) regarding fodder-fed and work animals: due to the hadith 'There is no charity on pregnant, work, and fodder-fed animals.' And because the cause is the growing wealth, and its proof is the basis [؟] or being prepared for trade, and they are not found. And because in fodder-fed animals the cost accumulates so growth is absent in meaning. The intended meaning of negating zakat on fodder-fed animals is the zakat of grazing animals, because if they were for trade the zakat of trade would be obligatory. And the intended meaning of negating it on work animals is general. Al-‘ulūfah (with fatha on ‘ayn) is what is fed from sheep and others, singular and plural the same; al-‘ulūfah (with dammah) is plural of ‘alaf. It is said: 'I fed the animal' and not 'I fed it' (with hamza), and the animal is ma‘lūfah and ‘alīf. Like this in Ghāyat al-Bayān. And we mentioned earlier from al-Qunyah that if he had camels that work for four months in the year and he fattens them for the rest, it is befitting that no zakat is obligatory on them.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof explaining that zakat is not due on animals that are fed fodder (علوفة) or used as work animals (عوامل). The primary proof is a hadith: 'There is no charity on pregnant, work, and fodder-fed animals.' The reasoning (تعليل) is that zakat is caused by growing wealth (مال نامٍ), and fodder-fed animals have high maintenance costs that prevent natural increase. Work animals also lack growth. However, if these animals are kept for trade, then trade zakat applies. The commentator defines linguistic terms and adds a practical example from al-Qunyah: if work camels are used for labor part of the year and fattened the rest, no zakat is due.

Key Terms
علوفة (ʿulūfah): Animals fed fodder rather than grazing freely; not subject to zakat.
عوامل (ʿawāmil): Work animals used for labor; exempt from zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are fodder-fed animals ('alufah) not subject to zakat?
A) Because the hadith specifically excludes them.
B) Because they lack natural growth due to high costs.
C) Both A and B.
D) Because they are used for trade.

Key Takeaway
Zakat on livestock is only due on grazing animals (sa'imah); fodder-fed and work animals are exempt unless used for trade.

Trade vs. Non-Trade: The Condition That Changes the Ruling
Qualification of exemption rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when fodder-fed or work animals become subject to zakat (due to trade) and apply the correct zakat category (livestock vs. trade goods).

Core Idea
The exemption of fodder-fed and work animals applies only when not used for trade.

The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq makes a crucial qualification: the negation of zakat on 'alufah and 'awamil refers specifically to livestock zakat. If these animals are purchased or kept for trade, they fall under the rules of zakat al-tijarah (trade goods). This lesson explores that distinction and its practical implications for the modern Muslim.

Guided Path
1
Note the qualification in the text
The author says: 'The intended meaning of negating zakat on fodder-fed animals is the zakat of grazing animals, because if they were for trade the zakat of trade would be obligatory.' Identify the dual theme: livestock zakat (on sa'imah) vs. trade zakat (on all trade goods).
This shows that the exemption is not absolute.
2
Understand the concept of trade goods (mal tijarah)
Goods purchased with the intent to sell are subject to zakat at 2.5% of market value after one year. This applies to any asset, including animals, if held for trade.
Intent (niyyah) and action (purchase/sale) are key.
3
Apply the distinction to scenarios
Given a case, decide: is the animal held for grazing/fodder/work (exempt) or for resale (subject to trade zakat)? Use the signs of trade: frequent buying/selling, profit motive, etc.
Remember: the animal itself is exempt from livestock zakat, but its value may be subject to trade zakat.

Source Text

Ruling on Lost Property After Zakat Becomes Obligatory
Ruling-with-proof on zakat obligation after property loss

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat when the property is lost after the year, distinguish between loss (halk) and consumption (istihlak), and apply the rule of istibdal to trade goods vs. grazing animals.

Core Idea
Zakat is on the asset ('ayn); its loss after the year drops the obligation, but consumption does not.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains a key Hanafi distinction: if your zakatable property is genuinely lost after the year has passed, the zakat obligation falls away entirely or proportionally. However, if you deliberately consume or dispose of the property, the obligation remains because you are at fault. The text also explores what counts as consumption, especially when you exchange one zakatable asset for another.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
What is the Hanafi rule when zakatable property is lost after the year? State it precisely: if all is lost, all obligation drops; if part, proportional.
Loss must be genuine, not through owner's fault.
2
Understand the underlying principle
Why does the obligation drop? Because zakat is due on the asset itself (al-'ayn), not on the liability (al-dhimmah). Loss of the asset removes the subject of the obligation.
This principle distinguishes Hanafi from some Shafi'i views.
3
Examine the evidence (dalil)
The hadith 'Bring a quarter of the tithe...' is cited as a general command. It does not specify that the obligation survives loss, implying it is contingent on the existence of the asset.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but supports the Hanafi position.
4
Distinguish loss from consumption
If the owner consumes the property after the year, the obligation remains due to transgression. Consumption includes deliberate disposal without a valid substitute.
Withholding animals for fodder/water until death is debated: some say consumption, some say not.
5
Apply the istibdal rule
Exchanging trade goods for trade goods does not break the year or count as consumption, because zakat is on the value. Exchanging grazing animals, even for their own kind, is consumption because zakat is attached to the specific animal.
This affects whether the new asset continues the previous year's count.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

في الذمة، فعندنا تجب في العين وهو المشهور من قول الشافعي وفي قول له تجب في الذمة والعين مرتهنة بها. كذا في غاية البيان. ثم الظواهر تؤيد ما قلنا مثل قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام) هاتوا ربع العشور من كل أربعين درهماً درهم. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا تمكن من الأداء وفرط في التأخير حتى هلك وما إذا منع الإمام أو الساعي بعد الطلب حتى هلك، وفي الثاني خلاف وعامتهم على السقوط وهو الصحيح لأنه لم يفوت بهذا المنع ملكاً يستدعي زماناً فالحبس لذلك اهـ. وقيد بالهلاك لأنه لو استهلكه بعد الحول لا تسقط عنه لوجود التعدي، واختلف فيما لو حبس السائمة للعلف أو للماء حتى هلكت، قيل هو استهلاك فيضمن، وقيل لا يضمن كالوديعة إذا استهلاك، واستبدال ملکه قوله : ( وقيد بالهلاك لأنه لو استهلكه أقول : المراد بالاستهلاك. إخراج النصاب عن . قصداً بلا بدل يقوم مقامه فاستبدال مال التجارة بمال التجارة ليس باستهلاك لقيام الثاني مقام الأول لأن الزكاة لم تتعلق بعينه بخلاف السائمة فإن استبدالها ولو بجنسها استهلاك لأن بدلها لا يقوم مقامها لتعلق الزكاة بعينها قوله : (واختلف فيما لو حبس السائمة للعلف الخ) قال في النهر : الذي يقع في نفسي ترجيح الأول، ثم رأيته في البدائع جزم به ولم يحك غيره قوله : (للعلف أو للماء) اللام بعنى عن تأمل قوله : واستبدال مال التجارة بمال التجارة ليس باستهلاك) أي وليس بهلاك أيضاً خلافاً لما فهمه في النهر والدنانير إذا باعها بجنسها أو بخلاف جنسها بأن باع الدراهم بالدراهم أو الدنانير بالدنانير أو الدراهم بالدنانير. وقال الشافعي : ينقطع حكم الحول فعلى قياس قوله لا تجب الزكاة في مال الصيارفة لوجود الاستبدال منهم ساعة
His saying: (And not) the lost after obligation, i.e., nothing on the lost after obligation. If all the property is lost, the entire obligation drops; if some, it drops proportionally. Al-Shafi'i said: He is liable if it is lost after being able to pay. This is based on whether zakat is due on the asset or on the liability. According to us, it is due on the asset, which is the well-known saying of al-Shafi'i too. In one of his sayings, it is due on the liability and the asset is held as collateral. This is in Ghayat al-Bayan. Then the apparent evidences support what we say, such as his saying (peace be upon him): 'Bring a quarter of the tithe from every forty dirhams: one dirham.' It is general and includes cases where he was able to pay and delayed until it was lost, and where the imam or the collector prevented after demand until it was lost. In the second case there is disagreement, but the majority say it drops, and that is correct because he did not, by this prevention, cause loss of ownership or possession to anyone, so it is like him asking a poor person. Al-Fath al-Qadir preferred it as more in accordance with fiqh because although the collector is specified, the owner has a choice in selecting the place of payment between the asset and the value, and the value is distributed over many places, and the choice requires time, so the detention is for that. End. And it is restricted to loss, because if he consumed it after the year, it does not drop due to transgression. And there is disagreement about if he withheld grazing animals for fodder or water until they died: some say it is consumption so he guarantees; some say no guarantee, like a trust if he withheld it for that until it died, no guarantee. This is in al-Mi'raj. And we mentioned that forgiving a debt after the year absolutely is not consumption, so no zakat on it. In al-Khaniyah: Exchanging trade goods for trade goods is not consumption, and for non-trade goods it is consumption. And exchanging his property... His saying: (And it is restricted to loss because if he consumed it...) I say: The meaning of consumption is removing the nisab from [his ownership] intentionally without a substitute that takes its place. So exchanging trade goods for trade goods is not consumption because the second takes the place of the first, since zakat is not attached to the specific asset. Unlike grazing animals, exchanging them even for their own kind is consumption because their substitute does not take their place due to zakat being attached to the specific asset. His saying: (And there is disagreement about if he withheld grazing animals for fodder or water...) He said in al-Nahr: What occurs to me is preference for the first, then I saw it in al-Bada'i decided and no other mentioned. His saying: (for fodder or for water) the lam means 'against'? Contemplate. His saying: (And exchanging trade goods for trade goods is not consumption) i.e., also not loss, contrary to what was understood in al-Nahr, because the nisab remains as it is due to the existence of its substitute. Unlike the exchange of grazing animals even for their own kind, because zakat is attached to the specific asset, so the substitute does not take its place. He said in al-Bada'i: If he exchanges trade goods for trade goods, which are merchandise, before the completion of the year, the ruling of the year is not invalidated, whether he exchanges them for their own kind or for a different kind, without disagreement, because the obligation of zakat in trade goods is attached to the meaning of wealth, which is monetary value, so the year is contracted upon the meaning and it remains, not lost by exchange. Similarly, for dirhams and dinars if he sells them for their own kind or for a different kind, such as selling dirhams for dirhams or dinars for dinars or dirhams for dinars. And al-Shafi'i said: The ruling of the year is cut off, based on his saying that zakat is not obligatory on the wealth of money-changers due to their constant exchange.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof addressing what happens to the zakat obligation when the zakatable property is lost after the completion of the year (after wujub). The Hanafi rule: if the entire property is lost, the entire zakat drops; if part is lost, the obligation drops proportionally. The Shafi'i position differs: if the owner had the ability to pay and delayed, he remains liable for the lost amount. This hinges on whether zakat is due on the asset itself (al-‘ayn) or on the liability (al-dhimmah). The Hanafis hold it is on the asset, so loss of the asset removes the obligation. The commentator supports this with the general hadith 'Bring a quarter of the tithe...' which does not distinguish loss cases. He also discusses the case where the imam or collector prevents the owner from paying until the property is lost; the majority rule that the obligation drops because the owner did not commit aggression. The passage then distinguishes between genuine loss (halk) and deliberate consumption (istihlak). If the owner consumes the asset after the year, the obligation remains due to transgression. There is disagreement on whether withholding grazing animals from fodder or water until they die counts as consumption. Finally, the text delves into the effect of exchanging (istibdal) zakatable assets: exchanging trade goods for trade goods does not break the year or count as consumption, because zakat is on the value, not the specific item. But exchanging grazing animals, even for their own kind, is consumption because zakat is attached to the specific animal. A quote from al-Bada'i closes the passage.

Key Terms
الهالك (al-hālik): Property that is genuinely lost (e.g., destruction, theft) after the zakat year, which drops the obligation if not due to owner's action.
الاستهلاك (al-istihlāk): Deliberate consumption or disposal of the zakatable property without a valid substitute; this does not waive the zakat obligation.
الاستبدال (al-istibdāl): Exchange of one property for another; relevant for whether it breaks the zakat year or counts as consumption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person's 40 sheep are lost in a flood after the year but before he had a chance to pay zakat, what is the ruling?
A) He must still pay zakat because the obligation was established.
B) The zakat obligation drops because the asset is lost.
C) He must pay zakat from other wealth.
D) He must pay only if he delayed intentionally.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, zakat is on the asset; genuine loss of the asset after the year removes the obligation, but deliberate consumption does not.

The Hanafi Dispute on Zakat Exemption (Afw): Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the scope of 'afw in zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on 'afw (exemption) in zakat and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa extends zakat exemption to all wealth; the Sahibayn restrict it to grazing livestock.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi disagreement over the concept of 'afw (exemption) in zakat. The base text likely stated a general rule, and the commentator clarifies that while Imam Abu Hanifa applies exemption universally, his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, limit it to grazing livestock (sawa'im). Understanding this difference is essential for correctly applying zakat thresholds on cash and livestock.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disputed Concept
The term 'afw (exemption) refers to the amount of wealth that is not subject to zakat despite exceeding the nisab threshold. The dispute centers on whether this exemption applies to all types of wealth or only to specific categories.
Exemption here is different from the nisab itself; it concerns the surplus over the nisab.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position
Abu Hanifa holds that 'afw applies to all wealth, including cash. This means that if someone has, for example, 300 dirhams, the exemption applies to the 100 dirhams above the nisab, so only zakat on 200 dirhams is due.
This position is considered the Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad restrict 'afw solely to grazing livestock (sawa'im). According to them, for cash (dirhams and dinars), any amount exceeding 200 dirhams is fully subject to zakat with no exemption.
Their reasoning: what exceeds 200 dirhams has no exemption because the ruling is built on the unit of the nisab.
4
Analyze the Reasoning (Talil)
The text provides the Sahibayn's reasoning: 'because what exceeds two hundred dirhams has no exemption according to them.' This indicates that for cash, the entire amount above the nisab is zakatable, unlike livestock where small excesses may be exempt.
The underlying principle may relate to the ease of calculating zakat on cash versus the difficulty with livestock.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi Position
Although both positions have merit, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa, applying 'afw to all wealth. However, some later scholars may prefer the Sahibayn's view for caution (ihtiyat).
Check local fatwa practice; but the dominant view is Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عند أبي حنيفة في جميع الأموال وعندهما لا يتصور العفو إلا في السوائم لأن ما زاد على مائتي درهم لا عفو فيه عندهما ا هـ .
According to Abu Hanifa, [exemption] is in all wealth, but according to them (the two disciples), exemption is only conceivable in grazing livestock, because what exceeds two hundred dirhams has no exemption according to them. End.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute on the concept of 'afw (exemption) in zakat. The base text likely stated a general rule, and the commentator explains the positions. Abu Hanifa holds that exemption applies to all types of wealth, including cash, so there is no zakat on small amounts below nisab. However, his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, restrict exemption solely to grazing livestock (sawa'im). Their reasoning: for cash (dirhams and dinars), any amount exceeding 200 dirhams, even a small excess, is subject to zakat with no exemption for the surplus. This difference arises from their understanding of the hadith evidence and the nature of zakat on different types of property. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is often that of Abu Hanifa in this regard, though caution (ihtiyat) may be observed.

Key Terms
العفو (al-‘afw): Exemption: the amount excluded from zakat before reaching nisab or the surplus over nisab that is not subject to zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Only grazing livestock (sawa'im)
C) Only cash (dirhams and dinars)
D) Only trade goods

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on 'afw centers on whether exemption applies to all wealth (Abu Hanifa) or only to grazing livestock (Sahibayn); the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

Destruction of Zakatable Property After Obligation: The Hanafi Rule and Its Proof
Ruling on destruction of property after zakat becomes due, with Shafi'i dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat when property perishes after the year and explain the proof from the hadith and the underlying usul principle.

Core Idea
Zakat is on the property itself; natural destruction after wujub drops the obligation.

What happens to your zakat obligation if your wealth is destroyed after the year has passed? The Hanafi school distinguishes between natural loss (halak) and deliberate consumption (istihlak). This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof from the hadith, and the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i over the nature of the zakat obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Determine what the ruling is: for total destruction (all drops), partial destruction (proportionally), and note the condition that it is natural loss (halak) not intentional consumption.
The key is the distinction between halak and istihlak.
2
Locate the primary evidence
Find the hadith cited: 'Bring a quarter of the tithe…' and note that it is unqualified (mutlaq), applying to all cases regardless of ability to pay.
The hadith is ahad and zanni al-thubut, but it is the proof for the Hanafi position.
3
Understand the usul principle behind the ruling
The difference between Hanafi and Shafi'i stems from whether zakat is on the property (al-ayn) or on the liability (al-dhimmah). Hanafis hold it is on the property, so if the property is gone, the obligation disappears.
This is a fundamental usul al-fiqh point applicable to many zakat rulings.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that zakat is on the dhimmah, so the owner remains liable if he had ability to pay. The Hanafi rebuttal uses the hadith's unqualified wording and the majority view that the obligation drops when the collector prevents payment.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis say no zakat on lost property; Shafi'is say zakat is due if the owner was able to pay.
5
Evaluate the tarjih within the Hanafi school
Note that the commentator prefers the ruling of saqut (dropping) even when the collector prevents, as it respects the owner's right to choose the method of payment. This is the mufta bihi position.
The tarjih authority is Fath al-Qadir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا) الهالك بعد الوجوب أي لا شيء في الهالك بعد الوجوب فإن هلك المال كله سقط الواجب كله وإن بعضه فبحسابه وقال الشافعي : يضمن إذا هلك بعد التمكن من الأداء وهو مبني على أن الزكاة تجب في العين أو في الذمة، فعندنا تجب في العين وهو المشهور من قول الشافعي وفي قول له تجب في الذمة والعين مرتهنة بها. كذا في غاية البيان. ثم الظواهر تؤيد ما قلنا مثل قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام) هاتوا ربع العشور من كل أربعين درهماً درهم. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا تمكن من الأداء وفرط في التأخير حتى هلك وما إذا منع الإمام أو الساعي بعد الطلب حتى هلك، وفي الثاني خلاف وعامتهم على السقوط وهو الصحيح لأنه لم يفوت بهذا المنع ملكاً على أحد ولا يداً فصار كما لو طلب واحد من الفقراء، ورجحه في فتح القدير بأنه الأشبه بالفقه لأن الساعي وإن تعين لكن للمالك رأي في اختيار محل الأداء بين العين والقيمة، ثم القيمة شائعة في محال كثيرة والرأي يستدعي زماناً فالحبس لذلك اهـ. وقيد بالهلاك لأنه لو استهلكه لا تسقط عنه لوجود التعدي، واختلف فيما لو حبس السائمة للعلف أو للماء حتى هلكت، قيل هو استهلاك فيضمن، وقيل لا يضمن كالوديعة إذا منعها لذلك حتى هلكت لم يضمن. كذا في المعراج . وقدمنا أن الإبراء عن الدين بعد الحول مطلقاً ليس باستهلاك فلا زكاة فيه.
His saying: 'nor [zakat] on what is destroyed after obligation' means: nothing is due on property destroyed after obligation becomes due. If all the wealth perishes, the entire obligation drops; if part, then proportionally. Al-Shafi'i said: He is liable if it perishes after he was able to pay. This is based on whether zakat is obligated on the property itself (al-ayn) or on the liability (al-dhimmah). According to us, it is obligated on the property, and that is the well-known view of al-Shafi'i, but he has another view that it is obligated on the liability and the property is pledge for it. This is cited in Ghayat al-Bayan. Then, the apparent implications support what we said, such as his statement (peace be upon him): 'Bring a quarter of the tithe: for every forty dirhams, one dirham.' It is unqualified, so it includes cases where he was able to pay and delayed negligently until it perished, and where the Imam or collector prevented him after demand until it perished. In the second case, there is disagreement, but the majority hold it drops, and that is correct because by this prevention he did not cause loss of ownership to anyone nor control, so it is like if a single poor person demanded. Al-Marghinani in Fath al-Qadir favored it as closer to fiqh because although the collector is specified, the owner has an opinion in choosing the place of payment between the property and its value; then the value is distributed over many places and opinion requires time, so detention for that reason. End. And he restricted [the ruling] to destruction because if he consumes it, it does not drop due to transgression. They differed regarding detaining livestock for fodder or water until they perished: it is said that it is consumption and he is liable; it is said that he is not liable, like a deposit when one detains it for that reason and it perishes. This is in al-Mi'raj. And we have previously stated that forgiving a debt after the year is absolutely not consumption, so there is no zakat on it.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on zakatable property that perishes after zakat becomes obligatory. According to the Hanafi school, if the property is destroyed naturally without fault of the owner, the zakat obligation drops in proportion. Imam al-Shafi'i held that the owner is liable if he had the ability to pay and delayed, causing loss. This difference stems from a fundamental principle: does zakat attach to the specific property (al-ayn) or to the owner's liability (al-dhimmah)? Hanafis hold zakat is upon the property itself, so if the property perishes, the obligation ceases. The commentator cites the hadith 'Give a quarter of the tithe...' as evidence, showing the obligation is on the property. The analysis then discusses cases where the owner delays payment or the collector prevents collection. The majority ruling is that if the collector prevents the owner after seeking the zakat and the property perishes, the obligation drops because the owner did not wrong anyone. This is the preferred view, as it respects the owner’s right to choose between paying in kind or value. The passage also distinguishes between destruction (halak) and intentional consumption (istihlak): consumption does not drop the obligation. Another ruling: if an owner detains livestock for fodder or water, leading to death, there is a difference of opinion whether it counts as consumption. Some analogize to a deposit: if depositor detains deposit and it perishes, he is not liable unless he acted wrongfully. Finally, forgiving a debt (ibra') after the year is not consumption, so no zakat is due on it.

Key Terms
الهالك (al-hālik): The perished property: property destroyed naturally without owner's fault.
الاستهلاك (al-istihlāk): Consumption: deliberate use or disposal of property such that it is no longer in owner's possession.
الإبراء (al-ibrā’): Forgiveness of a debt: waiving the right to collect a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The obligation drops
C) The owner must pay half
D) The obligation is postponed

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, zakat is an obligation on the property itself; natural destruction (halak) after the year removes the obligation, but intentional consumption (istihlak) does not.

The Collector's Option When Sa'imah Is Sold
Explanation of collector's options when sa'imah is sold.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the collector's options when sa'imah is sold and apply the ruling depending on whether the collector was present at the time of sale.

Core Idea
The collector may take zakat from the buyer if present; if absent, only from the seller.

Selling zakatable livestock (sa'imah) before zakat is paid is considered consumption (istihlak), not substitution. This triggers the collector’s right to collect the wajib from either the seller or the buyer, depending on his presence at the time of sale. This lesson explains the two scenarios and the rationale behind the collector’s authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify selling sa'imah as consumption
Recognise that selling sa'imah for mal (including its like) is istihlak because the obligation attaches to both the physical animal and its value.
Consumption means the zakat obligation is not extinguished; it must be fulfilled from the remaining property.
2
Distinguish the collector's presence and absence
If the collector is present at the sale session, he has two options: take the value of the wajib from the seller (sale stands) or take the wajib animal from the buyer (sale voided to that extent). If absent at sale and arrives after the parties have left the session, he may only take from the seller.
The collector’s authority is like that of a judge in ijtihad.
3
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
Consider a seller who sells a flock of sa'imah. If the collector is present, he can decide which course to follow. If absent, he is restricted to the seller.
4
Compare with 'ushr on food
For food subject to 'ushr, the collector may take from either party regardless of presence, because 'ushr attaches more strongly to the physical item.
This contrast highlights the specific nature of zakat on livestock.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة فصل في الغنم
بيع
السائمة
مال السائمة بالسائمة استهلاك وإقراض النصاب بعد الحول ليس باستهلاك، وإن نوى المال على المستقرض، وكذا لو أعار ثوب التجارة بعد الحول ا وإنما كان هـ. استهلاكاً مطلقاً لأن الوجوب فيها متعلق بالصورة والمعنى فبيعها يكون استهلاكاً لا استبدالاً، فإذا باعها فإن كان المصدق حاضراً فهو بالخيار إن شاء أخذ قيمة الواجب من البائع وتم البيع في الكل وإن شاء أخذ الواجب من العين المشتراة وبطل البيع في القدر المأخوذ وإن لم يكن حاضراً وقت البيع وحضر بعد التفرق عن المجلس فإنه لا يأخذه من المشتري وإنما يأخذ قيمة الواجب من البائع ولو باع طعاماً وجب فيه العشر فالمصدق بالخيار إن شاء أخذ من البائع وإن شاء من المشتري، سواء حضر قبل الافتراق أو بعده تعلق العشر بالعين أكثر من تعلق الزكاة بها ألا ترى أن العشر لا يعتبر فيه المالك بخلاف الزكاة، كذا في البدائع. وفي معراج الدراية ولو استبدل السائمة بجنسها ينقطع حكم الحول لأن وجوب الزكاة في السائمة باعتبار عينها، وفي غيرها باعتبار ماليتها، فالعين الثانية في السائمة غير الأولى لفوات متعلق الوجوب بخلاف العروض لأن متعلق الوجوب هو المالية وهي باقية مع الاستبدال اهـ.

لأنه

Book of Zakat, Chapter on Sheep. Selling of sa'imah for sa'imah is consumption (istihlak), and lending the nisab after the hawl is not consumption, even if he intends the money upon the borrower. Similarly, if he lends a trade garment after the hawl... And it is consumption absolutely because the obligation in them is attached to both form and meaning, so selling them is consumption, not substitution. Therefore, if he sells them and the sadaqah collector is present, he has the option: if he wishes, he takes the value of the wajib from the seller and the sale is complete for all; if he wishes, he takes the wajib from the purchased item and the sale is void to the extent taken. If he was not present at the time of sale and appears after separation from the session, he does not take it from the buyer but takes the value of the wajib from the seller. If he sells food on which 'ushr is obligatory, the collector has the option: if he wishes, he takes from the seller, if he wishes, from the buyer, whether he appears before or after separation. The attachment of 'ushr to the item is stronger than the attachment of zakat to it; do you not see that 'ushr does not consider the owner unlike zakat. Thus in al-Bada'i. In Ma'raj al-Dirayah: if he exchanges sa'imah for its kind, the rule of the hawl is cut off because the obligation of zakat on sa'imah is with consideration of its 'ayn, and on others with consideration of its monetary value. So the second 'ayn in sa'imah is other than the first due to loss of the subject of obligation, unlike trade goods because the subject of obligation is monetary value and it remains with substitution. End. Because they restricted with substitution: since removing zakat wealth from his ownership without compensation like gift to non-poor, bequest, or with compensation that is not wealth such as marrying a woman, settling for blood money of intentional killing, or a woman redeeming herself, it is consumption and he guarantees the zakat. And their statement: 'exchanging trade goods for their like is not consumption' is excepted when he engages in preferential pricing (muhabah) with what people do not overlook, then he guarantees the amount of zakat of the preferential portion and it becomes a debt in his liability, and the zakat of what remains transfers to the item and remains with its existence as in al-Bada'i. So when it becomes consumed by gift... So immediately, as when he sells sa'imah for sa'imah. And we have that the obligation in dirhams and dinars is attached to meaning also, not to the 'ayn, and the meaning remains after substitution, so the rule of the hawl is not nullified, as in the hawl, unlike exchanging sa'imah for sa'imah because the rule there attaches to the 'ayn so the hawl that was initiated on the first is nullified and a new hawl begins for the second. And similar will come shortly in the author's words from al-Mi'raj. His statement: (And other than trade goods is consumption). Al-Fath restricted it by that he intends for the substitute non-trade at the time of substitution. He said: we said that only because if he did not intend for the substitute non-trade while the original was for trade, the substitute falls for trade. His statement: (And he appears after separation from the session). He restricted by session because in al-Walwaljiyya: the meaning of separation is by body, so that if they were in the session of contract, the collector may take from the buyer even if he has taken it and moved it, because the completion of sale before bodily separation is a matter of ijtihad, and the collector in sadaqah funds is like the judge in other rulings due to his established authority. So the collector may exercise ijtihad. If his ijtihad leads to the sale being complete, he takes the zakat from the seller because the right is in the seller's liability; if his ijtihad leads to the sale not being complete, he takes from the buyer.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a sharh on the rulings of selling sa'imah (pasturing livestock subject to zakat) and the options available to the sadaqah collector (musaddiq). The author begins by distinguishing between consumption (istihlak) and substitution (istibdal). Selling sa'imah for sa'imah is considered consumption because the zakat obligation attaches to both the physical animal and its meaning (value). Thus, the sale does not extinguish the obligation; rather, the collector may, if present, choose to take the wajib value from the seller or the wajib animal from the buyer (voiding the sale to that extent). If the collector was absent at the time of sale and arrives after the parties have left the session, he may only take from the seller, not the buyer. For 'ushr on food, the collector may take from either party regardless of presence. The reason is that 'ushr attaches more strongly to the physical item. The passage then discusses exchanging sa'imah for its kind: this cuts off the hawl because zakat on livestock depends on the specific animal, whereas for trade goods it depends on value, which remains after exchange. The author also addresses exceptions: removing zakat property without compensation (gift, bequest) or with non-wealth consideration (marriage, blood money) is consumption; preferential pricing (muhabah) in trade requires guarantee of zakat on the discount. Finally, the collector's ijtihad is emphasized: since he acts as a judge, he can decide based on his reasoning whether the sale was completed before bodily separation, and accordingly take from seller or buyer.

Key Terms
سائمة (sa'imah): Livestock that graze freely in pasture for most of the year and are subject to zakat.
مصدق (musaddiq): The official collector of zakat appointed by the state.
استهلاك (istihlak): Removing the zakatable property from ownership in a way that nullifies the zakat obligation, such as selling or gifting it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person sells his sa'imah to another. The zakat collector was present at the sale. Which of the following is NOT a valid option for the collector?
A) Take the value of the wajib from the seller, leaving the sale intact.
B) Take the wajib animal from the buyer, voiding the sale to that extent.
C) Take the wajib animal from the seller, leaving the sale intact.
D) Force the buyer to pay the zakat out of his own pocket.

Key Takeaway
The collector's options when sa'imah is sold depend on his presence at the sale; when absent after separation, he may only take from the seller.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Exchanging Sa'imah and the Continuity of the Hawl
Explains why exchanging sa'imah cuts the hawl while exchanging trade goods does not.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why exchanging sa'imah for its kind cuts off the hawl, while exchanging trade goods does not, and apply the distinction based on the subject of obligation.

Core Idea
Hawl is cut when sa'imah is exchanged for its kind because obligation attaches to the specific animal, not value.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between sa'imah (livestock) and trade goods ('urud) regarding the effect of exchange on the zakat year (hawl). When sa'imah is exchanged for its kind, the hawl is cut off and a new one begins. For trade goods, the hawl continues because the obligation attaches to monetary value, which remains after exchange. This lesson unpacks the reasoning (ta'lil) behind this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of property
Distinguish between sa'imah (livestock subject to zakat) and trade goods ('urud al-tijarah). The ruling on exchange differs.
The same applies to cash (dinar/dirham) as trade goods? Actually cash is also value-based.
2
Understand the subject of obligation (mahall al-wujub)
For sa'imah, the obligation attaches to the physical animal ('ayn). For trade goods, it attaches to the monetary value (maliyya).
This is the key difference derived from istihsan.
3
Apply to exchange of sa'imah for its kind
Exchange (istibdal) replaces the original animal with a new one. Since the obligation is 'ayn-based, the subject is lost; thus the hawl is cut and a new hawl begins for the new animal.
Selling (istihlak) is different; it triggers immediate obligation.
4
Apply to exchange of trade goods for their kind
The value remains; the obligation transfers to the new item; hawl continues uninterrupted.
Exception: if the exchange involves muhabah (preferential pricing beyond usual tolerance), then partial consumption occurs.
5
Consider the collector's ijtihad on completion of exchange
As with sale, the collector's authority allows him to determine if the exchange was completed before bodily separation; this affects from whom he collects.

كتاب الزكاة فصل في الغنم
بيع
السائمة
مال السائمة بالسائمة استهلاك وإقراض النصاب بعد الحول ليس باستهلاك، وإن نوى المال على المستقرض، وكذا لو أعار ثوب التجارة بعد الحول ا وإنما كان هـ. استهلاكاً مطلقاً لأن الوجوب فيها متعلق بالصورة والمعنى فبيعها يكون استهلاكاً لا استبدالاً، فإذا باعها فإن كان المصدق حاضراً فهو بالخيار إن شاء أخذ قيمة الواجب من البائع وتم البيع في الكل وإن شاء أخذ الواجب من العين المشتراة وبطل البيع في القدر المأخوذ وإن لم يكن حاضراً وقت البيع وحضر بعد التفرق عن المجلس فإنه لا يأخذه من المشتري وإنما يأخذ قيمة الواجب من البائع ولو باع طعاماً وجب فيه العشر فالمصدق بالخيار إن شاء أخذ من البائع وإن شاء من المشتري، سواء حضر قبل الافتراق أو بعده تعلق العشر بالعين أكثر من تعلق الزكاة بها ألا ترى أن العشر لا يعتبر فيه المالك بخلاف الزكاة، كذا في البدائع. وفي معراج الدراية ولو استبدل السائمة بجنسها ينقطع حكم الحول لأن وجوب الزكاة في السائمة باعتبار عينها، وفي غيرها باعتبار ماليتها، فالعين الثانية في السائمة غير الأولى لفوات متعلق الوجوب بخلاف العروض لأن متعلق الوجوب هو المالية وهي باقية مع الاستبدال اهـ.
.
لأنه
وقيدوا بالاستبدال لأن إخراج مال الزكاة عن ملكه بغير عوض كالهبة من غير الفقير والوصية أو بعوض ليس بمال بأن تزوج امرأة وصالح به عن دم العمد أو اختلعت به المرأة فهو استهلاك فيضمن به الزكاة وقولهم إنَّ استبدال مال التجارة بمثله ليس باستهلاك يستثنى منه ما إذا جابى بما لا يتغابن الناس في مثله فإن يضمن قدر زكاة المحاباة ويكون ديناً في ذمته، وزكاة ما بقي تتحول إلى العين تبقى ببقائها كما في البدائع . فإذا صار مستهلكاً بالهبة
اهـ.
فساعة كما إذا باع السائمة بالسائمة، ولنا أن الوجوب في الدراهم والدنانير متعلق بالمعنى أيضاً لا بالعين، والمعنى قائم بعد الاستبدال فلا يبطل حكم الحول كما في الحول بخلاف ما إذا استبدل السائمة بالسائمة لأن الحكم هناك يتعلق بالعين فيبطل الحول المنعقد على الأول فيستأنف للثاني حول ويأتي قريباً نحوه في كلام المؤلف عن المعراج قوله : ( وبغير مال التجارة استهلاك) قيده في الفتح بأن ينوي في البدل عدم التجارة عند الاستبدال قال : وإنما قلنا ذلك لأنه لو لم ينو في البدل عدم التجارة وقد كان الأصل للتجارة يقع البدل للتجارة قوله : ( وحضر بعد التفرق عن المجلس) قيد بالمجلس لما في الولوالجية : المراد من التفرق بالبدن حتى لو كانا في مجلس العقد كان للساعي أن يأخذ من المشتري، وإن كان قد قبضه ونقله لأن تمام البيع قبل التفرق بالأبدان مجتهد فيه، والساعي في مال الصدقة بمنزلة القاضي في سائر الأحكام لثبوت ولايته فيها فكان للساعي أن يجتهد، فإن أدى اجتهاده إلى أن البيع قد تم أخذ الزكاة من البائع لأن الحق في ذمة البائع لأن البائع استهلك المال بإخراجه عن ملكه فصار الحق واجباً في ذمته، وإن أدى اجتهاده إلى أن البيع لم يتم أخد من المشتري
