Owner's Option When Exact Zakat Animal is Missing
Explains owner's option when wajib sin is missing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the exact wajib animal for zakat is unavailable, and apply the owner's option to give a higher or lower animal or value.

Core Idea
When the exact zakat animal is missing, the owner—not the collector—chooses a substitute and adjusts the surplus or deficit.

You know that zakat on livestock requires giving an animal of a specific age (sin). But what if you don't own that exact type? The Hanafi school provides a clear option: you can give a higher-grade animal and take back the difference, or give a lower animal and pay the difference. This lesson examines the ruling and its reasoning from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the original wajib
Recognize that a specific sin (age category) is due, e.g., bint makhad for camels, but the owner does not possess it.
The wajib is determined by the nisab and type of livestock.
2
State the three options given by the matn
The owner may: (1) give a higher animal and reclaim the surplus, (2) give a lower animal and pay the deficit, or (3) pay the cash value.
The value adjustment is based on market value.
3
Identify who holds the khiyar (option) and why
The text explicitly states that the choice belongs to the owner, not the collector (sāʿī). The reason is that the right is attached to the specific property (ʿayn al-māl), not to the owner's liability.
Al-Mabsut is cited as the source.
4
Explain the dalil from al-Mabsut
The collector has no right to object if the owner specifies which animal to give, because the zakat right is in the specific animal itself, not in the seller's liability.
This prevents the collector from forcing a particular substitute.
5
Note the practical implication
The owner can choose the most convenient substitute, and the collector must accept it subject to value adjustment.
This ruling facilitates payment when the exact wajib is unavailable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجب سن ولم يوجد دفع أعلى منها وأخذ الفضل أو دونها ورد الفضل أو القيمة
قوله : (ولو وجب سن ولو يوجد دفع أعلى منها وأخذ الفضل أو دونها ورد الفضل أو دفع القيمة) بيان لمسألتين: الأولى لو وجب عليه سن كبنت مخاض مثلاً ولم يكن عنده فصاحب المال مخير إن شاء دفع الأعلى واسترد الفضل أو الأدنى ورد الفضل فقد جعل الخيار للمالك دون الساعي فيهما، وقد صرح به في المبسوط وقال ليس للساعي إذا عين المالك
لأن الحق في عين المال بعد فيأخذ منه دون ذمة البائع، وطريق الأخذ منه أن يجبر البائع على الأداء منه وهو المراد من الأخذ من المشتري ا هـ .
An animal of a certain age (sin) is due and not found; he pays a higher one and takes the surplus, or a lower one and gives the surplus, or pays the value. His statement: (And if a sin is due and not found, he may pay a higher and take the surplus, or a lower and give the surplus, or pay the value) Explanation of two issues: The first: if an animal of a certain age, like a bint makhad, is due and he does not have it, the owner of the property has the choice: if he wishes, he gives a higher and reclaims the surplus, or a lower and gives the surplus. So the choice is given to the owner, not the collector. This is stated in al-Mabsut: the collector has no right if the owner specifies the animal because the right is in the specific property, so he takes from it, not from the seller’s liability. The way of taking from him is that he forces the seller to pay from it, and that is the meaning of taking from the buyer. End.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling when the exact wajib sin (age category) of livestock for zakat is not available. The matn states that the owner may give a higher quality animal and take back the surplus, or give a lower quality animal and pay the difference, or simply pay the cash value. The sharh clarifies that there are two issues. First, the owner has the option (khiyar) to choose any of these alternatives; the collector cannot force him to choose a specific one. Second, the proof from al-Mabsut is that the collector's right is attached to the specific animal (ayn al-mal) not to the seller's liability. Therefore, if the owner specifies which animal to take, the collector must accept that. The phrase 'taking from the buyer' means compelling the seller to hand over that animal.

Key Terms
سن (sin): The specific age or category of livestock that is due as zakat, e.g., bint makhad for camels.
فضل (fadl): The surplus or difference in value when giving a higher or lower animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who has the option (khiyar) when the exact wajib sin is not available?
A) The sadaqah collector (musaddiq)
B) The owner of the livestock
C) The buyer of the livestock
D) The judge

Key Takeaway
When the exact wajib animal for zakat is missing, the owner may give a higher or lower animal or its value, and the choice belongs to the owner, not the collector.

Rulings on Returning a Gift of Nisab and Mixing Wealth
Discusses return of gifted nisab, mixing inheritance with profit, and implications for zakat hawl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on return of gifted nisab (ruju') as faskh min al-asl with exceptions, and distinguish the effect of mixing inheritance vs profit on zakat.

Core Idea
Return of a gift is faskh min al-asl but not absolute; inheritance is not subsidiary while profit is subsidiary in zakat.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into the implications of returning a gifted nisab and how mixing wealth from inheritance or profit affects zakat. You'll learn that the return (ruju') of a gift is treated as annulment from the beginning (faskh min al-asl) but with important exceptions that impact the zakat calculation. Additionally, you'll see a nuanced difference between inherited wealth and profit when mixed with existing nisab.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of ruju' in gift
The donor's return of a gifted nisab is considered faskh min al-asl (annulment from the origin), meaning ownership reverts to the donor as if the gift never happened. However, this principle has exceptions.
2
Identify the exceptions to the absolute annulment
The donor does not own separate increments (e.g., offspring) that arose during the donee's possession. Also, if the donor acquired new property during the hawl and then returned the gift, the hawl for the new property starts from the acquisition time, not the original hawl.
This shows ruju' is not a complete annulment.
3
Apply the rule to mixing inherited wealth
If someone inherits additional nisab after the hawl and mixes it with his own, and then half perishes, half of the zakat is dropped. This is because inherited wealth is not subsidiary to the original.
This is the view of some Hanafi authorities; there is a dispute.
4
Distinguish the rule for profit
Profit earned after the hawl is considered subsidiary (tabi') to the principal. If mixed and half perishes, the loss is assigned to the profit (as 'afw), so no zakat is dropped.
This is agreed upon by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المستفاد بعد الحول فإذا رجع بقضاء أو غيره لا شيء عليه لو هلكت عنده بعده لأن الرجوع فسخ من الأصل والنقود تتعين في مثله فعاد إليه قديم ملكه ثم هلك فلا ضمان، ولو رجع بعد ما حال الحول عند الموهوب له فكذلك خلافاً لزفر فيما لو كان بغير قضاء فإنه يقول: يجب على الموهوب له فإنه مختار فكان تمليكاً قلنا : بل غير مختار لأنه لو امتنع عن الرد أجبر كذا في فتح القدير. وقولهم إن الرجوع فسخ من الأصل ليس على إطلاقه فقد صرحوا في الهبة أن الواهب لا يملك الزوائد المنفصلة برجوعه . . وفي الظهيرية : ولو وهب النصاب ثم استفاد مالاً في خلال الحول ثم رجع في الهبة يستأنف الحول في المستفاد من حين استفاده، فهذه المسألة تدل على أن الرجوع في الهبة ليس فسخاً للهبة من الأصل إذ لو كان فسخاً لما وجب استئناف في من وقت الاستفادة ا هـ . بلفظه . ثم اعلم أنه لو وهب النصاب في خلال الحول ثم تم الحول عند الموهوب له ثم رجع الواهب بقضاء أو غيره فلا زكاة على واحد منهما كما في الخانية، وهي من حيل إسقاط الزكاة قبل الوجوب كما لا يخفى. وفي المعراج : ولو حال الحول على مائتي درهم ثم ورث مثلها فخلطه بها وهلك النصف سقط نصف الزكاة لأن أحدهما ليس بتابع للآخر بخلاف ما لو ربح بعد الحول مائتين ثم هلك نصف الكل مختلطاً لم يسقط شيء لأن الربح تبع فيصرف الهلاك إليه كالعفو، وعندهما لا يتصور العفو في غير السوائم ا هـ. وسوى في المحيط بين الإرث والربح عندهما في عدم السقوط، وعند محمد يسقط نصفها وتمام تفاريعها فيه. وفي المعراج : ولو باع السوائم قبل تمام الحول بيوم فراراً عن الوجوب قال محمد: يكره . وقال أبو يوسف : لا يكره وهو الأصح ولو باعها للنفقة لا يكره بالإجماع، ولو احتال لإسقاط الواجب يكره بالإجماع، ولوفر من الوجوب بخلاً لا تأثيماً يكره بالإجماع ا هـ
قوله : (وفي المعراج ولو باع السوائم الخ) قال في متن درر البحار وشرحه غرر الأذكار ولا يكره أي يجوز أبو يوسف بلا كراهة حيلة دفعها أي منع وجوب الزكاة بأن يستبدل نصاب السائمة آخر الحول أو يخرجها عن ملكه في آخره ثم يدخلها لأن هذا امتناع عن الوجوب لا إبطال حق الغير، إذ ربما يخاف عدم امتثال أمره تعالى فيكون عاصياً والفرار من المعصية طاعة. وفي المحيط هذا أصح ومحمد خالفه أي أبا يوسف وكره حيلة دفعها ومعه الشافعي، واختار قوله الشيخ حميد الدين الضرير لأن في الحيلة إضراراً بالفقراء وقصد إبطال
The acquired (property) after the hawl: if he returns (the gift) by court order or otherwise, nothing is due upon him if it perishes with him after that, because the return is annulment from the origin (faskh min al-asl) and currencies are determined in its like, so his previous ownership returns and then it perishes, so no guarantee. And if he returns after the hawl has passed with the donee, similarly, contrary to Zufar in case it was without court order, for he says: it is obligatory on the donee because he is free agent, so it is a transfer of ownership. We say: rather he is not free agent, because if he refuses to return, he is forced. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And their statement that return is annulment from the origin is not absolute; they explicitly stated in gift that the donor does not own the separate increments by his return. And in al-Zahiriyya: if he gifted the nisab and then acquired property during the hawl, then returned the gift, the hawl for the acquired starts anew from the time of acquisition. This indicates that return in gift is not annulment of the gift from the origin, because if it were annulment, there would be no requirement to start a new hawl from the time of acquisition. End quote. Then know that if he gifted the nisab during the hawl, then the hawl completed with the donee, then the donor returned it by court order or otherwise, no zakat is due on either of them, as in al-Khaniyya, and it is among the legal stratagems (hiyal) to drop zakat before obligation, as is obvious. And in al-Mi'raj: if a full hawl passes on two hundred dirhams, then he inherits the like, mixes them, and half perishes, half of the zakat is dropped because one is not subsidiary to the other, unlike if he made a profit of two hundred after the hawl then half of the total mixed perishes, nothing is dropped because profit is subsidiary, so the loss is assigned to it like the 'afw (exempt portion). And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) 'afw is not conceived except for sa'imah. End. And al-Muhit made no distinction between inheritance and profit according to them in non-dropping, while according to Muhammad half drops, and all its details are in it. And in al-Mi'raj: if he sells the sa'imah one day before the completion of the hawl to flee from obligation, Muhammad said: it is disliked (makruh). Abu Yusuf said: it is not disliked, and it is the most sound (al-ah). If he sells them for maintenance, it is not disliked by consensus. If he uses a stratagem to drop the wajib, it is disliked by consensus. If he flees from obligation out of miserliness without regarding it sinful, it is disliked by consensus. End. His statement: (And in al-Mi'raj: and if he sells the sa'imah...) He said in the text of Durar al-Bihar and its commentary Ghurar al-Adhkar: it is not disliked, i.e., Abu Yusuf permits without dislike, the stratagem of avoiding it, i.e., preventing the obligation of zakat by exchanging the nisab of sa'imah at the end of the hawl or removing it from his ownership at the end then re-entering it, because this is abstention from obligation, not nullification of the right of others, since perhaps he fears not complying with Allah's command and would be sinful, and fleeing from sin is obedience. In al-Muhit, this is most correct. Muhammad disagreed with Abu Yusuf and disliked the stratagem of avoiding it, and al-Shafi'i agreed with him. Shaykh Hamid al-Din al-Darir chose his statement because the stratagem harms the poor and intends to nullify.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage covers several interrelated rulings on how changes in ownership affect zakat. First, it discusses the return (ruju') of a gifted nisab. If the donor takes back the property after the hawl has passed at the donee, and it perishes, no liability falls on the donor because the return is considered an annulment of the gift from the beginning (faskh min al-asl), so the property reverts to the donor and then perishes. However, this is not absolute: if the donee acquired separate increments (like offspring) before the return, the donor does not own them. Also, if the donor acquired new property after giving the gift and then returned the gift, the hawl for the newly acquired property starts from the time of acquisition, showing that return is not a complete annulment. The text then mentions a legal stratagem (hilah): giving away the nisab before hawl so that no zakat is due on either party when returned after hawl. Next, it addresses mixing inherited property with existing nisab: if half perishes, half the zakat drops because inheritance is not subsidiary. In contrast, profit is subsidiary, so if profit and original mix and half perishes, the loss is assigned to the profit (as the exempt portion), so no zakat drops. There is a dispute among Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Imam Muhammad regarding inheritance. Finally, the passage discusses selling sa'imah one day before hawl to avoid zakat. Abu Yusuf allows it without dislike because it is abstention from obligation, not nullification of the poor's right; the person may fear being unable to fulfill the obligation properly. Muhammad dislikes it because it harms the poor and intends to nullify their right. The relied-upon view is Abu Yusuf's (al-ah). Selling for genuine need (nafaqah) is permitted by consensus. Using a stratagem to drop the wajib is disliked by consensus, and fleeing out of miserliness is also disliked.

Key Terms
رجوع (ruju'): Returning a gift (hibah) by the donor to himself, which is considered a revocation of the gift.
تابع (tabi'): Subsidiary or dependent; here, profit is considered subsidiary to the principal nisab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to the zakat obligation if a person mixes inherited wealth with his existing nisab and half of the total perishes?
A) Zakat is due on the full original nisab because the loss is not assigned.
B) Half of the zakat is dropped because inheritance is not subsidiary.
C) No zakat is due because the nisab is lost.
D) The ruling varies; some authorities say half drops, others say no drop.

Key Takeaway
Return of a gift is faskh min al-asl with exceptions, and mixing inheritance with nisab reduces zakat differently than mixing profit.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
6 min
Selling Sa'imah Before Hawl to Avoid Zakat: A Hanafi Dispute
Discusses the ruling on selling sa'imah before hawl to avoid zakat, with a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on selling sa'imah one day before hawl to avoid zakat, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf permits selling sa'imah before hawl as abstention from sin; Muhammad dislikes it as harming the poor.

This passage presents a clear intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a person may sell his sa'imah (grazing livestock) one day before the completion of the zakat hawl to avoid the obligation. Abu Yusuf sees it as a permissible avoidance of potential sin, while Muhammad al-Shaybani and Imam al-Shafi'i consider it disliked because it harms the poor. The relied-upon view in later Hanafi texts is that of Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The issue is whether it is permissible (ja'iz) or disliked (makruh) to sell zakatable livestock (sa'imah) one day before the hawl ends with the express intention of avoiding zakat.
This is a legal stratagem (hilah) to evade an obligation.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf holds that it is ja'iz without any dislike. His reasoning: the person is abstaining from an obligation he might not be able to fulfill properly, and fleeing from potential sin is an act of obedience.
He distinguishes between nullifying a right of the poor (which would be haram) and avoiding the obligation before it becomes due.
3
State Muhammad's position
Muhammad al-Shaybani considers it makruh (disliked). His reasoning: it harms the poor by depriving them of their right, and the intention is to nullify their claim.
Al-Shafi'i agrees with Muhammad.
4
Determine the tarjih (preferred view)
The text states that Abu Yusuf's view is al-ah (most sound) and this is supported by al-Mi'raj and al-Muhit. However, Shaykh Hamid al-Din al-Darir chose Muhammad's view. The mufta bihi in later Hanafi practice is Abu Yusuf's view.
The passage also notes consensus on certain conditions: selling for genuine need (nafaqah) is not disliked; using a stratagem to drop a wajib is disliked by consensus; fleeing out of miserliness is disliked.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage covers several interrelated rulings on how changes in ownership affect zakat. First, it discusses the return (ruju') of a gifted nisab. If the donor takes back the property after the hawl has passed at the donee, and it perishes, no liability falls on the donor because the return is considered an annulment of the gift from the beginning (faskh min al-asl), so the property reverts to the donor and then perishes. Key Terms
حيلة (hilah): A legal stratagem to avoid an obligation, here to avoid zakat.
السوائم (al-sawa'im): Grazing livestock (camels, cattle, sheep, goats) that are zakatable if they reach nisab and a hawl passes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view on selling sa'imah one day before hawl to avoid zakat?
A) It is disliked (makruh) because it harms the poor.
B) It is permissible without dislike (ja'iz) according to Abu Yusuf, and this is the most sound view.
C) It is haram because it is a stratagem to avoid an obligation.
D) It is wajib to sell to avoid sin.

Key Takeaway
Selling sa'imah before hawl to avoid zakat is permissible (ja'iz) without dislike according to the relied-upon Hanafi view, though Muhammad al-Shaybani considered it makruh.

Owner's Options When Zakat Age Is Unavailable
Sharh on Kanz al-Daqa'iq about zakat on sheep

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on paying a higher or lower age or value in zakat on sheep, and explain the evidence and intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Core Idea
The owner has the choice to pay a higher/lower age with compensation or pay value; the tax collector cannot force the choice.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, commenting on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explains the options available to a zakat payer when the exact age of sheep is not available. It covers two main issues: (1) paying a higher or lower age with compensation, and (2) paying monetary value. The author also discusses exceptions and intra-Hanafi disagreements, grounding the ruling in the hadith and the principle of ease.

قوله : (ولو وجب سن ولو يوجد دفع أعلى منها وأخذ الفضل أو دونها ورد الفضل أو دفع القيمة) بيان لمسألتين: الأولى لو وجب عليه سن كبنت مخاض مثلاً ولم يكن عنده فصاحب المال مخير إن شاء دفع الأعلى واسترد الفضل أو الأدنى ورد الفضل فقد جعل الخيار للمالك دون الساعي فيهما، وقد صرح به في المبسوط وقال ليس للساعي إذا عين المالك لأن الحق في عين المال بعد فيأخذ منه دون ذمة البائع، وطريق الأخذ منه أن يجبر البائع على الأداء منه وهو المراد من الأخذ من المشتري ا هـ . استثنى في الهداية من ذلك ما إذا أراد المالك وأخذ الفضل من الساعي فإنه لا إجبار على الساعي لأنه شراء فحينئذ لم يكن للمالك خيار في هذه الصورة. وتبعه في التبيين وتعقبه في غاية البيان بأن الزكاة وجبت بطريق اليسر فإذا كان للساعي ولاية الامتناع من قبول الأعلى يلزم العسر وفي ذلك العود على الموضوع بالنقض فلا يجوز وأيضاً فيه خلاف السنة لأن من لزمه الحقة تقبل منه الجذعة إذا لم تكن عنده حقه، وكذلك من لزمه بنت لبون وعنده حقه يقبل منه الحقة ويعطى المصدق عشرين درهماً أو شاتين كما في صحيح البخاري، وهو دليلنا على دفع القيمة في الزكاة وهي في المسألة الثانية، وتقدير الفضل بالعشرين أو الشاتين بناء على الغالب لا أنه تقدير لازم ا قولهم إنه شراء ولا إجبار فيه فممنوع لأنه ليس شراء حقيقياً ولم يلزم من الإجبار ضرر بالساعي لأنه عامل لغيره، فالظاهر إطلاق المختصر من أن الخيار للمالك فيهما لكن ذكر محمد في الأصل أن الخيار للمصدق أي الساعي ورده في النهاية والمعراج بأن الصواب خلافه، وذكر في البدائع أن الخيار لصاحب المال دون المصدق إلا في فصل واحد وهو ما إذا أراد صاحب المال أن يدفع بعض العين لأجل الواجب فالمصدق بالخيار بين أن لا يأخذ وبين أن يأخذ بأن كان الواجب بنت لبون فأراد أن يدفع بعض الحقة بطريق القيمة، فالمصدق إن شاء قبل وإن شاء لم يقبل لما فيه من تشقيص العين والتشقيص في الأعيان عيب فكان له أن لا يقبل ا هـ. وتعقبه الزيلعي بأنه غير مستقيم لوجهين: أحدهما أنه مع العيب يساوي قدر الواجب وهو المعتبر في الباب والثاني أن فيه إجبار المصدق على شراء الزائد ا هـ. وقد قدمنا
ثم قال في البحر الرائق: دفع الأعلى وأما سناً أن يأبى ذلك في الصورتين. ثم قال: قوله : (لأنه ليس شراء حقيقياً) قال في النهر : كونه ليس بشراء حقيقة بل ضمناً لا يقتضي الإجبار، كيف والفاضل عن الواجب ملكاً للساعي ولا طريق لتملكه إياه إلا بالشراء قوله : (والثاني أن فيه إجبار المصدق على شراء الزائد) لم يظهر لنا هذا الكلام ولم أر من تعقبه وفي كلام المؤلف تسليم له وأنه لا يضر، ولقائل أن يقول إنه غير وارد على ما في البدائع لأن كلامه فيما إذا دفع البعض عن الواجب عليه بطريق القيمة البحر الرائق ج ٢ م ٢٥ يصير
His statement: (And if an age is obligated and is not found, he may pay a higher one and take the surplus, or a lower one and return the surplus, or pay the value) is an explanation of two issues: The first: If an age is obligated, e.g., a bint makhad, and he does not have it, then the owner of the wealth is given the choice: if he wishes, he may pay the higher and take back the surplus, or the lower and return the surplus. So the choice is given to the owner, not the tax collector, in both issues. This is stated in al-Mabsut, and it said: The tax collector does not have [the right] when the owner specifies, because the right is still attached to the specific wealth, so he takes from it, not from the guarantee of the seller. The way to take from him is to force the seller to pay from it, and that is what is meant by taking from the purchaser. Exception is made in al-Hidaya for the case where the owner wants to take the surplus from the tax collector: then there is no compulsion on the tax collector because it is a purchase, so then the owner has no choice in this case. And al-Tabyin followed it, and Ghayat al-Bayan objected: Zakat was obligated in a way of ease, so if the tax collector has authority to refuse to accept the higher, it would cause hardship, and in that there is a return to the subject in a contradictory manner, so it is not permissible. Also it is against the Sunnah because whoever owes a hiqqa, a jadha'a is accepted from him if he does not have a hiqqa, and likewise whoever owes a bint labun and has a hiqqa, the hiqqa is accepted from him and the collector gives him twenty dirhams or two sheep, as in Sahih al-Bukhari. This is our evidence for paying value in zakat, which is the second issue. The estimation of the surplus at twenty or two sheep is based on what is common, not that it is a fixed estimation. Their statement that it is a purchase and there is no compulsion in it is rejected, because it is not a real purchase, and compulsion does not harm the tax collector because he is an agent for others. So the apparent meaning of the abridgment is that the owner has the choice in both, but Muhammad stated in al-Asl that the choice is for the collector (the tax collector), and al-Nihaya and al-Mi'raj refuted that, saying the correct is contrary. Al-Bada'i stated that the choice is for the owner, not the collector, except in one case: when the owner wants to pay part of the specific animal for the obligated [age] as a value, then the collector has the choice to take or not, as when the obligated is bint labun and he wants to pay part of a hiqqa as a value, then the collector may accept or not, because it involves splitting the specific animal, and splitting a specific animal is a defect, so he has the right not to accept. Al-Zayla'i objected that it is not sound for two reasons: first, despite the defect, it equals the value of the obligated, which is what matters in the chapter; second, it forces the collector to buy the excess. We have already mentioned this.
Then al-Bahr al-Raiq said: Paying the higher, and as for the age that he may refuse in both cases... Then he said: His statement: (Because it is not a real purchase) – al-Nahr said: It is not a real purchase but a constructive one, which does not entail compulsion. How so, since the surplus over the obligated is owned by the collector, and there is no way for him to possess it except by purchase. His statement: (The second is that it compels the collector to buy the excess) – this statement is not clear to us, and I have not seen anyone who objected to it. In the author's words there is an acknowledgment of it and that it does not harm. But one could say that it does not apply to what is in al-Bada'i, because his words are about when he pays part of a specific animal for the obligated as a value. Al-Bahr al-Raiq, vol. 2, p. 25, becomes.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage is a sharh (commentary) on the matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the ruling when the exact age of a sheep obligated for zakat is not found. The author explains two issues: (1) paying a higher or lower age with compensation, and (2) paying the value. The main ruling is that the owner has the choice, not the tax collector, as stated in al-Mabsut. However, al-Hidaya makes an exception when the owner wants to take the surplus from the collector, then it is considered a purchase and the collector cannot be forced. The commentator from Ghayat al-Bayan objects to this exception, arguing it creates hardship and contradicts the Sunnah, citing the hadith from Bukhari where the Prophet accepted a jadha'a for a hiqqa and gave compensation. This hadith also serves as evidence for the permissibility of paying value in zakat. The author then discusses the intra-Hanafi disagreement: Imam Muhammad reportedly held that the collector has the choice, but al-Nihaya and al-Mi'raj side with the owner. Al-Bada'i further restricts the owner's choice in one case where partial payment causes splitting of the animal (a defect). Al-Zayla'i objects to al-Bada'i. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq then adds his own comments, defending the view that the owner's choice is general, and responding to Zayla'i's objection. The ruling is based on ease and the hadith, and the mufta bihi position is that the owner has the choice, except in the case of partial value payment where the collector may reject due to defect.

Key Terms
سن (sinn): The specific age or type of animal (e.g., bint makhad, jadha'a) obligated in zakat on sheep.
المصدق (al-musaddiq): The tax collector or assessor appointed by the state to collect zakat on livestock.
القيمة (al-qīmah): The monetary value of the animal paid in cash instead of the animal itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the owner's option when the exact age of sheep obligated for zakat is not available?
A) The owner must buy the exact age from the market.
B) The owner may pay a higher age and take back the surplus, but cannot pay a lower age.
C) The owner may pay a higher or lower age with compensation, or pay the monetary value.
D) The tax collector decides which age to accept from the owner.

Key Takeaway
The owner has the choice to substitute a different age or pay value in zakat on sheep when the exact age is unavailable, based on the hadith and the principle of ease.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
12 min
The Option (Khiyar) When Giving a Superior Animal in Zakat
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar with expansion from al-Hidayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the khiyar when an owner gives a superior animal in zakat and evaluate the exception for splitting.

Core Idea
The owner has the option to give a superior animal unless it involves splitting, which gives the collector the option to refuse.

When a zakat payer offers a better animal than required and asks for the surplus, a legal option (khiyar) arises. This lesson examines who holds that option—the owner or the collector—based on the Hanafi textual sources and the principle of ease in zakat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The passage discusses the situation where the owner wants to give a superior animal and take the surplus from the collector. Determine the underlying question: who has the right to accept or refuse?
The issue is not about the permissibility of paying value, but about the option (khiyar) to give a superior animal with compensation.
2
Follow the initial objection from Ghayat al-Bayan
The commentator presents the objection that refusing the superior creates hardship and contradicts the Sunnah. Examine the hadith about accepting jadha'ah when hiqqah is unavailable, which proves compensation is allowed.
This hadith is cited as evidence for the permissibility of paying value, but here it is used to argue that the collector cannot refuse the superior.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar
The text reports multiple views: the Mukhtasar gives the option to the owner; Imam Muhammad gives it to the collector; al-Bada'i' gives it to the owner except when splitting occurs. Trace the reasoning behind each view.
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq favors al-Bada'i's exception for splitting.
4
Understand the exception for tashqis (splitting)
When the owner pays part of a higher-age animal as value for the obligation, splitting is considered a defect. The collector may refuse. Evaluate the objections by al-Zayla'i and the author's response.
The dispute hinges on whether the defect is offset by equal value and whether the collector is forced to buy the surplus.
5
Derive the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The text concludes that the owner's option is the stronger view, but the collector may refuse in the splitting case. The fatwa in zakat follows Muhammad's view on value permissibility and the owner's option for khiyar.
See the tarjih from al-Nihayah and al-Mi'raj.

Book of Zakat, Chapter on Sheep. Paying the superior [animal]. And as for a [missing word] that he refuses that in the two scenarios. An exception was made in al-Hidayah from that for when the owner wants and takes the surplus from the collector, then there is no compulsion on the collector because it is a purchase, so then there is no option for the owner in this scenario. He was followed in al-Tabyin and refuted in Ghayat al-Bayan that zakat was obligated by way of ease, so if the collector has the authority to refuse accepting the superior, difficulty occurs, and in that is a return to the subject with nullification, so it is not permissible. Also, it contradicts the Sunnah because the one who owes a hiqqah, a jadha'ah is accepted from him if he does not have a hiqqah, and likewise the one who owes a bint labun and has a hiqqah, the hiqqah is accepted from him and the collector gives twenty dirhams or two sheep as in Sahih al-Bukhari, and that is our evidence for paying value in zakat, and it is in the second issue. And estimation of the surplus by the twenty or two sheep is based on the majority, not that it is a fixed estimation. Their statement that it is a purchase and there is no compulsion therein is rejected because it is not a real purchase, and no harm comes from compulsion on the collector because he is an agent for others. So apparently the summary (al-Mukhtasar) gives the option to the owner in both, but Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl that the option belongs to the collector, i.e., the agent, and it was refuted in al-Nihayah and al-Mi'raj that the correct is contrary to that. It was mentioned in al-Bada'i' that the option belongs to the owner, not the collector, except in one case: when the owner wants to pay part of the item for the obligation, then the collector has the option between not taking and taking, e.g., if the obligation is a bint labun and he wants to pay part of a hiqqah by way of value, then the collector may accept or not accept because it involves splitting the item, and splitting items is a defect, so he may not accept. al-Zayla'i refuted it as unsound for two reasons: first, even with the defect, it equals the value of the obligation which is considered in the chapter; second, it compels the collector to buy the surplus. We have already presented their right eventually. Similarly, the dispute regarding the stratagem for pre-emption (shuf'ah). As for a stratagem after the pre-emption becomes due, it is disliked by agreement. It is said the fatwa in pre-emption is according to Abu Yusuf's saying, and in zakat according to Muhammad's saying, and this is a good detail. The stratagem to avoid the obligation of zakat is prohibited according to most jurists, so much so that Malik invalidates the sale to avoid obligation, and al-Shafi'i prohibits the sale even if it is valid. Ahmad said: if the nisab decreases during some of the year, or he sells it or exchanges it for another type, the year is broken unless he intends thereby to escape zakat when its obligation is near, then it does not drop. He said (i.e., the commentator): (And in that is a return to the subject with nullification. He said in al-Nahr: how can it return to its subject with nullification given the permissibility of paying value? And it may be said against it that value is not available to the owner at all times, so if he does not have the obligatory [animal] nor the value and the collector refrains from taking the superior, difficulty occurs, so contemplate. He said: (because it is not a real purchase) He said in al-Nahr: its not being a real purchase but virtually does not necessitate compulsion; how so, since the surplus over the obligation is ownership of the collector and there is no way for him to own it except by purchase. He said: (and the second: that it compels the collector to buy the surplus) This statement is not apparent to us, and I have not seen anyone refute it, and in the author's speech there is acknowledgment of it and that it does not harm. One could say that it does not apply to what is in al-Bada'i' because his speech is about when he pays part of the obligation by way of value. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq vol. 2 p. 25 becomes compelling him to buy the surplus is sound, and it is not hidden that splitting the item harms the poor, so the owner does not have that, so what is in al-Bada'i' stands. But the author qualified the aforementioned option between the three things by the absence of the obligatory age (sin), as in most books, and it is a conventional qualification because the option exists even when the obligatory age exists. Hence it was said in al-Mi'raj: some of our associates thought that paying value is a substitute for the obligation such that the issue was called 'substitution', but it is not so, because resorting to a substitute is not permissible except when the original is absent, and paying value in the presence of the stipulated [animal] is permissible according to us. In al-Bada'i': our associates differed; according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), the obligation for non-grazing animals is a part of the nisab in meaning not form, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is form and meaning, but it is permissible to substitute another for it in meaning. They differed on grazing animals according to his saying; it is said they are like others, and it is said the stipulated obligation is in meaning, and according to the two it is stipulated obligation in form and meaning, but it is permissible to substitute another for it in meaning. On this principle are based the issues of al-Jami': a man has two hundred qafiz of wheat for trade worth two hundred dirhams and has no other property. If he pays from its same [type], he pays five qafiz without dispute. If he pays its value, then according to him (Abu Hanifa) the value is considered on the day of obligation in increase and decrease, and according to the two in both cases it is considered on the day of payment. They differed according to his saying on grazing animals: it is said [the day of] obligation, and it is said [the day of] payment, previously mentioned, and its completion is therein. In al-Muhit: the value of grazing animals is considered on the day of payment by consensus, and that is the most correct. It is mentioned in al-Jami': if the wheat spoils from what befell it until its value became one hundred, then he pays two and a half dirhams without dispute if he chooses value, because part of the item perished and the obligation attached to it fell. And if it increased in itself in value, the consideration is the day of obligation. In al-Hidayah: it is permissible to pay value in zakat, kaffarah, zakat al-fitr, 'ushr, and vows. In Fath al-Qadir: if he pays three fat sheep for four medium ones, or part of a bint labun for a bint makhad, it is permissible because the stipulated is medium, so the superior is not included in the text, and quality is considered in non-ribawi items, so it stands in place of the fourth sheep. Contrary to if it was a mithli: if he pays four good qafiz for five medium ones and they equal in value, it is not permissible. Or clothing: if he pays a garment worth two garments, it is not permissible except for one garment. Or if he vowed to give two sheep or free two medium slaves, and he gives one sheep or frees one slave worth each of the two mediums, it is not permissible. As for the first, because quality is not considered when comparing with its own kind, so quality does not stand for the fifth qafiz. As for the second, because the stipulated is absolute garment in kaffarah, not restricted to medium, so the superior and others are included under the text. As for the third, because the act of worship is in the pouring (of blood) and freeing, and he has committed to two pourings and two freings, so he does not exit from [the obligation], and the surplus remains the owner's property; he does not take the value of the surplus from him, nor is this the case of paying the superior and taking the surplus, and there is no splitting at all, so contemplate. Then it became apparent to me that this second one returns to the absolute statement of al-Bada'i' first that...
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the rulings of paying zakat from grazing animals (specifically sheep). It discusses two main issues: (1) the ruling on an owner giving a superior animal with compensation (taking surplus from the collector), and (2) the permissibility of paying value (qimah) instead of the specified animal. The commentary opens with an exception from al-Hidayah: if the owner wants to give a better animal and takes the surplus from the collector, there is no compulsion on the collector because it is treated as a purchase. However, this is contested by the author of Ghayat al-Bayan, who argues that zakat is based on ease, so refusing the superior creates hardship and contradicts the Sunnah. Proof is cited from Sahih al-Bukhari: if someone owes a hiqqah but does not have it, a jadha'ah is accepted; and if someone owes a bint labun but has a hiqqah, the hiqqah is accepted with the collector giving 20 dirhams or two sheep. This hadith is used as evidence for the permissibility of paying value in zakat (the 'second issue'). The author then clarifies that the estimation of 20 dirhams or two sheep is not a fixed ruling but based on prevailing circumstances. The claim that it is a purchase with no compulsion is rejected because it is not a real purchase, and the collector suffers no harm as an agent. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: the summary (al-Mukhtasar) gives the option to the owner, but Imam Muhammad in al-Asl gives it to the collector. This is refuted in al-Nihayah and al-Mi'raj. In al-Bada'i', the option is for the owner except in one case: when the owner pays part of the obligation through value (e.g., paying part of a hiqqah for a bint labun), then the collector may refuse due to splitting (tasqis) being a defect. al-Zayla'i criticizes this for two reasons: (1) even with defect, it equals the value of the obligation, and (2) it forces the collector to buy the surplus. The discussion continues with a side note on legal stratagems for shuf'ah and zakat, where the fatwa for shuf'ah is on Abu Yusuf's view and for zakat on Muhammad's. The prohibition of using sale to avoid zakat is emphasized, with Maliki and Shafi'i positions noted. Returning to the main issue, the author addresses objections from al-Nahr about returning to the subject with nullification, and the practical difficulty if the owner has neither the obligatory animal nor value. The second objection about forcing the collector to buy the surplus is examined, and it is concluded that it does not invalidate al-Bada'i' because splitting harms the poor. The option is then re-examined: it exists even when the obligatory age is present, contrary to some qualifications. Next, the passage delves into the nature of the wajib in zakat: according to Abu Hanifa, for non-grazing animals (like trade goods), the wajib is part of the nisab in meaning, not form; for the two disciples, it is both form and meaning, but substitution is allowed. A similar difference exists for grazing animals. This principle is applied to examples from al-Jami': a man with 200 qafiz of wheat for trade worth 200 dirhams. If he pays from the same wheat, he gives 5 qafiz. If he pays value, Abu Hanifa considers value on the day the obligation arose (wujub), while the two consider the day of payment (ada'). For grazing animals, the correct view is consensus on the day of payment. The permissibility of paying value is stated from al-Hidayah for zakat, kaffarah, sadaqat al-fitr, ushr, and vows. Finally, examples from Fath al-Qadir: paying three fat sheep for four medium ones is permissible because quality counts in non-ribawi items; but paying four good qafiz for five medium ones of equal value is not permissible because quality does not compensate for quantity in mithli items. Similarly, clothing substitution is limited, and vow fulfillment requires precise adherence. The passage ends with a reflection that the second example returns to the earlier statement from al-Bada'i'.

Key Terms
الخيار (al-khiyār): The option or choice given to either the owner or the collector regarding the acceptance of a superior animal with compensation or a payment of value.
التشقيص (al-tashqīṣ): Splitting an item, such as paying part of a hiqqah (a higher-age camel) to fulfill the obligation of a bint labun (a lower-age one). Considered a defect (ʿayb) because it splits the animal.
الساعي (al-sāʿī): The collector appointed by the state or imam to collect zakat from livestock and other apparent wealth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in which situation does the collector have the option to refuse a zakat payment?
A) When the owner gives a superior animal of the same species.
B) When the owner pays value (qimah) instead of the specified animal.
C) When the owner pays part of an animal as value for the obligation (tashqis).
D) The collector never has the option to refuse.

Key Takeaway
The owner generally has the option to give a superior animal in zakat and take the surplus, but the collector may refuse if the payment involves splitting an animal as value.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
15 min
Paying Value (Qimah) in Zakat and the Timing of Valuation
General ruling on paying value in zakat with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute on valuation timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi permissibility of paying value in zakat and identify the correct day for valuation according to the consensus and intra-Hanafi differences.

Core Idea
Paying value in zakat is permissible even when the specified animal exists; valuation for grazing animals is on the day of payment by consensus.

One of the distinctive Hanafi positions is the permissibility of paying cash or kind in lieu of the exact specified animal in zakat. This lesson explores the evidence from the hadith, the intra-Hanafi debate on whether it is a substitute or primary option, and the important question of when to value the payment for grazing and trade goods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on paying value
The text explicitly states from al-Hidayah: 'it is permissible to pay value in zakat, kaffarah, sadaqat al-fitr, ushr, and vows'. Note that this is a general ruling that goes beyond necessity.
This is a distinctive Hanafi view; Shafi'is restrict it to cases where the specified item is absent.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
The hadith about accepting jadha'ah when hiqqah is unavailable, and giving 20 dirhams or two sheep, is used as proof. Although the hadith mentions a case of necessity, the Hanafis extend it to general permissibility based on the principle of istihsan.
The text says 'estimation of the surplus by 20 dirhams or two sheep is based on prevalence, not a fixed estimation'.
3
Understand the nature of the wajib: part of nisab in meaning or form
The passage discusses a fundamental difference between Abu Hanifa and the two disciples. For non-grazing animals (e.g., trade goods), Abu Hanifa says the wajib is part of the nisab in meaning only; the two say it is both form and meaning. This affects whether substitution is allowed and when valuation occurs.
For grazing animals, there is further ikhtilaf, but the consensus is stated in al-Muhit: valuation on the day of payment.
4
Determine the day of valuation for grazing animals
The text cites al-Muhit: 'the value of grazing animals is considered on the day of payment by consensus'. This is the most correct view, even though there was earlier disagreement.
For trade goods (al-ard), Abu Hanifa uses the day of obligation; the two use the day of payment. But the consensus here specifically addresses grazing animals.
5
Apply the ruling to quality vs. quantity examples
The passage gives examples from Fath al-Qadir: paying three fat sheep for four medium ones is permissible because quality counts in non-ribawi items. But paying four good qafiz of wheat for five medium ones is not permissible because wheat is ribawi (mithli) and quality does not compensate for quantity. Similarly, clothing substitution is allowed, but vow fulfillment requires exact number of animals or slaves.
These examples illustrate the boundary of paying value: it works for non-mithli items where quality can substitute, but not for mithli items where quantity is essential.

And estimation of the surplus by the twenty or two sheep is based on the majority, not that it is a fixed estimation. Their statement that it is a purchase and there is no compulsion therein is rejected because it is not a real purchase, and no harm comes from compulsion on the collector because he is an agent for others. So apparently the summary (al-Mukhtasar) gives the option to the owner in both, but Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl that the option belongs to the collector, i.e., the agent, and it was refuted in al-Nihayah and al-Mi'raj that the correct is contrary to that. The stratagem to avoid the obligation of zakat is prohibited according to most jurists, so much so that Malik invalidates the sale to avoid obligation, and al-Shafi'i prohibits the sale even if it is valid. Hence it was said in al-Mi'raj: some of our associates thought that paying value is a substitute for the obligation such that the issue was called 'substitution', but it is not so, because resorting to a substitute is not permissible except when the original is absent, and paying value in the presence of the stipulated [animal] is permissible according to us. In al-Bada'i': our associates differed; according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), the obligation for non-grazing animals is a part of the nisab in meaning not form, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is form and meaning, but it is permissible to substitute another for it in meaning. They differed on grazing animals according to his saying; it is said they are like others, and it is said the stipulated obligation is in meaning, and according to the two it is stipulated obligation in form and meaning, but it is permissible to substitute another for it in meaning. On this principle are based the issues of al-Jami': a man has two hundred qafiz of wheat for trade worth two hundred dirhams and has no other property. If he pays from its same [type], he pays five qafiz without dispute. If he pays its value, then according to him (Abu Hanifa) the value is considered on the day of obligation in increase and decrease, and according to the two in both cases it is considered on the day of payment. They differed according to his saying on grazing animals: it is said [the day of] obligation, and it is said [the day of] payment, previously mentioned, and its completion is therein. In al-Muhit: the value of grazing animals is considered on the day of payment by consensus, and that is the most correct. It is mentioned in al-Jami': if the wheat spoils from what befell it until its value became one hundred, then he pays two and a half dirhams without dispute if he chooses value, because part of the item perished and the obligation attached to it fell. And if it increased in itself in value, the consideration is the day of obligation. In al-Hidayah: it is permissible to pay value in zakat, kaffarah, zakat al-fitr, 'ushr, and vows. In Fath al-Qadir: if he pays three fat sheep for four medium ones, or part of a bint labun for a bint makhad, it is permissible because the stipulated is medium, so the superior is not included in the text, and quality is considered in non-ribawi items, so it stands in place of the fourth sheep. Contrary to if it was a mithli: if he pays four good qafiz for five medium ones and they equal in value, it is not permissible. Or clothing: if he pays a garment worth two garments, it is not permissible except for one garment. Or if he vowed to give two sheep or free two medium slaves, and he gives one sheep or frees one slave worth each of the two mediums, it is not permissible. As for the first, because quality is not considered when comparing with its own kind, so quality does not stand for the fifth qafiz. As for the second, because the stipulated is absolute garment in kaffarah, not restricted to medium, so the superior and others are included under the text. As for the third, because the act of worship is in the pouring (of blood) and freeing, and he has committed to two pourings and two freings, so he does not exit from [the obligation], and the surplus remains the owner's property; he does not take the value of the surplus from him, nor is this the case of paying the superior and taking the surplus, and there is no splitting at all, so contemplate. Then it became apparent to me that this second one returns to the absolute statement of al-Bada'i' first that...
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the rulings of paying zakat from grazing animals (specifically sheep). It discusses two main issues: (1) the ruling on an owner giving a superior animal with compensation (taking surplus from the collector), and (2) the permissibility of paying value (qimah) instead of the specified animal. The commentary opens with an exception from al-Hidayah: if the owner wants to give a better animal and takes the surplus from the collector, there is no compulsion on the collector because it is treated as a purchase. However, this is contested by the author of Ghayat al-Bayan, who argues that zakat is based on ease, so refusing the superior creates hardship and contradicts the Sunnah. Proof is cited from Sahih al-Bukhari: if someone owes a hiqqah but does not have it, a jadha'ah is accepted; and if someone owes a bint labun but has a hiqqah, the hiqqah is accepted with the collector giving 20 dirhams or two sheep. This hadith is used as evidence for the permissibility of paying value in zakat (the 'second issue'). The author then clarifies that the estimation of 20 dirhams or two sheep is not a fixed ruling but based on prevailing circumstances. The claim that it is a purchase with no compulsion is rejected because it is not a real purchase, and the collector suffers no harm as an agent. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: the summary (al-Mukhtasar) gives the option to the owner, but Imam Muhammad in al-Asl gives it to the collector. This is refuted in al-Nihayah and al-Mi'raj. In al-Bada'i', the option is for the owner except in one case: when the owner pays part of the obligation through value (e.g., paying part of a hiqqah for a bint labun), then the collector may refuse due to splitting (tasqis) being a defect. al-Zayla'i criticizes this for two reasons: (1) even with defect, it equals the value of the obligation, and (2) it forces the collector to buy the surplus. The discussion continues with a side note on legal stratagems for shuf'ah and zakat, where the fatwa for shuf'ah is on Abu Yusuf's view and for zakat on Muhammad's. The prohibition of using sale to avoid zakat is emphasized, with Maliki and Shafi'i positions noted. Returning to the main issue, the author addresses objections from al-Nahr about returning to the subject with nullification, and the practical difficulty if the owner has neither the obligatory animal nor value. The second objection about forcing the collector to buy the surplus is examined, and it is concluded that it does not invalidate al-Bada'i' because splitting harms the poor. The option is then re-examined: it exists even when the obligatory age is present, contrary to some qualifications. Next, the passage delves into the nature of the wajib in zakat: according to Abu Hanifa, for non-grazing animals (like trade goods), the wajib is part of the nisab in meaning, not form; for the two disciples, it is both form and meaning, but substitution is allowed. A similar difference exists for grazing animals. This principle is applied to examples from al-Jami': a man with 200 qafiz of wheat for trade worth 200 dirhams. If he pays from the same wheat, he gives 5 qafiz. If he pays value, Abu Hanifa considers value on the day the obligation arose (wujub), while the two consider the day of payment (ada'). For grazing animals, the correct view is consensus on the day of payment. The permissibility of paying value is stated from al-Hidayah for zakat, kaffarah, sadaqat al-fitr, ushr, and vows. Finally, examples from Fath al-Qadir: paying three fat sheep for four medium ones is permissible because quality counts in non-ribawi items; but paying four good qafiz for five medium ones of equal value is not permissible because quality does not compensate for quantity in mithli items. Similarly, clothing substitution is limited, and vow fulfillment requires precise adherence. The passage ends with a reflection that the second example returns to the earlier statement from al-Bada'i'.

Key Terms
القيمة (al-qīmah): The monetary value of the obligatory animal or item, paid in cash or kind as a substitute for the specific wajib.
السن الواجب (al-sinn al-wājib): The specific age of the animal that is required to be given in zakat for a particular nisab category (e.g., hiqqah, jadha'ah, bint labun).
المثلي (al-mithlī): A fungible good that is measured or weighed, like wheat, barley, and other commodities where quantity is the primary measure. Quality does not substitute for deficiency in quantity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Muhit, on which day should the value of grazing animals (sawa'im) be assessed for zakat?
A) The day the obligation became due (wujub).
B) The day of payment (ada').
C) The day of the year the nisab was complete.
D) It varies by the owner's choice.

Key Takeaway
Paying value in zakat is permissible in the Hanafi school; for grazing animals, the valuation is on the day of payment by consensus.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
10 min
Nature of the Wajib in Zakat on Livestock and Valuation Date
Intra-Hanafi dispute on nature of wajib and valuation date

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the nature of the wajib in zakat on livestock and apply the correct valuation date when paying value.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school permits paying value in zakat, but the valuation date differs—Abu Hanifa uses day of obligation, Sahibayn use day of payment.

Zakat on livestock can be paid in value rather than the prescribed animal. However, the date at which value is assessed becomes crucial. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples on whether the wajib is a conceptual part of the nisab or the specific animal. By the end of this lesson, you will understand the underlying principle and know the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
Recognize that the passage addresses both the nature of the wajib and the valuation date when paying value.
2
State Abu Hanifa's view for non-grazing
For non-grazing livestock, Abu Hanifa considers the wajib as a conceptual part of the nisab. Therefore, valuation is on the day of obligation.
If value later changes, it does not affect the amount fixed at obligation.
3
State Sahibayn's view for non-grazing
For the Sahibayn, the wajib is the specific animal in form and meaning. Thus, valuation is on the day of payment.
This means the payer may owe more if value increased.
4
Apply to grazing livestock
For sa'imah, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa. The relied-upon position (al-asahh) is the day of payment by consensus, as stated in al-Muhit.
The text says 'بالإجماع' meaning within the Hanafi school.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi for grazing livestock is valuation on day of payment. For non-grazing, both views exist, but fatwa tends towards Abu Hanifa's view.

أن يتصدق بقفيز دقل فتصدق بنصفه جيداً يساوي تمامه لا يجزئه لأن الجودة لا قيمة لها هنا للربوية وللمقابلة بالجنس بخلاف جنس آخر لو تصدق بنصف قفيز منه يساويه جاز ا هـ . قيد المصنف بالزكاة لأنه لا يجوز دفع المعطى لها . نهينا عن قوله: (ويؤخذ (الوسط) أي في الزكاة لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لا تأخذوا من خررات أموال الناس - أي كرائمها - وأخذوا من حواشي أموالهم أي من أوساطها ولأن فيه نظراً من الجانبين. كذا المعراج وذكر الحاكم الجليل في المنتقى الوسط أعلى الأدون وأدون الأعلى وقيل : إذا كان عشرون من الضأن وعشرون من المعز يأخذ الوسط ومعرفته أن يقوم الوسط من المعز والضأن فتؤخذ شاة تساوي نصف قيمة كل واحد That the book of Zakat, section on sheep: forcing him to buy the excess is correct, and it is not hidden that in splitting there is harm to the poor, so the owner does not own that, thus what is in al-Bada'i' is correct. But the author (of Kanz al-Daqa'iq) restricted the mentioned option between the three matters to the non-existence of the obligatory age, as in most books, and it is a coincidental restriction because the option is established even with the existence of the obligatory age. Hence it was said in al-Mi'raj: Some of our companions thought that paying value is a substitute for the obligatory, so they called the issue 'al-Ibdal' (substitution), but it is not so, because resorting to substitution is not permitted except when the original is absent, and paying value while the prescribed (animal) exists is permissible in our view. In al-Bada'i': Our companions differed; according to Imam (Abu Hanifa), the obligatory in other than grazing livestock is a part of the nisab in meaning not in form, and according to them (the two companions) it is form and meaning, but it is permissible to substitute something else for it in meaning. And they differed regarding grazing animals according to his statement; it is said they are like others, and it is said the obligatory is the prescribed in terms of meaning, and according to them the obligatory is the prescribed in form and meaning, but it is permissible to put something else in its place in meaning. The day of obligation and the day of payment differ. And they differed according to his statement regarding grazing animals: some said the day of obligation, some said the day of payment earlier, and its completion is in it. In al-Muhit: The value of grazing animals is considered on the day of payment by consensus, and it is the most correct. It is mentioned in al-Jami': If the wheat became spoiled by something that affected it until its value became one hundred, then he pays two and a half dirhams without dispute if he chooses value, because part of the specific item perished, so what was attached to it of the obligation falls away. If its value increased in itself, then the consideration is on the day of obligation. End quote. In al-Hidayah: It is permissible to pay value in zakat, expiation, sadaqat al-fitr, 'ushr, and vows. End quote. In Fath al-Qadir: If he pays three fat sheep for four medium ones, or some bint labun for bint makhad, it is permissible, because the prescribed is the medium, so the superior is not included in the text, and quality is considered in non-ribawi items, so it takes the place of the fourth sheep. Unlike if it was of the same kind, like if he paid four good qafiz for five medium ones equal in value, it is not permissible. Or clothing: if he pays a garment worth two garments, it is not permissible except for one garment. Or if he vowed to give two medium sheep or free two medium slaves, and he gave one sheep or freed one slave worth each of the two mediums, it is not permissible. As for the first, because quality is not considered when matched with its own kind, so quality does not take the place of the fifth qafiz. As for the second, because the prescribed is absolute garment in expiation, not restricted to medium, so the superior and others are included under the text. As for the third, because the act of devotion is pouring (blood) and freeing, and he has committed to two pourings and two freeings, so he does not exit from that, and the excess remains the property of the owner, not that he takes from him the value of the excess, nor is this a case of paying the superior and taking the surplus, and there is no splitting at all, so reflect. Then it appeared to me that this second refers to the absolute statement of al-Bada'i' first: that the middle is taken and added... (continued) ...
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the section of zakat for sheep. The author, Ibn Nujaym, discusses several interrelated issues. First, he addresses the owner's option to pay a superior animal and take back the excess value, clarifying that such splitting (tashqis) harms the poor and is not permitted. The matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) restricted the option to cases where the obligatory age is absent, but the author notes this is a technical restriction that does not negate the option when the age is present. Then, he delves into the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the nature of the wajib in zakat on livestock. According to Abu Hanifa, for non-grazing livestock (other than sa'imah), the wajib is a conceptual part of the nisab (juz' min al-nisab ma'nan la suratan), whereas for the Sahibayn it is the specific animal in both form and meaning. For grazing livestock (sawa'im), there are two narrations: one similar to non-grazing, and one where the wajib is the prescribed animal in meaning. Despite this difference, all agree that paying value is permissible. The practical consequence appears in the valuation date: for non-grazing livestock, Abu Hanifa uses the day of obligation, while the Sahibayn use the day of payment. For grazing livestock, the relied-upon position (al-asahh) is the day of payment by consensus. The author then cites examples from al-Jami' and al-Hidayah to illustrate these principles. Next, he discusses the permissibility of paying value in various obligations like zakat, expiation, sadaqat al-fitr, 'ushr, and vows, but not in udhiyah, hady, or 'itq because the devotion in those is tied to the physical act (bloodshed or freeing). He then defines 'al-wasat' (the middle animal) using the hadith 'Do not take the best of people's wealth, take from their average.' The middle is not a specific animal but a value-based concept: the superior of the inferior and the inferior of the superior. Examples are given for mixing different types (sheep and goats) or having all animals of the same age group. Finally, the author clarifies the difference between 'musaddiq' (the giver of sadaqah) and 'musaddiq' (the collector) based on Arabic pronunciation. The passage concludes with notes on which animals are exempt from zakat (like the one used for breeding, the fattened for eating, etc.) and the ruling on taking from the lean if there is no medium.

Key Terms
سوائم (sawā'im): Grazing livestock that are left to pasture freely for most of the year.
قيمة (qīmah): Monetary value; paying value in zakat instead of the prescribed animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon position for the valuation date of grazing livestock (sawa'im) when paying value?
A) Day of obligation
B) Day of payment
C) Either day, depending on the owner's choice
D) Day of slaughter

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits paying value in zakat on livestock, but the valuation date for grazing animals is the day of payment by consensus; for non-grazing, there is a difference, with Abu Hanifa using day of obligation and the Sahibayn using day of payment.

intermediate
8 min
Defining Al-Wasat: The Middle Animal in Zakat on Sheep
Definition of al-wasat and related hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-wasat (the middle animal) in zakat on sheep and apply the definition to determine which animal should be taken by the collector.

Core Idea
The middle animal (wasat) is defined by value, not species—it is the superior of the inferior and the inferior of the superior.

When collecting zakat on sheep, the collector must take an animal of average quality—neither the best nor the worst. This lesson unpacks the definition of 'al-wasat' based on the prophetic hadith and the explanation of later Hanafi scholars. Understanding the correct definition ensures justice for both the owner and the poor.

Guided Path
1
Cite the hadith
The Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'Do not take the best of people's wealth; take from their average.' This is the basis for taking the middle animal.
Hadith recorded in Sunan al-Nasa'i and Abu Dawud.
2
Define wasat
According to al-Mi'raj, 'al-wasat is the superior of the inferior and the inferior of the superior' (أعلى الأدون وأدون الأعلى). It is a value-based midpoint.
It is not a specific animal but determined by value.
3
Apply to mixed flocks
If a person has 20 sheep and 20 goats, the collector takes one sheep whose value is midway between the average of the sheep and the average of the goats.
Example from al-Mi'raj: if the average sheep is worth 20 dirhams and the average goat 10 dirhams, a sheep worth 15 dirhams is taken.
4
Exemptions from taking the middle
Certain animals are exempted because they are considered 'karaim' (best) or defective: the breastfeeding ewe, the fattened for eating, the pregnant ewe, the ram used for breeding, the very old, and the defective—unless the collector chooses.
These are considered above the middle or below acceptable.
5
Differentiate between giver and collector
The word 'musaddiq' has two pronunciations: one means the giver of sadaqah, the other means the collector. This distinction avoids confusion in fiqh texts.

Source Text
