لو فسدت الحنطة بما أصابها حتى صارت قيمتها مائة فإنه يؤدي درهمين ونصفاً بلا خلاف إذا اختار القيمة لأنه هلك جزء من العين فسقط ما تعلق به من الواجب، وإن زادت في نفسها قيمة فالعبرة ليوم الوجوب ا.هـ. وفي الهداية: ويجوز دفع القيمة في الزكاة والكفارة وصدقة الفطر والعشر والنذر ا هـ . وفي فتح القدير: لو أدى ثلاث شياه سمان عن أربع وسط أو بعض بنت لبون عن بنت مخاض جاز لأن المنصوص عليه الوسط فلم يكن الأعلى داخلاً في النص والجودة معتبرة في غير الربويات فتقوم مقام الشاة الرابعة بخلاف ما لو كان مثلياً بأن أدى أربعة أقفزة جيدة عن خمسة وسط وهي تساويها لا يجوز، أو كسوة بأن أدى ثوباً يعدل ثوبين لم يجز إلا عن ثوب واحد أو نذر أن يهدي شاتين أو يعتق عبدين وسطين فأهدى شاة أو أعتق عبداً يساوي كل منهما وسطين لا يجوز. أما الأول فلأن الجودة غير معتبرة عند المقابلة بجنسها فلا تقوم الجودة مقام القفيز الخامس، وأما الثاني فلأن المنصوص عليه مطلق الثوب في الكفارة لا بقيد الوسط فكان الأعلى وغيره داخلاً تحت النص، وأما الثالث فلأن القربة في الإراقة والتحرير وقد التزم إراقتين وتحريرين فلا يخرج عن والزائد باقي على ملك المالك لا أنه يأخذ منه قيمة الزائد ولا كان هذا عين دفع الأعلى وأخذ الفضل ولم يكن فيه تشقيص أصلاً فتدبر . ثم ظهر لي أن هذا الثاني راجع إلى إطلاق قول البدائع أولاً أن ويؤخذ الوسط ويضم مستفاد من جنس نصاب إليه ولو أخذ العشر والخراج والزكاة العهدة بواحد بخلاف النذر بالتصدق بأن نذر أن يتصدق بشاتين وسطين فتصدق بشاة بقدرهما جاز لأن المقصود إغناء الفقير وبه تحصل القربة وهو يحصل بالقيمة. وعلى ما قلنا لو نذر أن يتصدق بقفيز دقل فتصدق بنصفه جيداً يساوي تمامه لا يجزئه لأن الجودة لا قيمة لها هنا للربوية وللمقابلة بالجنس بخلاف جنس آخر لو تصدق بنصف قفيز منه يساويه جاز ا هـ . قيد المصنف بالزكاة لأنه لا يجوز دفع القيمة في الضحايا والهدايا والعتق، لأن معنى القربة إراقة الدم وذلك لا يتقوم وكذلك الإعتاق لأن معنى القربة فيه إتلاف الملك ونفي الرق وذلك لا يتقوم. كذا في غاية البيان ولا يخفى أنه مقيد ببقاء أيام النحر، وأما بعدها فيجوز دفع القيمة كما عرف في الأضحية والسن هي المعروفة والمراد بها هنا ذات سن إطلاقاً النوق بالناب لأن السن مما يستدل سمی المسنة بها صاحبها كما سمى من للبعض على الكل أو به على عمر الدواب. ووقع هنا إطلاق المصدق على الساعي وهو مشتبه برب المال، والفرق بينهما أنه إن كان بالصاد المخففة والدال المشددة المكسورة فهو بمعنى آخذ الصدقة، وإن كان بالصاد المشددة والدال المكسورة المشددة فهو المعطى لها . نهينا عن قوله: (ويؤخذ (الوسط) أي في الزكاة لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لا تأخذوا من خررات أموال الناس - أي كرائمها - وأخذوا من حواشي أموالهم أي من أوساطها ولأن فيه نظراً من الجانبين. كذا في الهداية والحزرات جمع حزرة بتقديم الزاي المنقوطة على الراء المهملة. وفي الخانية ولا تؤخذ الرُّبا والأكولة والماخض وفحل الغنم لأنها من الكرائم وقد أخذ الكرائم، ولا تؤخذ الهرم ولا ذات عوار إلا أن يشاء المصدق ا هـ . والأكولة الشاة السمينة التي أعدت للأكل والرُّبا بضم الراء المشددة وتشديد الباء مقصورة وهي التي تربي ولدها. كذا في المغرب والماخض التي في بطنها ولد وقد أطال فيه في البدائع وذكر أنه ليس للساعي مخالف لما أخذ الأدون وهو في الخانية. وفي فتح القدير : إن الأدلة تقتضي أن لا يجب في الأخذ من العجاف التي ليس فيها وسط اعتبار أعلاها وأفضلها وقد قدمنا عنهم خلافها في صدقة السوائم ا.هـ. وفي المعراج وذكر الحاكم الجليل في المنتقى الوسط أعلى الأدون وأدون الأعلى وقيل : إذا كان عشرون من الضأن وعشرون من المعز يأخذ الوسط ومعرفته أن يقوم الوسط من المعز والضأن فتؤخذ شاة تساوي نصف قيمة كل واحد منهما مثلاً الوسط من المعز تساوي عشرة دراهم والوسط من الضأن عشرين فتؤخذ شاة فيمتها خمسة عشر ا هـ . وكذا في البدائع وفيه : ولو كان له خمس من الإبل كلها بنات مخاض أوكلها بنات لبون أو حقاق أو جذاع ففيها شاة وسط . وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية : إذا كان لرجل الخيار لصاحب المال فإنه يشمل ما إذا أراد دفع الأعلى وأخذ الزائد، ثم رأيت صاحب النهر نبه على ذلك قوله : ( يقفيز دقل) الدقل محركة أردأ التمر (قاموس).
That the book of Zakat, section on sheep: forcing him to buy the excess is correct, and it is not hidden that in splitting there is harm to the poor, so the owner does not own that, thus what is in al-Bada'i' is correct. But the author (of Kanz al-Daqa'iq) restricted the mentioned option between the three matters to the non-existence of the obligatory age, as in most books, and it is a coincidental restriction because the option is established even with the existence of the obligatory age. Hence it was said in al-Mi'raj: Some of our companions thought that paying value is a substitute for the obligatory, so they called the issue 'al-Ibdal' (substitution), but it is not so, because resorting to substitution is not permitted except when the original is absent, and paying value while the prescribed (animal) exists is permissible in our view. End quote. In al-Bada'i': Our companions differed; according to Imam (Abu Hanifa), the obligatory in other than grazing livestock is a part of the nisab in meaning not in form, and according to them (the two companions) it is form and meaning, but it is permissible to substitute something else for it in meaning. And they differed regarding grazing animals according to his statement; it is said they are like others, and it is said the obligatory is the prescribed in terms of meaning, and according to them the obligatory is the prescribed in form and meaning, but it is permissible to put something else in its place in meaning. And upon this principle are built the issues of al-Jami': He has two hundred qafiz of wheat for trade, worth two hundred dirhams, and he has no other wealth. If he pays from its own kind, he pays five qafiz without dispute. If he pays its value, then according to him (Abu Hanifa) the value is considered on the day of obligation in increase and decrease, and according to them in both cases the day of payment is considered. The day of obligation and the day of payment differ. And they differed according to his statement regarding grazing animals: some said the day of obligation, some said the day of payment earlier, and its completion is in it. In al-Muhit: The value of grazing animals is considered on the day of payment by consensus, and it is the most correct. It is mentioned in al-Jami': If the wheat became spoiled by something that affected it until its value became one hundred, then he pays two and a half dirhams without dispute if he chooses value, because part of the specific item perished, so what was attached to it of the obligation falls away. If its value increased in itself, then the consideration is on the day of obligation. End quote. In al-Hidayah: It is permissible to pay value in zakat, expiation, sadaqat al-fitr, 'ushr, and vows. End quote. In Fath al-Qadir: If he pays three fat sheep for four medium ones, or some bint labun for bint makhad, it is permissible, because the prescribed is the medium, so the superior is not included in the text, and quality is considered in non-ribawi items, so it takes the place of the fourth sheep. Unlike if it was of the same kind, like if he paid four good qafiz for five medium ones equal in value, it is not permissible. Or clothing: if he pays a garment worth two garments, it is not permissible except for one garment. Or if he vowed to give two medium sheep or free two medium slaves, and he gave one sheep or freed one slave worth each of the two mediums, it is not permissible. As for the first, because quality is not considered when matched with its own kind, so quality does not take the place of the fifth qafiz. As for the second, because the prescribed is absolute garment in expiation, not restricted to medium, so the superior and others are included under the text. As for the third, because the act of devotion is pouring (blood) and freeing, and he has committed to two pourings and two freeings, so he does not exit from that, and the excess remains the property of the owner, not that he takes from him the value of the excess, nor is this a case of paying the superior and taking the surplus, and there is no splitting at all, so reflect. Then it appeared to me that this second refers to the absolute statement of al-Bada'i' first: that the middle is taken and added... (continued) ...
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the section of zakat for sheep. The author, Ibn Nujaym, discusses several interrelated issues. First, he addresses the owner's option to pay a superior animal and take back the excess value, clarifying that such splitting (tashqis) harms the poor and is not permitted. The matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) restricted the option to cases where the obligatory age is absent, but the author notes this is a technical restriction that does not negate the option when the age is present. Then, he delves into the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the nature of the wajib in zakat on livestock. According to Abu Hanifa, for non-grazing livestock (other than sa'imah), the wajib is a conceptual part of the nisab (juz' min al-nisab ma'nan la suratan), whereas for the Sahibayn it is the specific animal in both form and meaning. For grazing livestock (sawa'im), there are two narrations: one similar to non-grazing, and one where the wajib is the prescribed animal in meaning. Despite this difference, all agree that paying value is permissible. The practical consequence appears in the valuation date: for non-grazing livestock, Abu Hanifa uses the day of obligation, while the Sahibayn use the day of payment. For grazing livestock, the relied-upon position (al-asahh) is the day of payment by consensus. The author then cites examples from al-Jami' and al-Hidayah to illustrate these principles. Next, he discusses the permissibility of paying value in various obligations like zakat, expiation, sadaqat al-fitr, 'ushr, and vows, but not in udhiyah, hady, or 'itq because the devotion in those is tied to the physical act (bloodshed or freeing). He then defines 'al-wasat' (the middle animal) using the hadith 'Do not take the best of people's wealth, take from their average.' The middle is not a specific animal but a value-based concept: the superior of the inferior and the inferior of the superior. Examples are given for mixing different types (sheep and goats) or having all animals of the same age group. Finally, the author clarifies the difference between 'musaddiq' (the giver of sadaqah) and 'musaddiq' (the collector) based on Arabic pronunciation. The passage concludes with notes on which animals are exempt from zakat (like the one used for breeding, the fattened for eating, etc.) and the ruling on taking from the lean if there is no medium.

Key Terms
وسط (wasat): The middle animal in terms of value, defined as superior of the inferior and inferior of the superior.
مصدق (musaddiq): The person who gives sadaqah (with shadda and kasra) or the collector (with sukun on first letter and shadda on second).
كرائم (karā'im): The best of the wealth; animals that are excellent and should not be taken in zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how is the middle animal (wasat) defined?
A) The animal with median age.
B) The animal that is superior of the inferior and inferior of the superior in value.
C) The animal that is neither fat nor thin.
D) The animal chosen by the owner.

Key Takeaway
The middle animal (wasat) in zakat on sheep is determined by its monetary value, being the midpoint between the best and worst, as established by the prophetic hadith.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Taking the Middle in Zakat for Livestock and Paying Value
Explanation of taking middle and permissibility of paying value in zakat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking the middle in zakat on livestock, explain the permissibility of paying value in zakat, and identify the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad regarding all high-quality livestock.

Core Idea
In zakat on livestock, the middle quality is taken to balance rights, and paying value is allowed only in zakat.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rule that the zakat collector must take a middle-quality animal from mixed livestock, based on the Prophet's guidance. We also explore when paying monetary value is permitted and a key difference between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani when all animals are of high quality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage rules upon: taking the middle in zakat on livestock. The ruling is wajib, based on the hadith and the principle of fairness.
The act is the collector's selection of a medium animal.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence: the hadith 'Do not take from the best... take from the edges (middles).' Note the imperative form indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
The hadith is ahad, so the ruling is zanni in both transmission and meaning.
3
Define the middle and excluded categories
Understand 'middle' as the average value between best and worst. Identify precious animals (e.g., akula, rubba, makhid) that are prohibited to take in zakat.
The middle is determined by valuation when mixing types.
4
Understand the permissibility of paying value
Recognize that paying monetary value instead of the animal is valid in zakat because the goal is enriching the poor. Contrast with sacrifices (udhiya) and manumission where value is not accepted.
This is specific to zakat; vows are subject to riba rules.
5
Analyze the intra-madhhab dispute
When all livestock are high quality (e.g., 40 akula sheep), Abu Hanifa rules that one of the precious (high-quality) must be given, while Muhammad holds the middle is taken. Identify the mufta bihi as Abu Hanifa's view.
The practical difference: the owner gives a high-quality sheep instead of a medium one.

كتاب الزكاة فصل في الغنم ويؤخذ الوسط ويضم مستفاد من جنس نصاب إليه ولو أخذ العشر والخراج والزكاة العهدة بواحد بخلاف النذر بالتصدق بأن نذر أن يتصدق بشاتين وسطين فتصدق بشاة بقدرهما جاز لأن المقصود إغناء الفقير وبه تحصل القربة وهو يحصل بالقيمة. وعلى ما قلنا لو نذر أن يتصدق بقفيز دقل فتصدق بنصفه جيداً يساوي تمامه لا يجزئه لأن الجودة لا قيمة لها هنا للربوية وللمقابلة بالجنس بخلاف جنس آخر لو تصدق بنصف قفيز منه يساويه جاز ا هـ . قيد المصنف بالزكاة لأنه لا يجوز دفع القيمة في الضحايا والهدايا والعتق، لأن معنى القربة إراقة الدم وذلك لا يتقوم وكذلك الإعتاق لأن معنى القربة فيه إتلاف الملك ونفي الرق وذلك لا يتقوم. كذا في غاية البيان ولا يخفى أنه مقيد ببقاء أيام النحر، وأما بعدها فيجوز دفع القيمة كما عرف في الأضحية والسن هي المعروفة والمراد بها هنا ذات سن إطلاقاً النوق بالناب لأن السن مما يستدل سمی المسنة بها صاحبها كما سمى من للبعض على الكل أو به على عمر الدواب. ووقع هنا إطلاق المصدق على الساعي وهو مشتبه برب المال، والفرق بينهما أنه إن كان بالصاد المخففة والدال المشددة المكسورة فهو بمعنى آخذ الصدقة، وإن كان بالصاد المشددة والدال المكسورة المشددة فهو المعطى لها . قوله: (ويؤخذ (الوسط) أي في الزكاة لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لا تأخذوا من خررات أموال الناس - Book of Zakat, Chapter on Sheep: And the middle is taken, and acquired property of the same type of nisab is added to it. And if the tenth, kharaj, and zakat are taken, the responsibility is with one, unlike a vow to give charity: if he vows to give charity with two medium sheep and gives charity with one sheep equal to them, it is permissible because the purpose is enriching the poor, and thereby devotion is achieved, and it is achieved by value. And according to what we said, if he vows to give charity with a qafiz of poor dates and gives charity with half of it of good quality equal to the whole, it does not suffice because goodness has no value here due to riba and because of comparison by type, unlike another type if he gives charity with half a qafiz of it equal to it, it is permissible. The author restricted it to zakat because payment of value is not allowed in sacrifices, gifts, and manumission, because the meaning of devotion is bloodshed and that is not subject to valuation, and similarly manumission because the meaning of devotion is destruction of ownership and negation of slavery, and that is not subject to valuation. And the age (sen) is well-known, and what is meant here is having age, absolutely, she-camels by the canine tooth because the tooth is used to infer; the aged one is called by its owner, as it is called from the part for the whole or by it on the age of animals. And here the word 'musaddiq' is used for the collector, and it is confusable with the owner of wealth; the difference between them is that if it is with a unsharpened sad and a shadded dal with kasra, it means the taker of zakat, and if with a shadded sad and a kasra shadded dal, it is the giver. His saying: (And the middle is taken) i.e., in zakat, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Do not take from the best of people's wealth - i.e., their precious ones - and take from the edges of their wealth, i.e., from their middles,' and because there is consideration from both sides. Al-makhid is the one with a young in its belly. And he elaborated on it in al-Bada'i and mentioned that the collector does not have opposition to what he takes the lower, and it is in al-Khaniya. In Fath al-Qadir: The evidences require that in taking from the lean ones which have no middle, considering their highest and best is not obligatory, and we have previously mentioned their disagreement in zakat of grazing animals. End. In al-Mi'raj: And the noble judge mentioned in al-Muntaqa: The middle is the highest of the low and the lowest of the high. And it is said: If there are twenty sheep and twenty goats, he takes the middle, and its knowledge is that he values the middle of the goats and sheep, so a sheep is taken equal to half the value of each; for example, the middle of the goats is ten dirhams and the middle of the sheep is twenty, so a sheep is taken worth fifteen. End. And similarly in al-Bada'i, and in it: If he has five camels, all bint makhad, or all bint labun, or hiqaq, or jidha', then a medium sheep is due. In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya: If a man has the choice for the owner of wealth, it includes if he wants to give the higher and take the excess. Then I saw Saheb al-Nahr noted that. His saying: (a qafiz of daql) daql with fatha is the worst dates (Qamus). Palm trees of good dates, barni, and daql. Abu Hanifa said: From each palm tree its share of the tenth is taken. Muhammad said: The middle is taken if there are three types: good, medium, and bad. End. This requires that taking the middle is only when the wealth includes good, medium, and bad, or two types of them; but if all wealth is good, such as forty sheep that are akula, then one of the precious must be taken, not a medium sheep, according to the Imam, contrary to Muhammad, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a detailed commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding zakat on livestock. The author begins by quoting the matn: 'And the middle is taken, and acquired property of the same type of nisab is added to it.' He then explains the ruling on taking the middle value. The primary proof is the hadith: 'Do not take from the best of people's wealth... take from the edges (middles) of their wealth.' This ensures balance between the rights of the owner and the poor. The commentary lists animals that are considered 'precious' and thus not to be taken: the rubba (mother raising young), akula (fattened for eating), makhid (pregnant), and the ram. Also, the decrepit and defective are not taken unless the collector chooses. The definition of 'middle' is discussed: it is the average between the best and worst. When mixing different types (e.g., 20 sheep and 20 goats), the middle is determined by valuing the middle of each type and taking a sheep worth half the total middle value. For camels all of one type, a medium sheep is due. The passage then discusses the permissibility of paying value in zakat, contrasting it with sacrifices and manumission where value is not accepted. In zakat, since the objective is enriching the poor, paying value suffices. However, in a vow to give charity, if one vows a specific item, value may not substitute if the item is ribawi. The date example (daql) illustrates this: if one vows a qafiz of poor dates and gives half of good dates equal in value, it does not suffice because quality does not compensate for quantity in ribawi items. Finally, the passage records a disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad regarding when all property is of high quality: Abu Hanifa says one must give from the best, not the middle, while Muhammad holds that the middle is taken regardless. The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's, as indicated by the commentator's approval.

Key Terms
الوسط (al-wasat): In zakat, the middle quality of livestock, neither the best nor the worst. It is defined as 'the highest of the low and the lowest of the high'.
الكرائم (al-kara'im): The most valuable animals, such as young mothers, fattened sheep, pregnant, and breeding males. These are prohibited to take in zakat.
القيمة (al-qima): Monetary value paid in lieu of the actual zakatable animal. Allowed in zakat but not in sacrifices or manumission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person has forty sheep, all of which are of high quality (akula), what should he give according to Abu Hanifa?
A) He should give a medium-quality sheep.
B) He should give one of the high-quality sheep.
C) He may give the value instead.
D) He gives nothing because all are high quality.

Key Takeaway
In zakat on livestock, the middle quality is taken to ensure fairness; paying value is allowed only in zakat; and when all livestock are high quality, the best must be given according to the relied-upon position.

The Rule of Damm al-Mustafad (Adding Newly Acquired Property)
Explanation of the ruling on joining newly acquired property of the same type to the existing nisab for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule of damm al-mustafad, identify its proof from the hadith of camel zakat, explain the conditions for its application, and describe the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding debt.

Core Idea
Newly acquired property of the same type automatically joins the existing nisab's hawla — the year is for ease, not individual tracking.

The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the second part of the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq: 'and acquired property of the same type of nisab is added to it.' The commentator provides a proof from the Sunnah and discusses various scenarios. This lesson unpacks the rule of damm al-mustafad, its rationale, conditions, and a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding debt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the rule of damm al-mustafad: newly acquired property of the same type is added to the existing nisab for zakat calculation.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith on camel zakat where the Prophet set brackets without regard to timing of acquisition. This proves that new additions are automatically included.
The hadith is cited in the passage: 'أوجب في خمس وعشرين من الإبل بنت مخاض إلى خمس وثلاثين فإذا زادت واحدة ففيها بنت لبون'
3
Understand the rationale
The reason is homogeneity (al-mujānisah): tracking separate years for each acquisition would be difficult, so the hawla of the original suffices.
The hawla was ordained for ease, so the rule avoids hardship.
4
Explore conditions and exceptions
Addition applies only to the same type (jins), requires an existing nisab, and is blocked by impediments (e.g., cash from already-zakatized livestock according to Abu Hanifa).
The passage also discusses loss of nisab during the year and its effect on hawla.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
In the debt scenario, Abu Hanifa requires actual receipt of at least 40 dirhams before zakat is due on newly acquired money; the Sahibayn hold it is due immediately. The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) appears when the debtor dies insolvent.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text

His saying: (And is added acquired property of the same type of nisab to it) because the Prophet, peace be upon him, obligated in twenty-five camels a bint makhad up to thirty-five, and if one increases, then a bint labun, without distinction between the increase at the beginning of the year or during it. And because when there is homogeneity, differentiation is difficult, so considering the year for each acquired item becomes difficult, and the year was stipulated only for ease. And the meaning of adding is that zakat becomes due on the profit at the end of the year of the original. He restricted it to type because what is acquired from a different type, like camels with sheep, is not added because it does not lead to difficulty, because the year does not commence on it until it reaches a nisab. Then everything he acquires from the type he adds to it. And he restricted it to nisab because if the nisab is deficient and it is completed with the acquired item, then the year commences upon completion. As in al-Asbijabi. Unlike if he had a nisab at the beginning of the year and some of it perished during the year, then he acquires the completion of the nisab or more, it is added according to us because the deficiency during the year does not cut off the ruling of the year, so the acquired deficiency becomes like the acquired completion. In Ghayat al-Bayan. And he made 'acquired' absolute, so it includes acquired by inheritance, gift, purchase, or bequest together with the nisab. And it will come that one of the two currencies is added to the other, and that trade goods are added to the two currencies due to type in consideration of their value. In al-Muhit: If he has two hundred dirhams as a debt, and he acquires during the year one hundred dirhams, then the acquired is added to the debt in its year by consensus. And when the year on the debt is completed, according to Abu Hanifa he is not obliged to pay from the acquired unless he receives forty dirhams, but according to them (the two companions) he is obliged even if he does not receive anything from the debt. The benefit of the difference appears when the debtor dies bankrupt: according to him, the zakat of the acquired is waived; according to them, it is obligatory. End. And he pointed by 'him' (i.e., to the nisab) to the necessity of the continued existence of the nisab to which it is added. Therefore he said in al-Muhit: If someone is given a thousand as a gift, then acquires a thousand before the year, then the donor revokes the gift by a judge's ruling, then no zakat is due on the thousand profit until a year passes from when he owned it, because the year of the original (the gifted) became void, and it becomes void in the subsidiary matter. And in al-Mabsut: If the first wealth is lost, then he begins the year anew on the acquired, from when he owned it. If he finds a dirham of the first before the year, he adds it to what he has and pays zakat on all, because by loss, the original ownership does not cease; rather, his possession and disposal cease. So if that is removed before the completion of the year, it is as if the loss had not occurred. It is not hidden that the mentioned addition is when there is no impediment. If there is an impediment, then no addition. Therefore he said in al-Muhit: And the prices of camels, cows, and sheep already zakatized are not added to what he has of the nisab of its type according to Abu Hanifa, because in the addition... end.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage explains the second part of the matn: 'and acquired property of the same type of nisab is added to it.' The commentator provides the proof from the Sunnah: the Prophet (peace be upon him) set the nisab for camels in stages (25-35: bint makhad, 36-45: bint labun, etc.). This shows that when new camels are acquired during the year, they are added to the existing ones, and zakat is calculated on the total at the end of the hawla. The reason is homogeneity: it would be difficult to track each animal's individual year. Adding is only for the same type (e.g., camels to camels), not across types (e.g., camels to sheep), because different types do not cause the same difficulty. The commentator then discusses various scenarios: if the nisab is incomplete and new property completes it, the hawla starts from the completion. If part of the nisab is lost but later regained, the new acquisition is added because the intermediate loss does not break the hawla. The passage also addresses specific issues: in the case of a debt (money owed to someone), if the creditor acquires more money during the year, it is added to the debt's hawla by consensus. Then a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) arises: when the hawla on the debt completes, Abu Hanifa says zakat on the newly acquired money is not due until the creditor actually receives at least forty dirhams of the debt, while the two companions say zakat must be paid from the new money even if no debt is received. The practical difference appears if the debtor dies insolvent: Abu Hanifa says no zakat on the new money is due, whereas the two companions hold it is. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa. Further, if the principal nisab is lost, the hawla on the new acquisition starts anew, but if the original property is found before the hawla completes, it is rejoined. Finally, there is a condition: addition is only valid when there is no impediment. For example, the price received for already zakatized livestock (e.g., selling camels for cash) is not added to the existing nisab of the same type, according to Abu Hanifa, because mixing cash with livestock would cause difficulty in assessment.

Key Terms
ضم المستفاد (damm al-mustafad): The legal rule of adding newly acquired property (mustafad) of the same type to the existing nisab, so that zakat is calculated on the total at the end of the hawla of the original nisab.
الحول (al-hawla): The lunar year that must pass over the nisab for zakat to be due. For newly acquired property, it follows the hawla of the original nisab when added.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person has a debt owed to him of 200 dirhams and during the year he acquires 100 dirhams from another source, when must he pay zakat on that 100 dirhams?
A) Immediately upon the completion of the year on the debt.
B) Only after he receives at least 40 dirhams of the debt.
C) He does not need to pay zakat on it at all.
D) He pays zakat on the 100 dirhams separately after its own year.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule of damm al-mustafad simplifies zakat calculation by requiring that newly acquired property of the same type be added to the existing nisab, with the hawla determined by the original, except when impediments exist.

Zakat from Mixed Quality Herds or Fruits
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat from mixed quality assets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and Muhammad al-Shaybani's positions on selecting zakat assets from mixed quality properties and apply the correct ruling when all assets are uniformly good.

Core Idea
When zakatable assets vary in quality, Abu Hanifa takes proportionally; Muhammad takes average; both agree on best when all are best.

Zakat on livestock and produce requires selecting the specific asset to give. What happens when animals or fruits are of different qualities? This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents an internal Hanafi debate: Abu Hanifa insists each quality contributes its share, while his student Muhammad al-Shaybani prefers taking from the average. Understanding this dispute clarifies how to fulfill zakat fairly and avoid common mistakes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The dispute is about how to select the zakat asset when the property contains items of varying quality (e.g., good, medium, poor dates or sheep).
The passage uses the example of date palms and sheep.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa: Take from each quality its proportionate share. For dates, each palm gives its own tithe; for sheep, each quality class contributes a portion.
3
State Muhammad's position
Muhammad al-Shaybani: Take from the average quality of the entire lot, provided there are at least two quality levels (e.g., good and poor).
The passage specifies that this applies when there are three types or two of them.
4
Identify the boundary case
If all assets are uniformly of the best quality, both imams agree: one from the best must be given. The dispute only arises in mixed cases.
Example: forty fat sheep – one from the best is required by both.
5
Determine the practical difference
In a mixed herd, following Muhammad allows giving an average animal, while Abu Hanifa requires giving from each class, which could result in multiple animals or a more complex calculation.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is the quality of the zakat asset given.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نخيل تمر جيد برني ودقل قال أبو حنيفة : يؤخذ من كل نخلة حصتها من العشر. وقال محمد: يؤخذ من الوسط إذا كانت أصنافاً ثلاثة جيد ووسط ورديء ا هـ. وهذا يقتضي أن أخذ الوسط إنما هو فيما إذا اشتمل المال على جيد ووسط ورديء أو على صنفين منهما، أما لو كان المال كله جيداً كأربعين شاة أكولة فإنه يجب واحدة من الكرائم لا شاة وسط عند الإمام خلافاً لمحمد كما لا يخفى. تمام
Date palms: good, barni, and low-quality. Abu Hanifa said: Each palm tree gives its share of the tithe. Muhammad said: The average is taken if there are three types: good, medium, and bad. This implies that taking the average is only when the property includes good, medium, and bad, or two of them. But if all property is good, like forty fat sheep, then one from the best must be given, not an average sheep according to Imam, contrary to Muhammad, as is clear. End.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding the method of taking zakat from assets of varying quality, specifically dates and sheep. Abu Hanifa holds that each quality category should contribute its proportional share: from good dates, a good tithe; from low-quality, a low-quality tithe. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the zakat should be taken from the average quality of the entire lot, provided the lot includes three quality levels (good, medium, poor). The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq explains that Muhammad's view applies only when there is a mix; if all assets are uniformly good (e.g., forty fat sheep), then even Muhammad would require one from the best, not an average one. The text clarifies that the dispute affects the selection of the zakat animal or fruit, not the overall obligation. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but the author presents the views neutrally.

Key Terms
نخلة (nakhla): Date palm; each tree is considered separately for zakat on fruits.
وسط (wasat): Average quality; Muhammad's view takes zakat from the average quality of the whole.
كرائم (karā'im): The best quality animals; when all are good, one from the best is taken.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person owns forty fat sheep (all of the best quality), what does Imam Muhammad require for zakat?
A) An average sheep
B) One from the best
C) One from the worst
D) Nothing, because they are not mixed

Key Takeaway
When zakatable assets vary in quality, Abu Hanifa takes proportionally from each class; Muhammad takes the average; but both agree to give the best when all are best.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Adding Mustafad to the Nisab
Ruling with proofs and applications on adding mustafad to existing nisab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adding newly acquired wealth to the nisab, identify the conditions and exceptions, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding thinnī.

Core Idea
Newly acquired wealth of the same type is added to the nisab, but prices of already-zakat-paid assets are not added to avoid double zakat.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʼiq explains a key zakat rule: wealth acquired during the year (mustafad) is added to your existing nisab of the same type. The ruling is based on the prophetic practice of taxing camels without distinguishing when the increase occurred. However, the rule has conditions and a critical exception—the prohibition of thinnī (double zakat) prevents adding the sale price of assets that have already been zakat-paid. We will work through the proofs, conditions, and the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two students.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
State that the act is 'adding mustafad to the nisab' and the hukm is wajib (obligatory) when conditions are met.
The proof from sunnah shows aggregation without regard to timing.
2
Locate the Dalīl
Identify the hadith on camel zakat (bint makhad for 25-35, bint labun for 36-45) as the primary proof.
The Prophet did not differentiate between animals owned at the start or during the year.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalālah
The imperative to pay zakat on the total number of camels owned during the year implies that all acquisitions are included.
The principle: al-ʿamr yufīdu al-wujūb.
4
Note the Conditions
The acquired wealth must be of the same genus (jins) and the original nisab must remain intact (or at least the ownership persists).
Different types (e.g., camels with sheep) are not added.
5
Analyse the Exception of Thinnī
According to Abu Hanifa, the price of assets already zakat-paid (e.g., sold camels) is not added because it would cause double zakat in one year.
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagree: they add such prices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ويضم مستفاد من جنس نصاب إليه لأن النبي الله أوجب في خمس وعشرين من الإبل بنت مخاض إلى خمس وثلاثين فإذا زادت واحدة ففيها بنت لبون من غير فصل بين الزيادة في أول الحول أو في أثنائه، ولأنه عند المجانسة يتعسر التمييز فيعسر اعتبار الحول لكل مستفاد وما شرط الحول إلا للتيسير والمراد بالضم أن تجب الزكاة في الفائدة عند الحول على الأصل. قيد بالجنس لأن المستفاد من خلاف جنسه كالإبل مع الشياه لا تضم لأنه لا يؤدي إلى التعسير لأنه لا ينعقد الحول عليه ما لم يبلغ نصاباً، ثم كل ما يستفيده من الجنس يضمه إليه وقيد بالنصاب لأنه لو كان النصاب ناقصاً وكمل مع المستفاد فإن الحول ينعقد عليه عند الكمال. كذا في الأسبيجابي، بخلاف ما لو كان له نصاب في أول الحول فهلك بعضه في أثناء الحول فاستفاد تمام النصاب أو أكثر يضم أيضاً عندنا لأن نقصان في أثناء الحول لا يقطع حكم الحول فصار المستفاد النقصان كالمستفاد كماله . في غاية البيان وأطلق في المستفاد فشمل المستفاد بميراث أو هبة أو شراء أو وصية. وسيأتي أن أحد النقدين يضم إلى الآخر، وأن العروض للتجارة تضم إلى النقدين للجنسية باعتبار قيمتها. وفي المحيط : لو كان له مائتا درهم دین فاستفاد في خلال الحول مائة درهم فإنه يضم المستفاد إلى الدين في حوله بالإجماع، وإذا تم الحول على الدين فعند أبي حنيفة لا يلزمه الأداء من المستفاد ما لم يقبض أربعين درهماً، وعندهما يلزمه وإن لم يقبض من الدين شيئاً. وفائدة الخلاف تظهر فيما إذامات من عليه مفلساً سقط عنه زكاة المستفاد عنده وعندهما يجب ا هـ . وأشار بقوه إليه أي إلى النصاب إلى أنه لا بد من بقاء النصاب المضموم إليه ولذا قال في المحيط : ولو وهب له ألف ثم استفاد ألفاً قبل الحول ثم رجع الواهب في الهبة بقضاء قاض فلا زكاة عليه في الألف الفائدة حتى يمضي حول من حين ملكها لأنه بطل حول الأصل وهو الموهوب فيبطل في حق التبع ا وفي المبسوط : ولو ضاع المال الأول فإنه يستقبل الحول على المستفاد منه منذ ملكه فإن وجد درهماً من دراهم الأول قبل الحول ضمه إلى ما عنده فيزكي الكل لأن بالضياع لا ينعدم أصل الملك وإنما تنعدم يده وتصرفه، فإذا ارتفع ذلك قبل كمال الحول كان كأن الضياع لم يكن ا ولا يخفى أن الضم المذكور عند عدم مانع، أما إذا وجد مانع منه فلا ضم ولذا قال في المحيط : ولا يضم أثمان الإبل والبقر والغنم المزكاة إلى ما عنده من النصاب من جنسه عند أبي حنيفة لأن في الضم تحقيق الثني في الصدقة لأن الثني إيجاب الزكاة مرتين على مالك واحد في مال واحد في حول واحد، وأنه منفي لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لا ثني في الصدقة». وعندهما يضم، ضم مال ولو جعل السائمة علوفة بعد ما زكاها ثم باعها يضم ثمنها إلى ما عنده لخروجها عن الزكاة فصار كمال آخر فلم يؤد إلى الثني، وكذا لو جعل العبد المؤدى زكاته للخدمة ثم باعه يضم ثمنه إلى ما عنده، ولو أدى صدقة الفطر عن عبد الخدمة أو أدى عشر طعامه ثم باعه ثمنه إلى ما عنده لأنه ليس ببدل مال أديت الفطرة عنه لأن الفطرة إنما تجب بسبب رأس يمونه ويلي عليه دون المالية ألا ترى أنها تجب عن أولاده الأحرار والثمن بدل المالية، والعشر إنما يجب بسبب أرض نامية لا بالخارج فلم يثبت الاتحاد حتى لو باع الأرض النامية لا يضم ثمنها إلى ما عنده عند أبي حنيفة. ومن عنده نصابان من جنس واحد أحدهما ثمن إبل مزكاة فاستفاد نصاباً من جنسها فإنه يضم إلى أقربهما حولاً لأنهما استويا في علة الضم، وترجح أحدهما باعتبار القرب لكونه أنفع للفقراء، ولو كان المستفاد ربحاً أو ولداً ضمه إلى أصله، وإن كان أبعد حولاً لأنه يرجح باعتبار التفرع والتولد لأنه تبع وحكم التبع لا يقطع الأصل، ولو أدى زكاة الدراهم ثم اشترى بها سائمة وعنده من جنسها سائمة لم يضمها إليه لأنها بدل مال أديت الزكاة عنه ا هـ .
He said: (And newly acquired [wealth] of the same type as the nisab is added to it) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) obligated in twenty-five camels a bint makhad up to thirty-five; if one more, then a bint labun, without distinction between increase at the beginning of the year or during it. And because when of the same type, distinction is difficult, so considering a full year for each acquisition would be difficult, and the year was only stipulated for ease. The meaning of 'adding' is that zakat becomes obligatory on the gain at the end of the year on the original [nisab]. It is restricted by 'type' because acquired wealth of a different type, like camels with sheep, is not added because it does not lead to difficulty, as the year does not commence until a nisab is reached. Then everything acquired of the same type is added to it. And it is restricted by 'nisab' because if the nisab is deficient and completes with the acquired, then the year begins upon completion. Such is in al-Asbījābī. Contrary to if he had a nisab at the start of the year, then some of it perishes during the year, and he acquires the complete nisab or more; it is also added according to us because a decrease during the year does not cut off the ruling of the year, so the acquired supplement is like an acquired completion. In Ghāyat al-Bayān. He made it absolute regarding acquired, so it includes acquired by inheritance, gift, purchase, or bequest. And it will come that one of the two currencies is added to the other, and that trade goods are added to the two currencies for type based on their value. And in al-Muḥīṭ: If he had two hundred dirhams as a debt and acquired during the year one hundred dirhams, then the acquired is added to the debt in its year by consensus. When the year completes on the debt, according to Abu Hanifa, he is not obliged to pay from the acquired until he has received forty dirhams; according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he is obliged even if he has not received anything from the debt. The difference appears if the debtor dies insolvent: the zakat of the acquired is dropped according to him, and according to them it is obligatory. End. And he indicated [by saying] 'to it' i.e. to the nisab, that the nisab to which it is added must remain. Hence in al-Muḥīṭ: If he was given a gift of a thousand and then acquired a thousand before the year, then the donor revoked the gift by a judge's ruling, there is no zakat on the thousand acquired until a year passes from the time he owned it, because the year of the original (the gift) is invalidated, so it is invalidated for the dependent. And in al-Mabsūṭ: If the first wealth was lost, then he starts a new year on the acquired from the time he owned it; if he finds one dirham from the first dirhams before the year completes, he adds it to what he has, and pays zakat on all, because loss does not eliminate ownership, only possession and control. So if that is resolved before the year completes, it is as if there was no loss. And it is clear that the mentioned addition is only when there is no impediment; but if there is an impediment, there is no addition. Hence in al-Muḥīṭ: And the prices of camels, cows, and sheep already zakat-paid are not added to his nisab of the same type according to Abu Hanifa, because in that addition is the realization of thinnī (double zakat), because thinnī is requiring zakat twice on one owner for one wealth in one year, and it is negated by his statement (peace be upon him): 'There is no thinnī in charity.' According to them (the two), it is added. And if he made grazing livestock fodder after paying their zakat, then sold them, their price is added to what he has, because they exited from zakat and became other wealth, so it does not lead to thinnī. Likewise, if he made a slave whose zakat was paid for service, then sold him, his price is added to what he has. And if he paid zakāt al-fitr for a service slave, or paid the tithe of his food, then sold him, his price is added to what he has, because it is not a substitute for wealth for which fitr was paid; because fitr is obligatory due to a head he supports and cares for, not for monetary value; do you not see that it is obligatory for his free children? And the price is a substitute for monetary value. And the tithe is obligatory due to productive land, not due to the produce, so unity is not established. Thus even if he sold the productive land, its price is not added to what he has according to Abu Hanifa. And if one has two nisābs of the same type, one being the price of zakat-paid camels, and then he acquires a nisāb of that type, it is added to the one closer in year because both are equal in the cause for addition, and one is preferred due to proximity as it is more beneficial for the poor. And if the acquired is profit or offspring, he adds it to its origin, even if it is farther in year, because it is preferred due to being derived and generated, as it is a dependent, and the ruling of the dependent does not cut off the origin. And if he paid zakat on dirhams, then bought grazing livestock with them, and he already had grazing livestock of that type, he does not add them because they are a substitute for wealth on which zakat was paid. End.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This lengthy passage is a detailed exposition of the Hanafi ruling on adding newly acquired wealth (mustafad) to an existing nisab for zakat. The base ruling from Kanz al-Daqāʼiq is that any wealth acquired during the year of the same type as the existing nisab is added to it, and zakat is paid on the whole at the end of the year. The proof is from the Sunnah: the Prophet specified specific ages for zakat on camels (bint makhad for 25-35, bint labun for 36-45, etc.) without distinguishing whether the increase occurred at the start or middle of the year. This implies that all camels owned during the year are considered together. The rationale (ta'lil) is that if different types were not added, distinguishing each acquisition would be difficult, defeating the purpose of the year requirement, which is to ease calculation. The text then refines the ruling by specifying conditions: (1) The acquired must be of the same genus (jins) as the existing nisab; different types like camels and sheep are not added. (2) The existing nisab must be complete at the start; if it was deficient, the year begins only when it is completed by the acquisition. (3) If some of the original nisab is lost during the year, acquisitions can still be added because loss does not break the year. The text then discusses specific cases from al-Muhit and al-Mabsut: debt acquisitions, revoked gifts, loss of wealth, and the important case of thinni (double zakat). The prohibition of thinni (double zakat in one year) creates an exception: the prices of assets on which zakat has already been paid (e.g., the sale price of a sheep after its zakat was paid) are not added to the nisab according to Abu Hanifa, because doing so would cause zakat twice in one year on the same wealth. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that such prices are added. The passage then extends this to other cases: if a grazing animal is made fodder-fed (thus no longer subject to zakat) and then sold, its price is added; likewise, a slave whose zakat was paid for his service, or for whom fitr was paid, when sold, the price may or may not be added depending on the reason for zakat. This demonstrates the principle that the substitution (badal) of wealth for which zakat was paid is not added if the zakat was on the wealth itself (like camels), but if the zakat was due to a separate cause (like fitr due to dependency), then the price is added. Finally, the text covers cases with multiple nisabs and the addition of profit and offspring, which are added to their origin even if it is farther in year. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly given, but the text presents Abu Hanifa's view as the default and shows the ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
مستفاد (mustafād): Wealth newly acquired during the year, by gift, purchase, inheritance, etc.
ضم (ḍamm): Legal addition of mustafad to existing nisab for zakat calculation.
ثني (thinnī): Imposing zakat twice on the same wealth in one year; prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is the price of a camel that has already been zakat-paid not added to the nisab when acquired?
A) Because the price is less than nisab
B) Because adding it would result in thinni (double zakat in one year)
C) Because the price is not considered wealth for zakat
D) Because the year for the price starts from the sale date

Key Takeaway
Adding mustafad is wajib under conditions, but thinnī (double zakat) must be avoided; thus prices of already zakat-paid assets are not added according to Abu Hanifa.

Zakat Paid to Oppressive Rulers: Must It Be Repeated?
Ruling on whether zakat must be repeated if taken by oppressors, with proof from principles and precedent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether zakat taken by an oppressive ruler must be repeated, and explain the condition under which the obligation is discharged.

Core Idea
Zakat taken by an oppressor must be repeated unless the payer intended it as charity, because the ruler is not a valid recipient.

This lesson addresses a common conundrum: what if an oppressive ruler forcibly collects zakat from Muslims? Is the obligation discharged, or must the payer give zakat again to legitimate recipients? The Hanafi jurists distinguish between different types of wealth and consider the payer's intention. The core principle is that valid collection requires protection—which an oppressive ruler does not provide. However, if the payer intends the payment as charity to the ruler (who may be indebted and thus needy), the obligation may be dropped. We will examine the text from al-Bahr al-Raiq and its explanation of the rulings from al-Hidaya and other sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the payment of zakat, kharaj, or tithe to an oppressive ruler (bāghī). The base ruling in the matn is that it is not taken again (i.e., the obligation is discharged). However, the commentary qualifies this.
The ruling is conditional on the imam (ruler) not providing protection, as collection requires protection.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the principle 'al-jibāyah bil-ḥimāyah' (collection is with protection). This is a legal maxim derived from the purpose of taxation: tax is taken in exchange for the ruler's protection of the people.
This principle is cited from al-Hidaya: 'because the imam did not protect them, and collection requires protection'.
3
Analyze the distinction between zakat and kharaj
Al-Hidaya reports a fatwa that zakat must be repeated but kharaj is not. The reason is that oppressors are considered recipients of kharaj because they are fighters (muqātila) defending the land, so they have a right to it. Zakat, however, is solely for the poor, and oppressors are not poor (unless they are indebted).
This distinction shows that the ruling is not uniform across all types of wealth.
4
Evaluate the alternative view: intention of charity
A weaker view (qīla) holds that if the payer intended the payment as charity (ṣadaqa) to the oppressor, considering him poor due to his debts, then the obligation is dropped. This is supported by the precedent of Imam Muhammad permitting charity to a wealthy governor whose debts exceeded his wealth.
The text notes that this view is less cautious (the first view - requiring repetition - is aḥwaṭ).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq states that the first view (repeating zakat) is more cautious (aḥwaṭ), implying it is the relied-upon position for fatwa. However, the intention-of-charity view is also mentioned as viable.
Thus, a mufti would advise repetition as the safer option, but if the payer intended charity, it may suffice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولو أخذ العشر والخراج والزكاة بغاة لم يؤخذ أخرى) أي لم يؤخذ مرة أخرى لأن الإمام لم يحمهم والجباية بالحماية. قال في الهداية وأفتوا بأن يعيدوها دون الخراج لأنهم مصارف الخراج لكونهم مقاتلة والزكاة مصرفها الفقراء ولا يصرفونها إليهم، وقيل: إذا نوى بالدفع التصدق عليهم سقط عنه، وكذا الدفع إلى كل جائز لأنهم بما عليهم من التبعات فقراء والأول أحوط ا أطلق في الزكاة فشمل الأموال الظاهرة والباطنة ولذا قال في المبسوط : الأصح أن أرباب الأموال إذا نووا عند الدفع إلى الظلمة التصدق عليهم سقط عنهم جميع ذلك، وكذا جميع ما يؤخذ من الرجل من الجبايات والمصادرات لأن ما بأيديهم أموال المسلمين وما عليهم من التبعات فوق مالهم فهم بمنزلة الغارمين والفقراء حتى قال محمد بن يجوز دفع الصدقة لعلي بن عيسى بن ماهان والي خراسان وكان أميراً ببلخ وجبت عليه كفارة يمين فسأل فأفتوه بالصيام فجعل يبكي ويقول لحشمه إنهم يقولون لي ما عليك من التبعات فوق مالك من المال فكفارتك كفارة يمين من لا يملك شيئاً. قال في فتح القدير: وعلى هذا لو أوصى بثلث ماله الفقراء فدفع إلى السلطان الجائر سقط ذكره قاضيخان في الجامع الصغير. وعلى هذا فإنكارهم على يحيى بن يحيى تلميذ مالك حيث أفتى بعض ملوك المغاربة قوله : (فافتوه بالصيام الخ) هذا مخالف لما قدمه عن الكشف الكبير من أن التكفير بالمال لا يمنع الدين وجوبه على الأصح فكان هذا مبني على مقابل الأصح قوله : (غير ضائر) خبر المبتدأ وهو
He said: (And if oppressors take tithe, land tax, and zakat, it is not taken again) i.e., it is not taken a second time, because the imam did not protect them, and collection [requires] protection. He said in al-Hidāya: And they gave fatwa that they should repeat them [zakat] but not kharāj, because they [oppressors] are recipients of kharāj as they are fighters, and zakat's recipients are the poor, and they do not give it to them. And it was said: If he intended by the payment to give charity to them, it is dropped from him, and likewise payment to any oppressor because they, due to the liabilities upon them, are poor. And the first is more cautious. He made absolute in zakat so it includes apparent and hidden wealth, hence in al-Mabsūṭ: The correct [view] is that wealth owners, if they intend when paying to oppressors to give them charity, it is dropped from them all that, and likewise everything taken from a man of extractions and confiscations, because what is in their hands is the wealth of Muslims, and the liabilities upon them exceed their wealth, so they are in the position of debtors and the poor. So much so that Muhammad said: It is permissible to give charity to ʿAlī ibn ʿĪsā ibn Māhān, the governor of Khurāsān, and he was an amir in Balkh; an expiation for an oath became obligatory on him, and he asked, so they gave him a fatwa to fast, and he began to cry and said to his attendants: 'They tell me that the liabilities upon me exceed my wealth, so my expiation is the expiation of an oath of one who owns nothing.' He said in Fatḥ al-Qadīr: On this, if he bequeathed a third of his wealth to the poor, and he paid it to the oppressive sultan, it is dropped, mentioned by Qādīkhān in al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr. And on this is their disapproval of Yaḥyā ibn Yaḥyā, the student of Mālik, where he gave a fatwa to a king of the Maghreb... He said: (So they gave him a fatwa to fast...) this contradicts what was presented from al-Kashf al-Kabīr that expiation with wealth does not prevent the obligation of debt according to the most correct, so this is based on the opposite of the most correct. He said: (Non-harmful) is the predicate of the subject, and it is...
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage addresses a practical problem: what if an oppressive ruler (bāghī) forcibly takes zakat, kharāj, or tithe from a Muslim? The base ruling from Kanz al-Daqāʼiq is that it is not taken again (i.e., the obligation is not repeated). However, the commentator explains this is conditional: the imam (ruler) did not protect the payer from the oppressor, because protection is a prerequisite for valid collection. The text then reviews different opinions. Al-Hidāya reports a fatwa that zakat must be repeated (paid again to the rightful recipients) but kharāj is not repeated, because oppressors are entitled to kharāj as they are fighters (defenders) and thus deserve it, but they are not entitled to zakat, which is solely for the poor. A weaker view (qīla) is that if the payer intended the payment as charity (ṣadaqa) to the oppressor (considering him needy due to his debts), then the obligation is dropped. The same applies to any payment to an unjust ruler. The author notes that the first view (repeating zakat) is more cautious (aḥwaṭ). The text extends this to all types of zakat (apparent and hidden wealth) and even to other forced payments and confiscations. A supporting precedent from Imam Muhammad is given: he permitted paying charity to ʿAlī ibn ʿĪsā ibn Māhān, a wealthy governor, because his debts exceeded his wealth, making him eligible. Then a quote from Fatḥ al-Qadīr states that if one bequeaths a third to the poor and pays it to the oppressor, it is considered dropped. Finally, there is a comment about a fatwa from Yaḥyā ibn Yaḥyā (Maliki scholar) to a Maghreb king, and a note that this fatwa contradicts the more correct view that expiation by wealth does not remove the debt obligation. The text ends mid-sentence, possibly commenting on the phrase 'غير ضائر' (non-harmful).

Key Terms
بغاة (bughāh): Oppressive rulers or rebels who unjustly take wealth.
خراج (kharāj): Land tax on non-Muslim farmers; here the oppressors are considered its recipients as fighters.
جائز (jā'iz): Oppressive ruler (jā'ir); payment to him can be considered charity if intended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the more cautious (ahwat) ruling regarding zakat taken by an oppressive ruler?
A) It is discharged and not repeated
B) It must be repeated (paid again)
C) It is never valid regardless of intention
D) Only kharaj must be repeated

Key Takeaway
Zakat taken by an oppressor must be repeated unless the payer intended it as charity to the ruler, because the ruler is not a valid zakat recipient.
